Transferability of Water Rights (Shurb) in Hanafi Fiqh
Rulings on transferability of water rights: inheritance and bequest allowed, sale prohibited.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on inheritance, bequest, and sale of water rights (shurb), and explain why sale is prohibited while inheritance is allowed.

Core Idea
Water rights are inherited but not sold because they are financial rights, not valuable property.

Water rights (shurb) are a traditional means of accessing irrigation water. The Hanafi school distinguishes between transfer by inheritance or bequest, which is permitted, and transfer by sale or gift, which is prohibited. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind these rulings and examines an early custom-based exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three transactions
List the three legal acts discussed: inheritance, bequest, and sale of water rights.
Inheritance and bequest are allowed; sale is prohibited.
2
Understand the basis for inheritance and bequest
Water rights are considered a financial right (haqq mali), so they pass to heirs by inheritance and can be bequeathed by will.
Bequest is seen as akin to inheritance.
3
Understand the prohibition of sale
Water rights are not considered valuable property (mal mutaqawwim) in the relied-upon view, due to inability to possess them tangibly, leading to uncertainty (gharar).
This also applies to gift, lease, and charity.
4
Examine the Balkh dispute
Some Balkh scholars allowed sale based on local custom, but the Hanafi response limits custom to one town and upholds the original narration.
If a sale is ruled valid by a judge, it takes effect, but the general ruling prohibits it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويورث الشرب إلخ: أي تجري الوراثة في الشرب؛ لأنه حق مالي، فيجري فيه الإرث. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٩٣/٢] ولأن الورثة خلف الميت يقومون مقامه، وجاز أن يقوموا مقامه فيما لا يجوز تمليكه كالمعاوضات والتبرعات كالدين والقصاص والخمر، وكذا الشرب. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٣٥/٨] ويوصى بالانتفاع إلخ لأن الوصية أخت الميراث فكانت مثله تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٣٥/٨] ولأن جهالة الموصى به لا تمنع الوصية؛ لأنها من أوسع العقود حتى جازت للمعدوم وبالمعدوم [رمز الحقائق: ٣٩٣/٢] ولا يباع ولا يوهب إلخ وكذا لا يؤجر ولا يتصدق به؛ إما للغرر أو للجهالة الفاحشة، أو لعدم تصور قبضه، أو لعدم الملك فيه للحال؛ لأنه ليس مال متقوم في ظاهر الرواية، وعليه الفتوى حتى لو أتلف شرب إنسان بأن سقى أرضه من شرب غيره لا يضمن على رواية الأصل، وجوز بعض مشايخ بلخ بيعه؛ لتعامل أهل بلخ، والقياس يترك بالتعامل، قلنا: إنه تعامل أهل بلدة واحدة، وإذا حكم بصحة بيعه نفذ، وكذا لا يصلح مسمى في النكاح، ولا في الخلع، ولا في الصلح عن دم العمد، وهذه العقود صحيحة لا تبطل بهذا الشرط فيها، ويجب على الزوج مهر المثل، وعلى المرأة رد ما أخذت من المهر، وعلى القاتل الدية، وكذا لا يصلح بدلا في دعوى حق، وللمدعي أن يرجع في دعواه. (فتح، تكملة)
And the water right is inherited – meaning inheritance applies to the water right because it is a financial right, so inheritance applies to it. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2/393] And because the heirs are successors of the deceased, they stand in his place, and it is permissible for them to stand in his place regarding what cannot be owned like compensations and voluntary acts such as debt, retaliation, and wine, and likewise the water right. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq 8/435) And he may bequeath the usufruct – because bequest is the sister of inheritance, so it is like it. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq 8/435) And because ignorance of the bequeathed item does not prevent bequest, since it is among the most flexible contracts, even permissible for a non-existent or with a non-existent. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2/393] And it is not sold nor given as gift – and likewise not leased nor given as charity; either due to gharar (uncertainty) or gross ignorance, or because the concept of possession is inconceivable, or because there is no ownership at present; for it is not a valuable property (mal mutaqawwim) in the apparent narration, and the fatwa is upon that. Even if someone destroys another's water right by irrigating his land from another's water right, he is not liable according to the original narration. Some scholars of Balkh permitted its sale due to the practice of the people of Balkh, and analogy is abandoned for practice (ta'amul). We say: it is the practice of one town only, and if it is judged valid, it takes effect. Likewise, it is not valid as a specified dower in marriage, nor in khul', nor in reconciliation for intentional homicide – these contracts are valid and are not invalidated by this condition; the husband must give proper dower, the woman must return what she took of the dower, and the killer must pay blood money. Likewise, it is not valid as a substitute in a claim of right, and the claimant may retract his claim. (Fath, Completion)
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Kanz al-Daqaiq with commentary explaining the transferability of water rights (shurb). The relied-upon Hanafi position is that water rights are inheritable because they are financial rights; the heirs stand in the place of the deceased. Bequest of the usufruct is also allowed because bequest is akin to inheritance and ignorance of the object does not invalidate it. However, water rights cannot be sold, gifted, leased, or given in charity because they are not considered valuable property (mal mutaqawwim) in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). The text notes a dissenting view from some scholars of Balkh who allowed sale based on local custom, but the response is that this custom is limited to one town and does not override the general ruling. Furthermore, water rights cannot be specified as a dower in marriage, in khul', or in blood money reconciliation; if such conditions are made, the contract remains valid but the specified amount is replaced by the proper value. Similarly, it cannot be a substitute in a claim.

Key Terms
شرب (shurb): A water right or share in a water source for irrigation.
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; water rights cannot be owned in the full sense.
مال متقوم (mal mutaqawwim): Valuable property that is legally recognized and can be sold; water rights are not considered so in the relied-upon view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Selling the water right to a neighbor.
B) Bequeathing the usufruct of the water right.
C) Giving the water right as dower (mahr) in marriage.
D) Using the water right to settle a blood money claim.

Key Takeaway
Water rights are inheritable and bequeathable but not saleable in the relied-upon Hanafi view, due to their status as financial rights rather than valuable property.

Qatl bi Sabab: Ruling and Inheritance Exception
Explains killing by cause, its rulings, and the exception from inheritance exclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for qatl bi sabab, including the obligation of diyah on the 'aqilah, absence of kaffarah, and the exception from inheritance exclusion, and explain the Shafi'i counter-position.

Core Idea
A killer by cause is liable for diyah but does not forfeit inheritance — indirect killing leaves the default inheritance rule intact.

In previous lessons, we covered the four types of killing that exclude inheritance. This lesson introduces the fifth type: killing by cause (qatl bi sabab). Unlike direct killing, the indirectness here changes the rulings: diyah is due on the 'aqilah, no kaffarah is required, and importantly, the killer still inherits from the victim. Let's examine the proof and the Shafi'i disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what qatl bi sabab is and what hukm applies: diyah is wajib on the 'aqilah, no kaffarah, no sin of killing (only sin of the hazardous act).
Examples: digging a well or placing a stone on a public path without authority.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence for this ruling. The passage uses qiyas: the digger is treated like one who pushes another into the well, so diyah is on the 'aqilah. The lack of direct act explains the absence of kaffarah.
The text states: 'so he is treated as the one who pushes and throws in'.
3
Trace the inheritance exception
The passage states that all other types of killing exclude inheritance, but qatl bi sabab does not. Understand why: the killer is not directly killing, so the default rule of inheritance (no exclusion) remains.
Hanafi rebuttal to Shafi'i: killing is absent (ma'dum), so it cannot be the basis for exclusion.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Shafi'i considers qatl bi sabab to be like khata' in all rulings, including inheritance exclusion. The Hanafi school disagrees, limiting the analogy to diyah only.
The thamarah al-khilaf: the killer inherits (Hanafi) vs. does not (Shafi'i).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that the killer by cause does inherit. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
No explicit tarjih authority given, but the text clearly presents it as the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقتل بسبب: [بالجر عطف على القتل أي موجب القتل بسبب إما مرفوع أو مجرور على الوجهين وخبره قوله: "الدية على العاقلة"، وهو القسم الخامس من الأنواع الخمسة. كحافر البئر إلخ: تفسير للقتل بسبب أي القتل بسبب كحافر البئر في غير ملكه وهو مشروط بما إذا كان بغير إذن السلطان، وكذا واضع خشبة على قارعة الطريق ونحو ذلك، إلا إذا مشى على البئر ونحوه بعد علمه بالحفر ونحوه. (فتح، رد المختار) الدية على العاقلة لأنه التلف، سبب وهو متعد فيه بالحفر فجعل كالدافع الملقي فيه فتجب فيه الدية صيانة للأنفس، فتكون على العاقلة؛ لأن القتل بهذا الطريق دون القتل بالخطأ فيكون معذورا، فتجب على العاقلة تخفيفا عنه كما في الخطأ بل أولى؛ لعدم القتل منه مباشرة، ولهذا لا تجب الكفارة فيه [تكملة البحر الرائق: ٦٣/٩] وهذا إذا كان الحفر على ممر الناس، وإذا لم يكن لا دية عليه. (تكملة، ملا مسكين)
لا الكفارة: أي لا تجب فيه الكفارة؛ لعدم المباشرة. [رمزه الحقائق: ٤٢٢/٢] ولا يأثم إثم القتل بل إثم الحفر والوضع في غير ملكه. (در مختار)
والكل إلخ أي كل نوع من أنواع القتل الذي تقدم يوجب حرمان الإرث إلا القتل بسبب، فإنه لا يوجب ذلك كما لا يوجب الكفارة وقال الشافعي هو ملحق بالخطأ في أحكامه. [تكملة البحر الرائق: ٦٣/٩] لأن الشرع أنزله قاتلا ولنا أن القتل معدوم فيه، والحق بالخطأ فبقي في غيره على الأصل. (فتح) عمد فيما سواها لأن إتلاف ما دون النفس لا يختص بآلة دون آلة، فلا يتصور فيه شبه العمد بخلاف النفس على ما بيناه، والذي يدلك على هذا ما روي أنس ابن مالك لله أن عمة الربيع - حق الضمان
And killing by cause: together with previous, ruling of diyah on 'aqilah. Example: digger of well on his own land without sultan's permission, or placer of stone on road. Diyah on 'aqilah because cause, no kaffarah because no direct act. No sin of killing but sin of digging/placing. All types cause inheritance exclusion except killing by cause. Shafi'i considers it like khata', but Hanafi: killing is absent, it is attached to khata' but remains on original (no exclusion). 'Amd for less than life: shibh 'amd does not exist; every instrument is same.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage covers the fifth type: qatl bi sabab (killing by cause), e.g., digging a well or placing a stone in a public path without authority. Ruling: diyah on 'aqilah, no kaffarah, no sin of killing (but sin of hazardous act). Unlike direct killing, here the killer is not the direct cause. Then a general rule: all types of killing exclude the killer from inheriting from the victim, except qatl bi sabab. The Shafi'i school attaches this to khata' for inheritance, but Hanafis say since the killer did not directly kill, the default rule of inheritance applies—no exclusion. Finally, a note that shibh 'amd only exists for killing life; for less than life (e.g., cutting limb), any instrument qualifies as 'amd, so shibh 'amd does not apply.

Key Terms
القتل بسبب (qatl bi sabab): Killing by cause, e.g., digging a well or placing a stone that leads to death indirectly.
حرمان الإرث (hirman al-irth): Exclusion from inheritance due to killing the testator.
العاقلة (al-'aqilah): The paternal male relatives of the killer who share in paying diyah collectively.
الكفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for accidental killing: freeing a slave or fasting two months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, does the killer by cause (e.g., digging a well) inherit from the victim?
A) Yes, because the killing is indirect and does not exclude inheritance.
B) No, all killers are excluded.
C) Only if the well was in his own property.
D) Only if he did not know the victim.

Key Takeaway
Qatl bi sabab imposes diyah on the 'aqilah but does not require kaffarah or exclude inheritance, distinguishing it from other killings.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate

Composition of the 'Aqila and the Killer's Liability
Defining the 'aqila's composition and the killer's role

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi composition of the 'aqila and evaluate the Shafi'i objection regarding the killer's contribution.

Core Idea
The killer is included in the 'aqila because the obligation is based on mutual support, and partial payment is not unjust.

The 'aqila is the clan responsible for paying diya in accidental homicide. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentaries defines who constitutes the 'aqila and addresses a key disagreement with the Shafi'i school: whether the killer himself contributes. The Hanafi position integrates the killer as one of the contributors, supported by the principle of nusra and the Quranic verse 'No bearer of burdens will bear the burden of another' (Quran 6:164), which Hanafi scholars interpret as permitting the killer's share.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling that the 'aqila consists of the nearest agnates (asabat) on the order of inheritance, and the killer is counted as one of them. Note also the rules for freed slaves and clients.
The killer's inclusion is explicit: 'wal-qatilu ka-ahadihim' (the killer is like one of them).
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds the killer should pay nothing because he is excused (ma'dhur). His reasoning: if the whole diya is not obligatory on him, the part should also not be obligatory, as a part does not differ from the whole.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi refutation: obligating the whole diya on the killer would be unjust (ijhaf), but obligating a part is not. Moreover, the diya is obligatory by way of support (nusra), and the killer supports himself more than others, making him more deserving of the obligation, not less.
The verse 'No bearer bears another's burden' is used to argue that the killer cannot bear the entire burden, but a share is his own responsibility.
4
Examine the other rulings on 'aqila composition
Note the additional rules: the 'aqila of a freed slave is the tribe of his master; the 'aqila of a client by muwalat is the master and his tribe; the 'aqila does not bear liability for intentional crime, compromise, or confession unless confirmed. For non-Arabs, the diya is based on locality or, if that fails, on the killer's own wealth.
The passage also includes a dispute regarding inclusion of the killer's father and sons, with two opinions.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: In the Hanafi school, the killer pays a share of the diya along with his 'aqila; in the Shafi'i school, the 'aqila pays the entire diya and the killer pays nothing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المعاقل
أحكام المعاقل
لذلك ضم إليهم أقرب القبائل نسبا على ترتيب العصبات، والقاتل كأحدهم، وعاقلة المعتق قبيلة مولاه، ويعقل عن مولى الموالاة مولاه وقبيلته، ولا تعقل عاقلة جناية العبد، والعمد، وما لزم صلحا أو اعترافا، إلا أن يصدقوه وأما آباء القاتل وأبناؤه، فقد قيل: يدخلون لقربهم، وقيل: لا يدخلون وعلى هذا حكم أهل الديوان إذا لم يتسع لذلك يضم إليه أقرب الديوان نصرة، ثم الأقرب فالأقرب، قالوا: هذا في حق العرب؛ لأنهم حفظوا أنسابهم، فأمكن إيجابه على أقرب القبائل، وأما العجم، فقد ضيعوا أنسابهم، فلا يمكن ذلك في حقهم، فإذا لم يمكن، فقد اختلفوا فيه، فقال بعضهم: يعتبر المحال والقرى الأقرب فالأقرب، وقال بعضهم: يجب الباقي في مال الجاني. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٢/٢] لذلك أي لما ذكر من قسمة الدية على كل واحد والقاتل كأحدهم: أي كواحد من العاقلة فيما يؤدي، فلا معنى لإخراجه ومؤاخذة غيره به وقال الشافعي له: لا يجب على القاتل شيء من الدية؛ لأنه معذور، ولهذا لا يجب عليه الكل، فكذا البعض؛ إذ الجزء لا يخالف الكل، قلنا: إيجاب الكل إجحاف به، ولا كذلك البعض، ولأنها تجب بالنصرة، ولا ينصر نفسه مثل ما ينصر غيره، بل أشد فكان أولى بالإيجاب عليه، فإذا كان المخطئ معذورا، فالبريء منه أولى، قال الله تعالى: {وَلا تَزِرُ وَازِرَةٌ وِزْرَ أُخْرَى} (الأنعام: ١٦٤) تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٦٣/٩] وعاقلة المعتق إلخ: يعني عاقلة المعتق – بفتح التاء – قبيلة مولاه الذي أعتقه؛ إذ نصرته بهم، واسمها ينبئ عنها، يؤيد ذلك قوله : "مولى القوم منهم". [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٦٣/٩]
مولى الموالاة إلخ ومولى الموالات هو الحليف، فيعقل عنه مولاه الذي عاقده، وعاقلة مولاه، وهو المراد بقوله: " وقبيلته" أي قبيلة مولاه الذي عاقده تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٦٣/٩] لأن العرب تتناصر به فأشبه ولاء العتاقة، وقال الشافعي: لا يجب عليهم شيء، وقد مر في الولاء. [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٢/٢]
The Book of 'Aqila. Rulings of 'Aqila. Therefore, the nearest tribes by lineage are joined to them in order of the 'asabat, and the killer is like one of them. The 'aqila of the freed slave is the tribe of his master. And he (the client) pays on behalf of the client of muwalat, his master and his tribe. And the 'aqila does not bear the injury of the slave, nor intentional homicide, nor what is binding by compromise or confession, unless they confirm him. And as for the killer's fathers and sons, it has been said: they enter due to their closeness, and it has been said: they do not enter. And on this is the ruling of the people of the register (diwan) if it does not extend to that: the nearest of the register is joined to him for support, then the nearest then the nearest. They said: this applies to Arabs because they preserved their lineages, so it is possible to impose it on the nearest tribes. As for non-Arabs, they have lost their lineages, so that is not possible concerning them. So if that is not possible, they differed about it: some said that localities and villages are considered, the nearest then the nearest; and some said the remainder is in the wealth of the perpetrator. Therefore, i.e., because of what was mentioned of dividing the diya upon each one, and the killer is like one of them, i.e., like one of the 'aqila in what he pays, so there is no meaning to excluding him and holding others responsible with him. Al-Shafi'i said: nothing of the diya is obligatory upon the killer because he is excused, and therefore the whole is not obligatory upon him, so likewise the part, since the part does not differ from the whole. We say: obligating the whole is unjust to him, but not so the part; and because the diya is obligatory by way of support, and he does not support himself like he supports others, rather more severely, so he is more deserving of the obligation. So if the mistaken one is excused, the innocent one is more deserving. Allah says: {And no bearer of burdens will bear the burden of another} (al-An'am 164). (Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:263). And the 'aqila of the freed slave etc.: meaning the 'aqila of the freed slave – with fatha on the ta – is the tribe of his master who freed him, because his support is through them, and his name indicates it, and that is supported by his (saw) statement: "The client of a people is from among them." (Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:263). Mawla al-muwalat etc. – mawla al-muwalat is the ally, so his master who made the contract with him pays on his behalf, and the 'aqila of his master, and that is meant by his statement "and his tribe", i.e., the tribe of his master who made the contract. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:263) because the Arabs support each other through him, so it resembles the clientage of emancipation. Al-Shafi'i said: nothing is obligatory upon them, and it has passed in the chapter of Wala. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:472).
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the composition of the 'aqila – the clan responsible for paying diya in cases of accidental homicide. The Hanafi position is that the 'aqila consists of the nearest agnates (asabat) to the killer, with the killer himself included as a member of the 'aqila, contributing his share. This is justified by the principle of support (nusra): the killer supports himself more than others, so he should not be exempt. The 'aqila of a freed slave is the tribe of his master who freed him, because the client is considered among the master's people (hadith: 'Mawla al-qawm minhum'). For a client by allegiance (mawla al-muwalat) – a non-kin ally – the 'aqila is his master and the master's tribe, as the Arabs support each other through this tie. The passage also addresses two opinions on whether the killer's father and sons are included (entering due to closeness, or not). For Arabs, the system is based on preserved lineage; for non-Arabs who lost their lineages, the 'aqila is determined by the nearest locality or, if that fails, the diya falls on the killer's own wealth. The Shafi'i objection that the killer is excused and should pay nothing is refuted: the entire diya would be harsh, but the part is not, and support logic makes the killer more liable, not less. The verse 'No bearer bears another's burden' is cited to show the killer does not bear the whole burden, but the part is fair.

Key Terms
عاقلة ('aqila): The group of male agnates (asabat) who pay the diya for accidental homicide committed by a member of their group.
مولى الموالاة (mawla al-muwalat): A non-kin ally who enters into a contract of mutual support with a master, creating a clientage relationship distinct from emancipation.
ديوان (diwan): A register or military unit; here it refers to the group of soldiers listed in the same register who act as an 'aqila when lineage cannot be determined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the killer himself included in the 'aqila for paying diya in accidental homicide?
A) The killer is considered an agnate of himself.
B) Because the killer supports himself more than he supports others, so he is more deserving of the obligation.
C) The killer is excused and therefore pays nothing.
D) The killer's wealth alone covers the entire diya.

Key Takeaway
The killer is an integral part of the 'aqila in Hanafi law, liable for a share of the diya based on the principle of mutual support (nusra).

Faraid — Inheritance

The Principle of Aqall al-Nasibayn: Lesser of Two Shares
Definition and first two examples of the aqall al-nasibayn rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for the khuntha's inheritance and apply it to a simple case with Quranic heirs.

Core Idea
The khuntha receives the lesser of his male and female shares, or nothing if deprived under both estimates.

This lesson introduces the core Hanafi principle for ambiguous hermaphrodites in inheritance. The rule is derived from the certainty principle: we give what is certain and avoid the doubtful. The passage defines the term and illustrates it with a case involving a husband, mother, and full sister who is a khuntha.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of aqall al-nasibayn
The khuntha's inheritance is the minimum of the two possible shares calculated as male and as female. If one estimation yields zero, he gets nothing.
This is the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and majority of Companions).
2
Identify the heirs in the first example
A woman dies leaving a husband, mother, and a full sister who is a khuntha. List the Quranic shares: husband 1/2, mother 1/3, sister gets residue as asabah.
Sister normally gets 1/2 as Quranic heir, but here she is a residuary due to being a khuntha.
3
Calculate under both male and female assumptions
As male (asabah), she gets residue = 1/6. As female, she gets 1/2 but the estate would 'awl to 8 (1/2+1/3+1/2 = 1+? Actually 1/2+1/3+1/2 = 1+1/3, so shares reduce). Compare: 1/6 vs reduced 1/2 under 'awl. The lesser is 1/6.
The khuntha receives the smaller amount (1/6). If deprived under one estimation, he gets nothing.
4
Apply the rule to the second example
Father dies leaving a son and a khuntha child. Son gets 2 shares, khuntha gets 1 share (Abu Hanifa's ruling). This is because the lesser of the two possibilities (male vs female) is 1 share when son gets 2.
This is the simplest case; the dispute arises when both are present and the method of calculation varies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقل النصيبين: المراد بأقل النصيبين أسوأ الحالين فيشمل حالة الحرمان] يعني للخنثى المشكل في الميراث الأقل من نصيب الذكر ومن نصيب الأنثى، فإنه ينظر نصيبه على أنه ذكر، وعلى أنه أنثى، فيعطى الأقل منهما، وإن كان محروما على أحد التقديرين فلا شيء له، فلو تركت امرأة زوجا وأما وأختا لأب وأم، وهي خنثى كان للزوج النصف، وللأم الثلث، وللخنثى ما بقي، وهو السدس على أنه عصبة؛ لأنه أقل، ولو قدر أنثى كان له النصف، وكانت المسألة تعول إلى ثمانية.  كتاب الخنثى ٥١٢ أحكام الخنثى فلو مات أبوه وترك ابنا له سهمان، وللخنثى سهم. أي للابن = عند أبي حنيفة . لو تركت زوجا وأما وأخوين من أم وأخا لأب وأم وهو خنثى، كان للزوج النصف، وللأم السدس، وللأخوين للأم الثلث، ولا شيء للخنثى؛ لأنه عصبة، و لم يفضل له شيء، ولو قدر أنثى، كان له النصف، وعالت المسألة إلى تسعة وهذا المذكور من حكم الخنثى هو مذهب أبي حنيفة، وهو قول عامة الصحابة، وعليه الفتوى وقال الشعبي للخنثى نصف ميراث ذكر، ونصف ميراث أنثى، وعن ابن عباس ما مثله؛ لأنه مجهول، وبه قال أبو يوسف ومحمد ومالك ،وأحمد، وعند الشافعي له أظهر الحالتين، وتوقف الزيادة على نصيبه إلى أن يتبين أمره أو يصطلح هو والورثة. (فتح، عيني، مسكين) فلو مات أبوه إلخ : أوضح المصنف الحكم المذكور بالتمثيل أي فلو مات أبو الخنثى وترك ابنا، فللابن سهمان، وللخنثى سهم؛ لأنه الأقل، وهو متيقن به فيستحقه، وعلى قول الشافعي الذي ذكرناه الآن: للخنثى الثلث، وللابن النصف؛ لأنه المتيقن ويوقف السدس، واختلف أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمها في هذا على قول الشعبي؛ لأن عنده للخنثى نصف ميراث ذكر ونصف ميراث أنثى، فقال محمد المال بينهما على اثني عشر سهما للابن سبعة، وللخنثى خمسة، وقال أبو يوسف المال بينهما على سبعة أسهم للابن أربعة، وللخنثى ثلاثة، اعتبر نصيب كل واحد منهما حالة انفراده، فإن الذكر لو كان وحده كان له كل المال، والخنثى لو كان وحده إن كان ذكرا كان له كل المال وإن كان أنثى كان له نصف المال فيأخذ نصف النصيبين، نصف الكل ونصف النصف، وذلك ثلاثة أرباع المال، وللابن كل المال، فيجعل كل ربع سهما، فبلغ سبعة أسهم: للابن أربعة، وللخنثى ثلاثة، وإنما كان كذلك؛ لأن الابن يستحق الكل عند الانفراد والخنثى ثلاثة أرباع، وليس للمال كل، وثلاثة أرباع، فيضرب كل واحد منهما في جميع حقه اعتبارا بطريق العول والمضاربة. ومحمد به اعتبر نصيب كل واحد منهما في حالة الاجتماع، فقال: لو كان الخنثى ذكرا كان المال بينهما نصفين ولو كان أنثى كان أثلاثا، فالقسمة على تقدير ذكورته من اثنين وعلى تقدير أنوثته من ثلاثة، وليس بينهما موافقة فتضرب إحداهما في الأخرى، تبلغ ستة، للخنثى منها على تقدير أنه أنثى سهمان، وعلى تقدير أنه ذكر ثلاثة، فله نصف النصيبين، وليس للثلاثة نصف صحيح، فتضرب الستة في اثنين تبلغ أثنى عشر، فيكون للخنثى ستة على تقدير أنه ذكر وأربعة على تقدير أنه أنثى فيأخذ نصف النصيبين خمسة؛ لأن نصف الستة ثلاثة ونصف الأربعة اثنان وقال شمس الأئمة: خرجا قول الشعبي و لم يأخذا به رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٨/٢] وقال في "الفتح": وفي تأخير صاحب الهداية قول محمد إشارة إلى اختياره؛ لأن الكل متفقون على تقليل نصيبه، وما ذهب إليه محمد أقل مما ذهب إليه أبو يوسف.
The lesser of the two shares: what is meant by 'lesser of the two shares' is the worse of the two states, which includes the case of being deprived. That is, for the ambiguous khuntha in inheritance, the lesser of the male share and the female share. He is given the lesser of the two, and if he would be deprived on one estimation, he gets nothing. For example, if a woman leaves a husband, a mother, and a sister [full] and she is a khuntha, the husband gets half, the mother gets one-third, and the khuntha gets what remains, which is one-sixth as an 'asaba (residuary), because it is less. If she were estimated as female, she would get half and the problem would 'awl to eight. If his father died leaving a son, for the son two shares and for the khuntha one share. That is for the son according to Abu Hanifa. If a woman left a husband, a mother, two maternal brothers, and a full brother who is a khuntha: for the husband half, for the mother one-sixth, for the two maternal brothers one-third, and nothing for the khuntha because he is an 'asaba and nothing remained for him. If she were estimated as female, she would get half and the problem would 'awl to nine. This mentioned ruling of the khuntha is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa and the saying of the majority of the Companions, and upon it is the fatwa. Al-Sha'bi said: For the khuntha is half the inheritance of a male and half the inheritance of a female. And from Ibn 'Abbas something like it, because he is unknown. And Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Malik, and Ahmad said the same. According to al-Shafi'i, he gets the more apparent of the two states and the increase over his share is suspended until his matter becomes clear or he and the heirs reach a settlement. 'If his father died, etc.': The author clarified the mentioned ruling by example. That is, if the father of the khuntha dies leaving a son, for the son two shares and for the khuntha one share, because it is the lesser and it is certain, so he receives it. According to the Shafi'i view we mentioned, for the khuntha is one-third, for the son half, and one-sixth is suspended. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differed on this according to al-Sha'bi's saying, because according to him the khuntha gets half the inheritance of a male and half of a female. Muhammad said: The wealth is divided between them into twelve shares: for the son seven, for the khuntha five. Abu Yusuf said: The wealth is divided into seven shares: for the son four, for the khuntha three. He considered each one's share in isolation: if the male were alone, he would get all; if the khuntha were alone, if male all, if female half. So he takes half of the two shares: half of the whole and half of the half, which is three-fourths. For the son is all the wealth. So each quarter is made one share, making seven shares: for the son four, for the khuntha three. It is like this because the son is entitled to all when alone, and the khuntha to three-fourths, and the wealth is [divided] into all and three-fourths, so each multiplies in his entire right considering the way of 'awl and partnership. Muhammad considered each one's share in the situation of meeting. He said: If the khuntha were male, the wealth would be halves; if female, thirds. The division on the assumption of his maleness is from two, and on his femaleness from three. There is no agreement between them, so one is multiplied by the other, reaching six. For the khuntha from it, on the assumption of being female, two shares; on being male, three. So he takes half of the two shares, and three does not have a proper half, so six is multiplied by two, reaching twelve. Thus for the khuntha is six on the assumption of being male and four on the assumption of being female. He takes half of the two shares: five, because half of six is three and half of four is two. Shams al-A'imma said: They both went out from al-Sha'bi's saying and did not act by it. In al-Fath: The author of al-Hidayah delaying [mentioning] Muhammad's saying indicates his preference, because all agree on reducing his share, and what Muhammad went to is less than what Abu Yusuf went to.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage details the inheritance rule for the ambiguous khuntha: he receives the lesser of the shares calculated based on him being male or female, or nothing if deprived under both assumptions. Examples illustrate this: in a case with a husband, mother, and full sister (who is khuntha), the khuntha gets the residue as an 'asaba (one-sixth) rather than half, because that is less. Another example: father dies leaving a son and a khuntha child; the son gets two shares, khuntha one, based on Abu Hanifa. The passage then presents a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the inheritance calculation when both a son and a khuntha are present. Al-Sha'bi (and later Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held that the khuntha gets half of what a male and female would get, but they differed on the calculation method: Abu Yusuf considered each's share in isolation, giving the khuntha three-fourths of the estate, resulting in a 4:3 ratio (son:khuntha). Muhammad considered the hypothetical scenarios of khuntha being male or female together, arriving at a 7:5 ratio (son:khuntha). The passage ends by noting that al-Hidayah prefers Muhammad's calculation as it gives less to the khuntha, aligning with the principle of giving the lesser share.

Key Terms
أقل النصيبين (aqall al-nasibayn): The lesser of the two shares: the khuntha inherits the minimum between what he would get as male and as female
عصبة (asabah): A residuary heir who takes what remains after Quranic shares; the khuntha may inherit as 'asaba if no male excludes him
عول (awl): Proportional reduction of shares when the sum of fractions exceeds the estate

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first example (husband, mother, full sister khuntha), what share does the sister receive according to Abu Hanifa?
A) 1/2
B) 1/6
C) 3/8
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The ambiguous khuntha inherits the lesser of his male and female shares, or nothing if deprived under one estimation.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Abu Yusuf vs Muhammad on the Son+Khuntha Case
Detailed calculation methods in the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the khuntha's share according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad and identify the practical difference.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad both follow al-Sha'bi's principle but differ on method, yielding 3/7 vs 5/12.

When a son and a khuntha are the only heirs, the calculation becomes complex. Both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad adopt al-Sha'bi's rule that the khuntha gets half of male and half of female shares, but they differ in how to apply it. This lesson unpacks their methods and the resulting shares.

Guided Path
1
Understand al-Sha'bi's principle
Al-Sha'bi held that the khuntha gets half the share of a male and half the share of a female. This forms the basis for both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
This differs from Abu Hanifa's direct 'lesser of two shares' rule.
2
Learn Abu Yusuf's method: individual isolation
Consider each heir alone: son alone takes all; khuntha alone, if male takes all, if female takes half. Average these: son gets all (1), khuntha gets (1 + 1/2)/2 = 3/4. So base shares: son 4, khuntha 3 (by making each quarter a share).
This gives son 4/7, khuntha 3/7 of the estate.
3
Learn Muhammad's method: hypothetical scenarios
Consider two scenarios: if khuntha male, estate halves between son and khuntha; if female, thirds (son 2/3, khuntha 1/3). LCM of 2 and 3 is 6. Under male scenario, khuntha gets 3/6; under female, 2/6. Average: (3+2)/2 = 2.5/6, but since half of 3 is 1.5 and half of 2 is 1, total 2.5, not integer. Multiply by 2 to get 12: male: 6/12, female: 4/12, average 5/12. So son gets 7/12, khuntha 5/12.
This gives khuntha 5/12, which is less than 3/7 (≈0.4167 vs 0.4286).
4
Compare the results and note the tarjih
Muhammad's share is slightly smaller, so it aligns better with the principle of giving the minimal share. Al-Hidayah prefers Muhammad's view.
The dispute highlights the complexity of applying general principles to ambiguous cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقل النصيبين: المراد بأقل النصيبين أسوأ الحالين فيشمل حالة الحرمان] يعني للخنثى المشكل في الميراث الأقل من نصيب الذكر ومن نصيب الأنثى، فإنه ينظر نصيبه على أنه ذكر، وعلى أنه أنثى، فيعطى الأقل منهما، وإن كان محروما على أحد التقديرين فلا شيء له، فلو تركت امرأة زوجا وأما وأختا لأب وأم، وهي خنثى كان للزوج النصف، وللأم الثلث، وللخنثى ما بقي، وهو السدس على أنه عصبة؛ لأنه أقل، ولو قدر أنثى كان له النصف، وكانت المسألة تعول إلى ثمانية.  كتاب الخنثى ٥١٢ أحكام الخنثى فلو مات أبوه وترك ابنا له سهمان، وللخنثى سهم. أي للابن = عند أبي حنيفة . لو تركت زوجا وأما وأخوين من أم وأخا لأب وأم وهو خنثى، كان للزوج النصف، وللأم السدس، وللأخوين للأم الثلث، ولا شيء للخنثى؛ لأنه عصبة، و لم يفضل له شيء، ولو قدر أنثى، كان له النصف، وعالت المسألة إلى تسعة وهذا المذكور من حكم الخنثى هو مذهب أبي حنيفة، وهو قول عامة الصحابة، وعليه الفتوى وقال الشعبي للخنثى نصف ميراث ذكر، ونصف ميراث أنثى، وعن ابن عباس ما مثله؛ لأنه مجهول، وبه قال أبو يوسف ومحمد ومالك ،وأحمد، وعند الشافعي له أظهر الحالتين، وتوقف الزيادة على نصيبه إلى أن يتبين أمره أو يصطلح هو والورثة. (فتح، عيني، مسكين) فلو مات أبوه إلخ : أوضح المصنف الحكم المذكور بالتمثيل أي فلو مات أبو الخنثى وترك ابنا، فللابن سهمان، وللخنثى سهم؛ لأنه الأقل، وهو متيقن به فيستحقه، وعلى قول الشافعي الذي ذكرناه الآن: للخنثى الثلث، وللابن النصف؛ لأنه المتيقن ويوقف السدس، واختلف أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمها في هذا على قول الشعبي؛ لأن عنده للخنثى نصف ميراث ذكر ونصف ميراث أنثى، فقال محمد المال بينهما على اثني عشر سهما للابن سبعة، وللخنثى خمسة، وقال أبو يوسف المال بينهما على سبعة أسهم للابن أربعة، وللخنثى ثلاثة، اعتبر نصيب كل واحد منهما حالة انفراده، فإن الذكر لو كان وحده كان له كل المال، والخنثى لو كان وحده إن كان ذكرا كان له كل المال وإن كان أنثى كان له نصف المال فيأخذ نصف النصيبين، نصف الكل ونصف النصف، وذلك ثلاثة أرباع المال، وللابن كل المال، فيجعل كل ربع سهما، فبلغ سبعة أسهم: للابن أربعة، وللخنثى ثلاثة، وإنما كان كذلك؛ لأن الابن يستحق الكل عند الانفراد والخنثى ثلاثة أرباع، وليس للمال كل، وثلاثة أرباع، فيضرب كل واحد منهما في جميع حقه اعتبارا بطريق العول والمضاربة. ومحمد به اعتبر نصيب كل واحد منهما في حالة الاجتماع، فقال: لو كان الخنثى ذكرا كان المال بينهما نصفين ولو كان أنثى كان أثلاثا، فالقسمة على تقدير ذكورته من اثنين وعلى تقدير أنوثته من ثلاثة، وليس بينهما موافقة فتضرب إحداهما في الأخرى، تبلغ ستة، للخنثى منها على تقدير أنه أنثى سهمان، وعلى تقدير أنه ذكر ثلاثة، فله نصف النصيبين، وليس للثلاثة نصف صحيح، فتضرب الستة في اثنين تبلغ أثنى عشر، فيكون للخنثى ستة على تقدير أنه ذكر وأربعة على تقدير أنه أنثى فيأخذ نصف النصيبين خمسة؛ لأن نصف الستة ثلاثة ونصف الأربعة اثنان وقال شمس الأئمة: خرجا قول الشعبي و لم يأخذا به رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٨/٢] وقال في "الفتح": وفي تأخير صاحب الهداية قول محمد إشارة إلى اختياره؛ لأن الكل متفقون على تقليل نصيبه، وما ذهب إليه محمد أقل مما ذهب إليه أبو يوسف.
The lesser of the two shares: what is meant by 'lesser of the two shares' is the worse of the two states, which includes the case of being deprived. That is, for the ambiguous khuntha in inheritance, the lesser of the male share and the female share. He is given the lesser of the two, and if he would be deprived on one estimation, he gets nothing. For example, if a woman leaves a husband, a mother, and a sister [full] and she is a khuntha, the husband gets half, the mother gets one-third, and the khuntha gets what remains, which is one-sixth as an 'asaba (residuary), because it is less. If she were estimated as female, she would get half and the problem would 'awl to eight. If his father died leaving a son, for the son two shares and for the khuntha one share. That is for the son according to Abu Hanifa. If a woman left a husband, a mother, two maternal brothers, and a full brother who is a khuntha: for the husband half, for the mother one-sixth, for the two maternal brothers one-third, and nothing for the khuntha because he is an 'asaba and nothing remained for him. If she were estimated as female, she would get half and the problem would 'awl to nine. This mentioned ruling of the khuntha is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa and the saying of the majority of the Companions, and upon it is the fatwa. Al-Sha'bi said: For the khuntha is half the inheritance of a male and half the inheritance of a female. And from Ibn 'Abbas something like it, because he is unknown. And Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Malik, and Ahmad said the same. According to al-Shafi'i, he gets the more apparent of the two states and the increase over his share is suspended until his matter becomes clear or he and the heirs reach a settlement. 'If his father died, etc.': The author clarified the mentioned ruling by example. That is, if the father of the khuntha dies leaving a son, for the son two shares and for the khuntha one share, because it is the lesser and it is certain, so he receives it. According to the Shafi'i view we mentioned, for the khuntha is one-third, for the son half, and one-sixth is suspended. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differed on this according to al-Sha'bi's saying, because according to him the khuntha gets half the inheritance of a male and half of a female. Muhammad said: The wealth is divided between them into twelve shares: for the son seven, for the khuntha five. Abu Yusuf said: The wealth is divided into seven shares: for the son four, for the khuntha three. He considered each one's share in isolation: if the male were alone, he would get all; if the khuntha were alone, if male all, if female half. So he takes half of the two shares: half of the whole and half of the half, which is three-fourths. For the son is all the wealth. So each quarter is made one share, making seven shares: for the son four, for the khuntha three. It is like this because the son is entitled to all when alone, and the khuntha to three-fourths, and the wealth is [divided] into all and three-fourths, so each multiplies in his entire right considering the way of 'awl and partnership. Muhammad considered each one's share in the situation of meeting. He said: If the khuntha were male, the wealth would be halves; if female, thirds. The division on the assumption of his maleness is from two, and on his femaleness from three. There is no agreement between them, so one is multiplied by the other, reaching six. For the khuntha from it, on the assumption of being female, two shares; on being male, three. So he takes half of the two shares, and three does not have a proper half, so six is multiplied by two, reaching twelve. Thus for the khuntha is six on the assumption of being male and four on the assumption of being female. He takes half of the two shares: five, because half of six is three and half of four is two. Shams al-A'imma said: They both went out from al-Sha'bi's saying and did not act by it. In al-Fath: The author of al-Hidayah delaying [mentioning] Muhammad's saying indicates his preference, because all agree on reducing his share, and what Muhammad went to is less than what Abu Yusuf went to.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage details the inheritance rule for the ambiguous khuntha: he receives the lesser of the shares calculated based on him being male or female, or nothing if deprived under both assumptions. Examples illustrate this: in a case with a husband, mother, and full sister (who is khuntha), the khuntha gets the residue as an 'asaba (one-sixth) rather than half, because that is less. Another example: father dies leaving a son and a khuntha child; the son gets two shares, khuntha one, based on Abu Hanifa. The passage then presents a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the inheritance calculation when both a son and a khuntha are present. Al-Sha'bi (and later Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held that the khuntha gets half of what a male and female would get, but they differed on the calculation method: Abu Yusuf considered each's share in isolation, giving the khuntha three-fourths of the estate, resulting in a 4:3 ratio (son:khuntha). Muhammad considered the hypothetical scenarios of khuntha being male or female together, arriving at a 7:5 ratio (son:khuntha). The passage ends by noting that al-Hidayah prefers Muhammad's calculation as it gives less to the khuntha, aligning with the principle of giving the lesser share.

Key Terms
أقل النصيبين (aqall al-nasibayn): The principle of giving the lesser of two shares, but here the dispute is on how to calculate that lesser share.
نصف ميراث ذكر ونصف ميراث أنثى (nisf mīrāth dhakar wa nisf mīrāth unthā): Half of male inheritance and half of female inheritance – al-Sha'bi's rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 3/7
B) 5/12

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the khuntha's share yields 3/7 vs 5/12; Muhammad's view is preferred.

Tarjih and Cross-Madhhab Comparison in the Khuntha Case
Tarjih of Muhammad's view and cross-madhhab comparison with Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why al-Hidayah prefers Muhammad's view and compare it with the Shafi'i suspension method.

Core Idea
Al-Hidayah prefers Muhammad's calculation because it gives the lesser share, consistent with the principle; Shafi'i suspends the extra share until resolution.

After presenting the intra-Hanafi dispute, the source concludes with the tarjih (preference) for Muhammad's view and mentions the Shafi'i approach. This lesson analyzes the reasoning behind the tarjih and contrasts it with the cross-madhhab perspective.

Guided Path
1
Understand the tarjih criterion
All scholars agree on minimizing the khuntha's share. Muhammad's method gives 5/12 (≈0.4167), Abu Yusuf's gives 3/7 (≈0.4286). The smaller number is consistent with the principle of aqall al-nasibayn.
The statement 'الكل متفقون على تقليل نصيبه' indicates consensus on the goal.
2
Note the indicator of preference in al-Hidayah
Al-Marghinani delays mentioning Muhammad's view, which is a subtle indication of preference (al-Tahavi also uses this style).
This is a known method of tarjih by sequence.
3
Compare with the Shafi'i view
Al-Shafi'i gives the khuntha the more apparent share (i.e., the larger of the two possibilities) and suspends the increase over his share until the ambiguity is resolved by clarification or agreement.
This differs significantly: Hanafi gives a fixed share, Shafi'i gives a provisional one.
4
Evaluate the practical outcomes
Under Shafi'i, the khuntha might receive a larger share if later determined female, or a smaller if male? Actually, Shafi'i gives the more apparent, which might be the larger if khuntha appears more female? The text says 'أظهر الحالتين' which is the more apparent state, not necessarily the larger. But in practice, it often leads to a larger share.
The suspended portion creates co-ownership until resolution, which can be problematic.

The lesser of the two shares: what is meant by 'lesser of the two shares' is the worse of the two states, which includes the case of being deprived. That is, for the ambiguous khuntha in inheritance, the lesser of the male share and the female share. He is given the lesser of the two, and if he would be deprived on one estimation, he gets nothing. For example, if a woman leaves a husband, a mother, and a sister [full] and she is a khuntha, the husband gets half, the mother gets one-third, and the khuntha gets what remains, which is one-sixth as an 'asaba (residuary), because it is less. If she were estimated as female, she would get half and the problem would 'awl to eight. If his father died leaving a son, for the son two shares and for the khuntha one share. That is for the son according to Abu Hanifa. If a woman left a husband, a mother, two maternal brothers, and a full brother who is a khuntha: for the husband half, for the mother one-sixth, for the two maternal brothers one-third, and nothing for the khuntha because he is an 'asaba and nothing remained for him. If she were estimated as female, she would get half and the problem would 'awl to nine. This mentioned ruling of the khuntha is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa and the saying of the majority of the Companions, and upon it is the fatwa. Al-Sha'bi said: For the khuntha is half the inheritance of a male and half the inheritance of a female. And from Ibn 'Abbas something like it, because he is unknown. And Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Malik, and Ahmad said the same. According to al-Shafi'i, he gets the more apparent of the two states and the increase over his share is suspended until his matter becomes clear or he and the heirs reach a settlement. 'If his father died, etc.': The author clarified the mentioned ruling by example. That is, if the father of the khuntha dies leaving a son, for the son two shares and for the khuntha one share, because it is the lesser and it is certain, so he receives it. According to the Shafi'i view we mentioned, for the khuntha is one-third, for the son half, and one-sixth is suspended. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differed on this according to al-Sha'bi's saying, because according to him the khuntha gets half the inheritance of a male and half of a female. Muhammad said: The wealth is divided between them into twelve shares: for the son seven, for the khuntha five. Abu Yusuf said: The wealth is divided into seven shares: for the son four, for the khuntha three. He considered each one's share in isolation: if the male were alone, he would get all; if the khuntha were alone, if male all, if female half. So he takes half of the two shares: half of the whole and half of the half, which is three-fourths. For the son is all the wealth. So each quarter is made one share, making seven shares: for the son four, for the khuntha three. It is like this because the son is entitled to all when alone, and the khuntha to three-fourths, and the wealth is [divided] into all and three-fourths, so each multiplies in his entire right considering the way of 'awl and partnership. Muhammad considered each one's share in the situation of meeting. He said: If the khuntha were male, the wealth would be halves; if female, thirds. The division on the assumption of his maleness is from two, and on his femaleness from three. There is no agreement between them, so one is multiplied by the other, reaching six. For the khuntha from it, on the assumption of being female, two shares; on being male, three. So he takes half of the two shares, and three does not have a proper half, so six is multiplied by two, reaching twelve. Thus for the khuntha is six on the assumption of being male and four on the assumption of being female. He takes half of the two shares: five, because half of six is three and half of four is two. Shams al-A'imma said: They both went out from al-Sha'bi's saying and did not act by it. In al-Fath: The author of al-Hidayah delaying [mentioning] Muhammad's saying indicates his preference, because all agree on reducing his share, and what Muhammad went to is less than what Abu Yusuf went to.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage details the inheritance rule for the ambiguous khuntha: he receives the lesser of the shares calculated based on him being male or female, or nothing if deprived under both assumptions. Examples illustrate this: in a case with a husband, mother, and full sister (who is khuntha), the khuntha gets the residue as an 'asaba (one-sixth) rather than half, because that is less. Another example: father dies leaving a son and a khuntha child; the son gets two shares, khuntha one, based on Abu Hanifa. The passage then presents a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the inheritance calculation when both a son and a khuntha are present. Al-Sha'bi (and later Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held that the khuntha gets half of what a male and female would get, but they differed on the calculation method: Abu Yusuf considered each's share in isolation, giving the khuntha three-fourths of the estate, resulting in a 4:3 ratio (son:khuntha). Muhammad considered the hypothetical scenarios of khuntha being male or female together, arriving at a 7:5 ratio (son:khuntha). The passage ends by noting that al-Hidayah prefers Muhammad's calculation as it gives less to the khuntha, aligning with the principle of giving the lesser share.

Key Terms
ترجيح (tarjih): Preference of one opinion over another within the school.
أظهر الحالتين (azhar al-halayn): The more apparent of the two states; used by Shafi'i for the khuntha's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does al-Hidayah prefer Muhammad's view over Abu Yusuf's?
A) Because Muhammad was the teacher of Abu Yusuf
B) Because Muhammad's view gives a smaller share to the khuntha
C) Because the majority of scholars follow Muhammad
D) Because the text of the Quran supports it

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi view gives the khuntha 5/12 with a son, chosen because it minimizes the share; Shafi'i suspends the extra portion until clarification.

Inheritance of the Khuntha: Abu Hanifa's Rule and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Faraid: intra-Hanafi dispute on khuntha inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's rule for the khuntha's inheritance, calculate shares using his method, and compare it with the methods of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
The khuntha receives the smaller certain share; any excess is suspended until gender is known.

This lesson explores the inheritance of a hermaphrodite (khuntha) in Hanafi law. The passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents Imam Abu Hanifa's position based on certainty, then discusses alternative views from al-Sha'bi and the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. We will work through the calculations and understand why the Hanafi school prefers the minimal share.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic scenario and Abu Hanifa's ruling
Read the passage's opening example: a father dies leaving a son and a khuntha. Under Abu Hanifa, the son takes two shares, the khuntha one share. This is the minimal certain share (assuming khuntha is female).
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Understand the principle of certainty
Abu Hanifa's method is based on yaqin: we are certain the khuntha is at least female, so we give that share. Any additional share for possible maleness is doubtful and suspended.
This avoids giving what may be unduly taken from other heirs.
3
Contrast with al-Sha'bi's average approach
Al-Sha'bi and others (including Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in one narration) argue the khuntha should get half of male plus half of female shares. However, they differ on the calculation method.
Abu Yusuf uses isolation; Muhammad uses coexistence.
4
Examine the numerical outcomes
Work through the numbers: Abu Hanifa: son 2/3, khuntha 1/3. Abu Yusuf: son 4/7, khuntha 3/7. Muhammad: son 7/12, khuntha 5/12. Notice Muhammad's share is less than Abu Yusuf's.
The author of al-Hidayah indicates preference for Muhammad's because it gives less to the khuntha.
5
Understand the tarjih
Abu Hanifa's view is from the majority of Companions and is based on certainty, so it is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
This is explicitly stated as 'عليه الفتوى'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو مات أبوه وترك ابنا له سهمان، وللخنثى سهم. أي للابن = عند أبي حنيفة. ولو تركت زوجا وأما وأخوين من أم وأخا لأب وأم وهو خنثى، كان للزوج النصف، وللأم السدس، وللأخوين للأم الثلث، ولا شيء للخنثى؛ لأنه عصبة، و لم يفضل له شيء، ولو قدر أنثى، كان له النصف، وعالت المسألة إلى تسعة وهذا المذكور من حكم الخنثى هو مذهب أبي حنيفة، وهو قول عامة الصحابة، وعليه الفتوى وقال الشعبي للخنثى نصف ميراث ذكر، ونصف ميراث أنثى، وعن ابن عباس ما مثله؛ لأنه مجهول، وبه قال أبو يوسف ومحمد ومالك ،وأحمد، وعند الشافعي له أظهر الحالتين، وتوقف الزيادة على نصيبه إلى أن يتبين أمره أو يصطلح هو والورثة. (فتح، عيني، مسكين) فلو مات أبوه إلخ : أوضح المصنف الحكم المذكور بالتمثيل أي فلو مات أبو الخنثى وترك ابنا، فللابن سهمان، وللخنثى سهم؛ لأنه الأقل، وهو متيقن به فيستحقه، وعلى قول الشافعي الذي ذكرناه الآن: للخنثى الثلث، وللابن النصف؛ لأنه المتيقن ويوقف السدس، واختلف أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمها في هذا على قول الشعبي؛ لأن عنده للخنثى نصف ميراث ذكر ونصف ميراث أنثى، فقال محمد المال بينهما على اثني عشر سهما للابن سبعة، وللخنثى خمسة، وقال أبو يوسف المال بينهما على سبعة أسهم للابن أربعة، وللخنثى ثلاثة، اعتبر نصيب كل واحد منهما حالة انفراده، فإن الذكر لو كان وحده كان له كل المال، والخنثى لو كان وحده إن كان ذكرا كان له كل المال وإن كان أنثى كان له نصف المال فيأخذ نصف النصيبين، نصف الكل ونصف النصف، وذلك ثلاثة أرباع المال، وللابن كل المال، فيجعل كل ربع سهما، فبلغ سبعة أسهم: للابن أربعة، وللخنثى ثلاثة، وإنما كان كذلك؛ لأن الابن يستحق الكل عند الانفراد والخنثى ثلاثة أرباع، وليس للمال كل، وثلاثة أرباع، فيضرب كل واحد منهما في جميع حقه اعتبارا بطريق العول والمضاربة. ومحمد به اعتبر نصيب كل واحد منهما في حالة الاجتماع، فقال: لو كان الخنثى ذكرا كان المال بينهما نصفين ولو كان أنثى كان أثلاثا، فالقسمة على تقدير ذكورته من اثنين وعلى تقدير أنوثته من ثلاثة، وليس بينهما ،موافقة فتضرب إحداهما في الأخرى، تبلغ ستة، للخنثى منها على تقدير أنه أنثى سهمان، وعلى تقدير أنه ذكر ثلاثة، فله نصف النصيبين، وليس للثلاثة نصف صحيح، فتضرب الستة في اثنين تبلغ أثنى عشر، فيكون للخنثى ستة على تقدير أنه ذكر وأربعة على تقدير أنه أنثى فيأخذ نصف النصيبين خمسة؛ لأن نصف الستة ثلاثة ونصف الأربعة اثنان وقال شمس الأئمة: خرجا قول الشعبي و لم يأخذا به رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٨/٢] وقال في "الفتح": وفي تأخير صاحب الهداية قول محمد إشارة إلى اختياره؛ لأن الكل متفقون على تقليل نصيبه، وما ذهب إليه محمد أقل مما ذهب إليه أبو يوسف.
If his father dies and leaves a son, he (the son) has two shares, and the khuntha has one share. That is for the son according to Abu Hanifa. And if (a woman) leaves a husband, a mother, two uterine brothers, and a full brother who is khuntha, the husband gets half, the mother a sixth, the two uterine brothers a third, and nothing for the khuntha because he is an 'asaba (residuary) and nothing remains for him. If (the khuntha) were female, she would get half, and the case would 'awl to nine. This mentioned ruling on the khuntha is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, and it is the saying of the generality of Companions, and upon it is fatwa. Al-Sha'bi said: The khuntha gets half the inheritance of a male and half the inheritance of a female. Ibn 'Abbas had something similar because (the khuntha) is unknown. Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Malik, and Ahmad said the same. According to al-Shafi'i, he gets the more apparent of the two states, and the increase over his share is suspended until his matter becomes clear or he and the heirs compromise. (Fath, 'Ayni, Miskin) 'If his father dies etc.': The author clarified the mentioned ruling by example, i.e., if the father of the khuntha dies leaving a son, the son has two shares and the khuntha one share because it is the lesser amount and is certain, so he takes it. According to al-Shafi'i's statement we just mentioned: the khuntha gets a third, the son a half because it is certain, and one-sixth is suspended. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad — may Allah have mercy on them — differed on this based on al-Sha'bi's statement because in his view the khuntha gets half of a male's inheritance and half of a female's. Muhammad said the estate is divided into twelve shares: the son gets seven, the khuntha five. Abu Yusuf said the estate is divided into seven shares: the son gets four, the khuntha three. He (Abu Yusuf) considered each one's share in isolation: if the male were alone, he would take all the property; if the khuntha were alone and were male, he would take all; if female, half. So he takes half of the two shares: half of the whole and half of half, that is three-quarters of the estate. The son takes the entire estate in isolation. Thus each quarter is made a share, totaling seven shares: four for the son, three for the khuntha. It is like this because the son is entitled to the whole when alone, and the khuntha to three-quarters, so the estate is (divided into) whole and three-quarters, and each is multiplied by his total right, following the method of 'awl and proportional distribution. Muhammad considered each one's share in the state of coexistence: he said if the khuntha were male, the estate would be divided in half; if female, in thirds. So division on the assumption of masculinity is from two, on femininity from three, and there is no congruence between them. Multiply one by the other, total six: for the khuntha, on the assumption that she is female, two shares; on assumption male, three shares. So he takes half of the two shares: there is no whole half of three, so multiply six by two, making twelve. Then the khuntha gets six on assumption male and four on assumption female, so he takes half of the two shares: five, because half of six is three and half of four is two. Shams al-A'imma said: they both diverged from al-Sha'bi's statement and did not act upon it. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:498) And in al-Fath: the author of al-Hidayah's delay in mentioning Muhammad's statement indicates his preference, because all agree on minimizing his share, and what Muhammad held is less than what Abu Yusuf held.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage discusses the inheritance of a hermaphrodite (khuntha) — a person with ambiguous or both male and female genitalia — in Hanafi fiqh. The author first states the position of Imam Abu Hanifa: when a khuntha inherits alongside a clear male, the khuntha takes the smaller of the two possible shares (i.e., assuming the khuntha is female, which gives less). This is based on certainty: we know the khuntha must be at least a female, so we give the lesser share and suspend any excess until clarity. The passage then presents an example: a woman dies leaving husband, mother, two uterine brothers, and a full brother who is khuntha. According to Abu Hanifa, the husband takes 1/2, mother 1/6, two uterine brothers 1/3 (total = 1), so no residue for the full brother as asaba. But if the khuntha were female, she would take 1/2, making the total exceed 1, causing 'awl to 9. The ruling of Abu Hanifa is said to be the view of the majority of Companions. Then other views are mentioned: al-Sha'bi and Ibn 'Abbas said the khuntha takes half of a male's share and half of a female's share — a compromise. This was adopted by Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Malik, and Ahmad. Al-Shafi'i said the khuntha takes the more apparent of the two states (e.g., if looks more male, he is treated as male; if more female, as female), and any increase over the minimum is suspended until clarification or agreement. The passage then explains the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, both following al-Sha'bi's principle but differing in calculation. Abu Yusuf's method: consider each heir's share if alone — son would take all (1), khuntha would take 1 if male or 1/2 if female, average = 3/4. Then the ratio of son's share (1) to khuntha's share (3/4) is 4:3, so son gets 4/7, khuntha 3/7. Muhammad's method: consider the two scenarios together — if khuntha is male, estate split 1/2 each; if female, son gets 2/3, khuntha 1/3. Find the LCM of denominators: 2 and 3 = 6. On male assumption: khuntha gets 3, on female: 2. The average of 3 and 2 is 2.5, which is not a whole number, so multiply by 2 to get 12 shares: on male: khuntha 6, son 6; on female: khuntha 4, son 8. Average for khuntha = (6+4)/2 = 5, son = (6+8)/2 = 7. Thus Muhamad gives khuntha 5/12 and son 7/12. Imam al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah placed Muhammad's view after Abu Yusuf's, indicating preference because it gives less to the khuntha and all agree on minimizing his share. The passage ends with a note that both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad diverged from al-Sha'bi's strict wording but did not actually apply it. This is a classic example of Hanafi analytical reasoning in inheritance, showing how different ijtihad methods yield different results even from the same principle.

Key Terms
الخنثى (al-khuntha): A person with ambiguous genitalia, neither clearly male nor female, or having both.
العصبة (al-'asabah): Residuary heir who takes the remainder after Quranic shares.
التعصيب (al-ta'sib): The rule that the khuntha inherits as an 'asaba if there is residue; otherwise nothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when a khuntha inherits alongside a clear son, what share does the khuntha receive?
A) Half of the son's share
B) The share of a female (i.e., half of a male's share in that context)
C) The average of male and female shares
D) An equal share with the son

Key Takeaway
The khuntha receives only the certain minimum share; any excess is suspended, and this is the operative fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Priority of Expenses from the Estate: Shroud, Debt, Will, Inheritance
Ruling statement defining order of priority from estate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of priority from the deceased's estate and explain the Hanafi ruling that debts to Allah are waived upon death.

Core Idea
Shroud first, then debt, then will, then inheritance; debts to Allah fall away upon death.

This lesson introduces the foundational order of claims against the deceased's estate. Knowing this sequence is crucial for correct funeral practice, debt clearance, will execution, and inheritance distribution. We will also examine a key difference with the Shafi'i school regarding debts owed to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four-step order
From the source text, extract the sequence: preparation (tajhiz), debt (dayn), will (wasiyyah), then division among heirs. Write them down in order.
The text states 'yabda'u min tarakati al-mayyiti bi-tajhizihi, thumma daynihi, thumma wasiyyatihi, thumma yuqsimu bayna warathatihi'.
2
Define the estate (tarika) and its exclusions
Understand what constitutes the estate: what the deceased leaves free from the attachment of another's right in a specific item. Note that if a specific item is encumbered (e.g., pawned), that right takes precedence even over shrouding.
The source says: 'tarikatu al-mayyiti ma yatrukuhu khalian 'an ta'alliqi haqqi ghayrihi bi-'aynihi'.
3
Distinguish debts to people vs. debts to Allah
The text prioritizes debts owed to people (dayn) over the will. Debts to Allah (like unpaid zakat, kaffarah) are waived upon death in the Hanafi school. Compare with the Shafi'i view that such debts must be paid from the estate.
The commentary says: 'al-murad bi-al-dayn alladhi mutalib min jihati al-'ibad la nahwa al-zakat... fa innaha tasqutu bi-al-mawt 'indana khilafan li-al-Shafi'i'.
4
Understand the will's limitation to one-third
After shrouding and debts, the will is executed from one-third of the remaining estate. Heirs' permission is needed if the will exceeds one-third.
The text says: 'thumma yabda'u bi-tanfidhi wasiyyatihi min thulthi ma baqiya ba'da al-tajhiz wa al-dayn'.
5
Recognize the three categories of heirs
The source concludes by listing heirs: Quranic shareholders (ashab al-fara'id), agnates ('asabat), and distant kindred (dhawi al-arham). They are prioritized in that order.
The text says: 'al-wurathu thalathatu asnaf: ashabu al-fara'id wa al-'asabat wa dhawi al-arham'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الفرائض يبدأ من تركة الميت بتجهيزه، ثم دينه ثم وصيته، ثم يقسم بين ورثته، أي بقضاء دينه أي بتنفيذ الباقي من المال هذا كتاب الفرائض: لما فرغ من بيان نصف العلم شرع في بيان النصف الآخر، والمناسبة بين الكتابين: أن الوصية أخت الميراث، والفرائض جمع فريضة من الفرض، وهو التقدير، يقال: فرض القاضي النفقة أي قدرها، وسمي العلم فرائض؛ لأن الله تعالى قدره بنفسه، ولم يفوض تقديره إلى ملك مقرب ولا نبي مرسل، وبين نصيب كل واحد من النصف، والربع والثمن، والثلثين والثلث، والسدس، بخلاف سائر الأحكام كالصلاة والزكاة والحج وغيرها؛ فإن النصوص فيها مجملة كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلاةَ وَآتُوا الزَّكَاةَ﴾ (البقرة:٤٣) وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ البيت (آل عمران: ٩٧) وإنما السنة بينتها، وهذا العلم من أشرف العلوم ، وقال علي: "العلم ثلاثة، وما سوى فضل آية محكمة أو سنة قائمة أو فريضة عادلة، وقد حث عليها على تعليمه وتعلمه بقوله: "تعلموا الفرائض وعلموها؛ فإنه نصف العلم. وهو ينسى، وهو أول شيء ينزع من أمتي [ رمز الحقائق: ٥١٢/٢] (ملا مسكين) تركة الميت التركة ما يتركه الميت خاليا عن تعلق حق الغير ،بعينه، وإن كان حق الغير متعلقا بعينه كالرهن والعبد الجاني، والمشترى قبل القبض فإن صاحبه يقدم على التجهيز كما في حال حياته [رمز الحقائق: ٥١٢/٢] بتجهيزه: أي يبدأ من تركة الميت بتجهيزه من غير تقتير ولا تبذير وهو قدر كفن الكفاية أو كفن السنة، أو قدر ما يلبسه في حياته من أوسط ثيابه، أو من الذي كان يتزين به في الأعياد والجمع، والزيارات على ما اختلفوا فيه. [رمز الحقائق: ٥١٢/٢] واجب ثم دينه بالجر أي يبدأ بوفاء دينه من جميع ماله إن وفت التركة بها، وإن لم يف يؤخر ما ثبت في المرض بإقراره عن سائر الديون وباقي الديون سواء، أخذ كل ذي حق بقدر حقه، وإنما قدم الدين على الوصية؛ لأنه والوصية تبرع، والمراد بالدين الذي مطالب من جهة العباد لا نحو الزكاة والكفارة والفدية وغيرها من الحقوق الواجبة لله تعالى فإنها تسقط بالموت عندنا خلافا للشافعي كذا قالوا وفيه نظر؛ إذ لو سقطت بالموت لم يبق للتكليف فائدة، ولما وجبت عليه الوصية، فالصواب أن يقال: لما ملكه بالموت إلى الوارث لم يجب على الوارث شيء إلا أن يوصي كوصية بسائر التبرعات. (ملتقطا من الشروح) ثم وصيته بالجر أيضا أي ثم يبدأ بتنفيذ وصيته من ثلث ما بقي بعد التجهيز والدين، وفي أكثر إلا بإجازة الورثة على ما مر ثم هذا ليس بتقديم على الورثة في المعنى، بل هو شريك لهم حتى إذا سلم له شيء سلم للورثة ضعفه أو أكثر. [ رمز الحقائق: ٥١٣/٢] بين ورثته اعلم أن الورثة ثلاثة أصناف أصحاب الفرائض والعصبات وذوو الأرحام، فيبدأ أولا بالصنف الأول أي أصحاب الفرائض، كما فعله المصنف حيث قال: وهم ذو فرض.
Book of Inheritances: From the estate of the deceased, one begins with his preparation [shroud], then his debt, then his will, then it is divided among his heirs. That is, after paying his debt and executing his will from the remaining wealth. This is the Book of Inheritances: When he finished explaining half of knowledge, he began explaining the other half. The connection between the two books is that the will is the sister of inheritance. Fara'id is the plural of faridah, from fard, which means estimation. It is said: 'The judge fard (establishes) the maintenance' i.e., estimates it. This knowledge is called fara'id because Allah the Exalted estimated it Himself, and did not delegate its estimation to any close angel or sent prophet, and He specified the share of each one: half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, third, and sixth, contrary to other rulings like prayer, zakat, hajj, etc., for the texts about them are general, such as 'Establish prayer and give zakat' (2:43) and 'For Allah, upon the people, is the pilgrimage to the House' (3:97), and the Sunnah only clarified them. This knowledge is among the noblest of sciences. Ali said: 'Knowledge is three, and what is beyond that is surplus: a decisive verse, an established Sunnah, or a just inheritance portion.' He urged teaching and learning it by saying: 'Learn the fara'id and teach them, for it is half of knowledge. It is forgotten, and it is the first thing to be taken away from my nation.' [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/512] (Mulla Miskin) 'Estate of the deceased': The estate is what the deceased leaves free from the attachment of another's right in a specific item. Even if another's right is attached to a specific item, like a pawn, a slave who committed an offense, or goods bought before taking possession, then the claimant takes precedence over the preparation, as in his lifetime. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/512] 'With his preparation': i.e., from the deceased's estate begins with his preparation without extravagance or stinginess. It is the amount of a sufficient shroud or a shroud according to Sunnah, or the amount of what he used to wear in his life from his medium-priced clothes, or from what he used to adorn himself with on 'Eids, Fridays, and visits, according to differences. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/512] 'Then his debt' is in the genitive, i.e., he begins by paying his debt from all his wealth if the estate is sufficient. If not, what was established during illness by his admission is delayed from other debts, and the remaining debts are equal; each claimant takes according to his share. He prioritized debt over the will because debt is due to creation, while the will is a donation. By debt is meant what is claimed from people, not like zakat, expiation, ransom, and other obligatory rights due to Allah, for they fall away upon death according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. So said they, but there is consideration: if they fell away upon death, there would be no benefit in obligation, and why would the will be obligatory? So the correct statement is that since ownership passes by death to the heir, nothing is obligatory upon the heir unless he wills, like a will for other donations. (Compiled from commentaries) 'Then his will' is also in the genitive, i.e., then he begins to execute his will from one-third of what remains after the preparation and debt. In most cases, it is not valid except with the heirs' permission, as mentioned. This is not a precedence over heirs in meaning; rather, he is a partner with them, such that if something goes to him, double or more goes to the heirs. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/513] 'Among his heirs': Know that the heirs are three types: Quranic shareholders, agnates, and distant kindred. One begins first with the first type, i.e., the Quranic shareholders, as the author did when he said: 'They are the owners of fard.'
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Inheritances (Kitab al-Fara'id) by stating the order of priority from the deceased's estate: first, his shrouding and burial expenses (tajhiz); second, payment of his debts; third, execution of his will (from one-third of the remainder); and fourth, distribution of the rest among his heirs. The text notes that debts to Allah (like unpaid zakat) fall away upon death according to the Hanafi school, unlike the Shafi'i view, but some scholars dispute this. The term 'fara'id' means fixed shares, and this knowledge is praised as half of knowledge because Allah Himself determined the shares. The passage also defines the estate (tarika) and clarifies that if a specific item in the estate is encumbered by another's right (like a pawn), that right takes priority even over burial expenses. Finally, it categorizes heirs into three groups: Quranic shareholders (ashab al-fara'id), agnates (asabat), and distant kindred (dhawi al-arham), with the Quranic shareholders receiving first.

Key Terms
التركة (al-tarikah): What the deceased leaves behind free from the attachment of another's right in a specific item
التجهيز (al-tajhiz): Preparation of the deceased for burial, including shrouding and necessary expenses
الفرائض (al-fara'id): The fixed shares of inheritance specified in the Quran and Sunnah; also the science of inheritance

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct order of priority from the deceased's estate?
A) Debt, will, shrouding, inheritance
B) Shrouding, debt, will, inheritance
C) Will, shrouding, debt, inheritance
D) Shrouding, will, debt, inheritance

Key Takeaway
The estate is used in a fixed order: shroud, debts to people, will (up to one-third), then inheritance; debts to Allah are waived upon death in the Hanafi school.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
12 min
Priority of Rights Attached to the Estate
States the order of spending from the estate and discusses the religious obligations dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of spending from the estate and explain why obligations owed to Allah (e.g., zakat) are not considered debts.

Core Idea
Funeral, debts to humans, will (from one-third), then inheritance — this order is binding in Hanafi law.

The Book of Fara'id opens with a fundamental principle: there is a strict sequence of claims against the deceased's estate. This lesson clarifies that sequence and explains a distinctive Hanafi position: that unpaid religious duties (zakat, expiation) drop upon death and are not treated as debts that must be paid from the estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four items in the sequence
State the order as given in the text: tajhiz (funeral preparation), dayn (debt to humans), wasiyyah (will from one-third of remainder), then distribution among heirs.
The text explicitly says: 'يبدأ من تركة الميت بتجهيزه، ثم دينه ثم وصيته، ثم يقسم بين ورثته.'
2
Distinguish between human debts and religious obligations
Note that the term 'dayn' in this context refers only to financial obligations owed to other people. Religious duties like zakat, kaffarah, and fidyah are categorized differently in Hanafi fiqh.
The commentator explains: 'والمراد بالدين الذي مطالب من جهة العباد لا نحو الزكاة والكفارة والفدية.'
3
Trace the Hanafi reasoning for dropping religious duties
Understand the Hanafi argument: upon death, ownership of the estate transfers to the heirs; the deceased's liability for religious duties ceases because the purpose of obligation (living accountability) ends. The heir is not obligated to fulfill them unless the deceased bequeathed it.
The text states: 'فإنها تسقط بالموت عندنا خلافا للشافعي.'
4
Note the practical consequence of the Shafi'i disagreement
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi fiqh, unpaid zakat is not deducted from the estate unless willed; in Shafi'i fiqh, it is a debt that must be paid before inheritance.
This difference affects how the estate is distributed to heirs.

Source Text
