كتاب الفرائض
الحقوق المتعلقة بالتركة
yبدأ من تركة الميت بتجهيزه، ثم دينه ثم وصيته، ثم يقسم بين ورثته، أي بقضاء دينه أي بتنفيذ الباقي من المال
هذا كتاب الفرائض: لما فرغ من بيان نصف العلم شرع في بيان النصف الآخر، والمناسبة بين الكتابين: أن الوصية أخت الميراث، والفرائض جمع فريضة من الفرض، وهو التقدير، يقال: فرض القاضي النفقة أي قدرها، وسمي العلم فرائض؛ لأن الله تعالى قدره بنفسه، ولم يفوض تقديره إلى ملك مقرب ولا نبي مرسل، وبين نصيب كل واحد من النصف، والربع والثمن، والثلثين والثلث، والسدس، بخلاف سائر الأحكام كالصلاة والزكاة والحج وغيرها؛ فإن النصوص فيها مجملة كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلاةَ وَآتُوا الزَّكَاةَ﴾ (البقرة:٤٣) وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ البيت (آل عمران: ٩٧) وإنما السنة بينتها، وهذا العلم من أشرف العلوم ، وقال علي: "العلم ثلاثة، وما سوى فضل آية محكمة أو سنة قائمة أو فريضة عادلة، وقد حث عليها على تعليمه وتعلمه بقوله: "تعلموا الفرائض وعلموها؛ فإنه نصف العلم. وهو ينسى، وهو أول شيء ينزع من أمتي [ رمز الحقائق: ٥١٢/٢] (ملا مسكين) تركة الميت التركة ما يتركه الميت خاليا عن تعلق حق الغير ،بعينه، وإن كان حق الغير متعلقا بعينه كالرهن والعبد الجاني، والمشترى قبل القبض فإن صاحبه يقدم على التجهيز كما في حال حياته [رمز الحقائق: ٥١٢/٢] بتجهيزه: أي يبدأ من تركة الميت بتجهيزه من غير تقتير ولا تبذير وهو قدر كفن الكفاية أو كفن السنة، أو قدر ما يلبسه في حياته من أوسط ثيابه، أو من الذي كان يتزين به في الأعياد والجمع، والزيارات على ما اختلفوا فيه. [رمز الحقائق: ٥١٢/٢] واجب ثم دينه بالجر أي يبدأ بوفاء دينه من جميع ماله إن وفت التركة بها، وإن لم يف يؤخر ما ثبت في المرض بإقراره عن سائر الديون وباقي الديون سواء، أخذ كل ذي حق بقدر حقه، وإنما قدم الدين على الوصية؛ لأنه والوصية تبرع، والمراد بالدين الذي مطالب من جهة العباد لا نحو الزكاة والكفارة والفدية وغيرها من الحقوق الواجبة لله تعالى فإنها تسقط بالموت عندنا خلافا للشافعي كذا قالوا وفيه نظر؛ إذ لو سقطت بالموت لم يبق للتكليف فائدة، ولما وجبت عليه الوصية، فالصواب أن يقال: لما ملكه بالموت إلى الوارث لم يجب على الوارث شيء إلا أن يوصي كوصية بسائر التبرعات. (ملتقطا من الشروح) ثم وصيته بالجر أيضا أي ثم يبدأ بتنفيذ وصيته من ثلث ما بقي بعد التجهيز والدين، وفي أكثر إلا بإجازة الورثة على ما مر ثم هذا ليس بتقديم على الورثة في المعنى، بل هو شريك لهم حتى إذا سلم له شيء سلم للورثة ضعفه أو أكثر. [ رمز الحقائق: ٥۱۳/۲] بين ورثته اعلم أن الورثة ثلاثة أصناف أصحاب الفرائض والعصبات وذوو الأرحام، فيبدأ أولا بالصنف الأول أي أصحاب الفرائض
Book of Inheritance. The rights attached to the estate. It begins from the estate of the deceased with his preparation (shrouding), then his debt, then his will, then it is divided among his heirs. Meaning: after paying his debt, meaning after executing what remains of the wealth. This is the Book of Inheritance: When he finished explaining half of knowledge, he began explaining the other half. The connection between the two books: the will is the sister of inheritance. 'Fara'id' is the plural of 'faridah' from 'fard' which means determination. It is said: the judge determined the maintenance, i.e., estimated it. This knowledge is called 'fara'id' because Allah Almighty determined it Himself and did not delegate its estimation to a close angel or a sent prophet, and He specified the share of each: half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, third, and sixth, unlike other rulings such as prayer, zakat, hajj, etc.; for the texts therein are general like His statement: 'And establish prayer and give zakat' and 'And for Allah upon the people is the pilgrimage to the House' – rather the Sunnah clarified them. This knowledge is among the most honorable knowledge. And 'Ali said: 'Knowledge is three, and whatever else is extra: a definitive verse, an established Sunnah, or a just inheritance law.' And he encouraged teaching and learning it by saying: 'Learn the inheritance laws and teach them, for it is half of knowledge. It is forgotten, and it is the first thing to be taken away from my nation.' [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/512] (Mulla Miskin) The estate of the deceased: the estate is what the deceased leaves free from any right of others attached to it specifically, but if the right of others is attached to it specifically like a pawn, a slave who committed a crime, or a purchased item before taking possession, then its owner is given priority over the shrouding as during his life. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/512] 'With his preparation': i.e., the preparation of the deceased begins from his estate without stinginess or extravagance. It is the amount of a sufficient shroud or the shroud of the Sunnah, or the amount of what he used to wear in his life from his middle garments, or from what he used to adorn himself with on Eid and Friday and visits, according to their differences. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/512] It is obligatory. 'Then his debt': with genitive case, i.e., paying his debt begins from all his wealth if the estate suffices for it; if not, what was established during illness by his acknowledgment is postponed from other debts, and the remaining debts are equal; each right-holder takes according to his right. Debt is given priority over the will because debt is compulsory while the will is a donation. What is meant by debt is that which is demanded from the perspective of the servants, not like zakat, expiation, ransom, and other obligations due to Allah Almighty, for they drop upon death according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. Thus they said, but there is consideration: if they dropped upon death, there would be no benefit to obligation, and the will would not be obligatory. So the correct view is to say: since the deceased owned it, upon death it becomes the property of the heir, nothing is obligatory on the heir unless he bequeaths, like a bequest of other donations. (Compiled from the commentaries) 'Then his will': with genitive case also, i.e., then execution of his will begins from one third of what remains after preparation and debt, and in most cases except by permission of the heirs, as previously discussed. Then this is not priority over the heirs in meaning; rather they are partners, so that if something is given to him, double or more is given to the heirs. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/513] 'Among his heirs': Know that the heirs are three categories: those of prescribed shares, the agnates (asabat), and the uterine kin (dhawi al-arham). He begins first with the first category, i.e., the prescribed share holders, as the author did when he said: 'They are the prescribed share holders.'
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Fara'id (Inheritance) in Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author first establishes the priority of rights against the estate: (1) Funeral expenses (tajhiz) – shrouding and burial, (2) Payment of debts (dayn), (3) Execution of the will (wasiyyah) from one-third of the remainder, and (4) Distribution among the legal heirs. The commentary then explains the virtue of this science, citing a hadith that it is half of knowledge because it deals with precise shares determined by Allah directly (Quranic verses provide exact fractions), unlike other obligations which are detailed by the Sunnah. The text also includes an important intra-madhhab (Hanafi vs. Shafi'i) dispute regarding obligations owed to Allah (e.g., zakat, kaffarah, fidyah). The Hanafi position (stated as 'عندنا') is that these obligations drop upon death because they are not considered debts in the sense of a human claim; the estate passes to the heirs who are not liable for the deceased's unperformed religious duties. The commentator notes a critique of this view but then supports the Hanafi stance by arguing that since the deceased's ownership transfers to the heir, no obligation falls on the heir unless the deceased bequeathed it. The passage concludes by classifying heirs into three groups: ashab al-furud (fixed-share heirs), asabat (agnatic heirs who take the residue), and dhawi al-arham (uterine kindred who inherit in the absence of the first two).

Key Terms
تركة (tarkah): Property left by the deceased free from any specific rights of others attached to it (except in cases like pawn, etc., where the owner is given priority before shrouding).
تجهيز (tajhiz): The preparation of the deceased for burial, including shrouding, done from the estate without extravagance or stinginess.
دين (dayn): Financial obligations owed to other people (not to Allah), which must be paid from the estate before the will and inheritance.
وصية (wasiyyah): The bequest made by the deceased, executed from one-third of the remaining estate after tajhiz and debts, and subject to heirs' permission if it exceeds one-third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following must be paid from the estate before the will is executed?
A) Unpaid zakat
B) Expiation for a missed fast
C) A loan taken from a friend
D) Fidyah for missed prayers

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi order of estate distribution prioritizes funeral expenses, then human debts, then the will (from one-third), and finally inheritance; religious duties drop at death.

Faraid — Inheritance

Father and Grandfather's Fixed Shares and Their States
Explains the fixed share of father and grandfather and their various inheritance states

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three inheritance states of the father, explain the grandfather's status, and identify the two exceptions where the grandfather differs from the father.

Core Idea
The father and true grandfather (without a female link) each inherit one-sixth with a child, but the grandfather has two exceptions and can be excluded by the father.

In this lesson, we examine the faraid rules for the father and the true grandfather. The father has three distinct states depending on the presence and gender of children. The grandfather, when the father is absent, is treated like the father except in two specific cases involving the mother's share and blocking the maternal grandmother. Understanding these nuances is essential for correct inheritance distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fixed share (fard) of the father
When the deceased leaves a child (including a son's son by consensus), the father receives one-sixth, as per Quran 4:11. This is the first state: fard only.
The child can be male or female; a son's son is also considered a child.
2
Understand the three states of the father
State 1: only fixed share (1/6) when a male child exists. State 2: only agnatic share (ta'sib) when no child exists. State 3: both fixed share and agnatic share when a female child exists (e.g., daughter gets 1/2, father gets 1/6 plus remainder as agnate).
The father never gets a fixed share larger than 1/6; the agnate share varies.
3
Recognize the grandfather's similar treatment
The true grandfather (jadd sahih, no female in lineage) takes the father's place in the father's absence. He gets the same three states as the father, except for two exceptions.
False grandfather (with female link) is a dhawi al-arham and does not inherit like the father.
4
Identify the two exceptions for the grandfather
Exception 1: In the case of radd (return), when the deceased leaves parents and a spouse, the father returns the mother's share from 1/3 of the whole to 1/3 of what remains after the spouse's share; the grandfather does not. Exception 2: The father blocks the paternal grandmother (mother of the father) from inheritance; the grandfather does not block her.
These exceptions prevent complete identity between father and grandfather.
5
Note the fourth state for the grandfather and blocking brothers
The grandfather has a fourth state: exclusion by the father, because the father is closer. Additionally, the grandfather blocks the brothers from inheritance, just as the father would, per Abu Hanifa's view.
This is a branching ruling from the grandfather standing in the father's place.

(عيني، فتح) إن لم يتخلل إلخ كأب أب الميت وهو الجد الصحيح، وإن دخل في نسبته إلى الميت أم فهو فاسد كأب أم الأب، وكأب أب أم الأب، فهو فاسد، وهو من ذوي الأرحام. (عيني)
Then for the father is one-sixth. He began explaining the fixed shares and said: "Then for the father is one-sixth" etc., meaning if a man dies leaving a father, a son, and a son's son, then for the father is one-sixth due to His saying the Exalted: 'And for the parents, for each one of them is one-sixth of what he left if he has a child' (4:11). And a son's son is a child legally by consensus, and his inclusion under 'child' is from the general metaphorical meaning, and it does not combine the literal and metaphorical. Know that for the father in inheritance there are three states: only fixed share, only agnatic share, and fixed share with agnatic share. Because either there is with him a child or a son's son even if below, or not. In the first case, whether that child is male or female, if male then he has the fixed share which is one-sixth, and if female like a daughter or a daughter's daughter then he has one-sixth, the daughter has half, and the remainder goes to the father by agnatic share. If there is no child with him, then he has absolute agnatic share due to His saying the Exalted: 'But if he has no child and his parents inherit from him, then for his mother is one-third' (4:11). He mentioned the mother's fixed share and made the remainder for him, proof that he is an agnate. This is the gist of what is in al-'Ayni and others. Only, the true grandfather, and the grandfather is like the father etc. Meaning that the grandfather in the absence of the father is like the father if no female intervenes in his lineage to the deceased, and this is the true grandfather. So he has one-sixth with a child and a son's son, and the grandfather being like the father is either by general metaphorical meaning or by consensus. (al-'Ayni, al-Fath) 'If no female intervenes' etc., like the father of the father of the deceased, which is the true grandfather. If a female enters his lineage to the deceased, he is false, like the father of the mother of the father, and the father of the father of the mother of the father, so he is false, and he is from the dhawi al-arham. (Mulla Miskeen) 'Except in returning her to one-third of what remains' etc., meaning that the grandfather is like the father except in two matters. One: what he indicated by his saying 'except in returning her to one-third of what remains', meaning if the deceased leaves parents and a wife, for example, then the father returns it from one-third of the whole to one-third of what remains. If the grandfather were in place of the father, she would have the full one-third. The second: what he indicated by his saying 'and the grandfather blocks the mother of the father', meaning that the father blocks her while the grandfather does not. This is the gist of what is in al-'Ayni. So he blocks the brothers: a branching on the grandfather being like the father, i.e., the grandfather blocks the brothers because he stands in his place, and this is according to the absolute statement of Abu Hanifa, as will come if Allah wills. Then the grandfather has the three states mentioned for the father, and he has a fourth state, which is being excluded by the father because he is closer. (al-'Ayni)
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the fixed shares of the father and grandfather. It begins by quoting the matn: 'For the father is one-sixth' and explains that this applies when the deceased leaves a father together with a child or a son's son, citing the Quranic verse from Surah al-Nisa'. The commentator clarifies that a son's son is legally considered a child by consensus, and the father's share is a fixed sixth. The father has three possible states in inheritance: (1) only fixed share (one-sixth) when there is a male child; (2) only agnatic share when there is no child; (3) both fixed share and agnatic share when there is a female child (e.g., daughter gets half, father gets sixth plus remainder). The grandfather, in the absence of the father, is treated like the father except in two matters: (a) the 'return' (radd) of the mother's share: if the deceased leaves parents and a spouse, the father returns the mother's share from one-third of the whole to one-third of what remains after the spouse's share, but the grandfather does not; (b) the grandfather does not block the mother of the father (i.e., the paternal grandmother) while the father does. The grandfather also blocks the brothers, based on Abu Hanifa's view. Like the father, the grandfather has three states, but he has a fourth: exclusion by the father.

Key Terms
الفرض (al-fard): A fixed share in inheritance prescribed by the Quran or Sunnah.
التعصيب (al-ta'sib): Agnatic inheritance, taking the remainder after fixed shares are distributed.
الجد الصحيح (al-jadd al-sahih): The true grandfather, whose lineage to the deceased contains no female.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the three states of the father in inheritance?
A) Fixed share only, Agnatic share only, Fixed share with Agnatic share
B) Sixth only, Half only, Whole
C) Fard only, Sunnah only, Fard with Sunnah
D) Male child, Female child, No child

Key Takeaway
The father's inheritance has three states; the true grandfather is like the father except in two exceptions and is excluded by the father.

Mother's Fixed Shares: The Three Scenarios
Ruling with proof for mother's inheritance shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for the mother's share in Hanafi inheritance and apply the conditions to determine her share.

Core Idea
The mother's share is one-third, one-sixth, or one-third of the remainder — based on children, siblings, and father.

In this passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, the author details the three fixed shares a mother may receive: one-third of the whole estate, one-sixth, or one-third of the remainder after the spouse's share. The ruling is derived from Quran 4:11, with a key difference among the Companions regarding how siblings block her share. Let's explore each scenario systematically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios and their rulings
First, list the three circumstances under which the mother receives a specific share: (1) no child or siblings → one-third of whole; (2) child or two or more siblings → one-sixth; (3) father and one spouse present → one-third of the remainder after spouse's share.
2
Locate the Quranic proofs
The passage cites Quran 4:11 for each scenario. The verse 'fa-in lam yakun lahu walad... fa-li-ummihi al-thuluth' gives one-third when no child. 'fa-in kana lahu ikhwatun fa-li-ummihi al-sudus' gives one-sixth when siblings exist. The parent's share of one-sixth each when there is a child also applies to the mother.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah for each proof
Understand how each verse phrase indicates the ruling. For one-third: the condition 'no child' triggers full third. For one-sixth: the word 'ikhwah' (brothers/siblings) triggers the reduction. For the remainder case: the combination of father and spouse is derived from combining verses and using the principle that father and spouse are present, so the mother's share is taken from the residue.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on the number of siblings
The majority of Companions (jumhur) hold that 'ikhwah' refers to two or more, blocking the mother to one-sixth. Ibn Abbas required three siblings. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf in interpretation.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi school follows the jumhur, as stated in the passage: 'qawl jumhur al-sahaba'. The mufta bihi is that two siblings block the mother to one-sixth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللأم الثلث: وذلك عند عدم الولد وولد الابن؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ وَلَدٌ وَوَرِثَهُ أَبَوَاهُ فَلِأُمِّهِ التَّلْتُ (النساء: ١١)، وعند عدم الاثنين من الإخوة والأخوات على ما نبين الآن (تكملة الإخوة: سواء كانا لأبوين، أو لأب، أو لأم، أو كانا مختلطين ذكورا وإناثا، أو أكثر من جهة واحدة لا أولادهم أي لا أولاد الإخوة والأخوات. السدس: يعني للأم مع واحد من هؤلاء المذكورين السدس؛ لما تلونا من قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِأَبَوَيْهِ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ مِمَّا تَرَكَ إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ وَلَدٌ ولقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ (النساء:١١)، ولفظ الجمع يطلق على الاثنين، فتحجب الأم بهما من الثلث إلى السدس من أي جهة كانا أو من جهتين؛ لأن لفظ الإخوة يطلق على الكل، وهذا قول جمهور الصحابة، وروي عن ابن عباس هما أنه لم تحجب الأم من الثلث إلى السدس إلا بثلاثة عملا بظاهر الآية رمز الحقائق: ٥١٣/٢] ومع الأب إلخ: يعني للأم مع الأب وأحد الزوجين ثلث الباقي بعد أن يخرج نصيب أحد الزوجين مثلا إذا ترك الميت أبا وزوجا وأما يكون للزوج النصف، وللأم ثلث النصف الباقي، وهو سدس الكل، وللأب ما بقي، وإذا ترك أبا وزوجة وأما يكون للزوجة الربع، وللأم ثلث الباقي، وهو ربع الكل، وللأب ما بقي. والحاصل أن للأم ثلاثة أحوال ثلث الكل، وذلك عند عدم الولد أو ولد الابن والعدد من الإخوة والأخوات، وثلث الباقي، وذلك مع الأب وأحد الزوجين، والسدس، وذلك مع الولد أو ولد الابن أو العدد من الإخوة والأخوات فاحفظه.
And for the mother is one-third: that is when there is no child nor child's son, due to His saying the Exalted: 'But if he has no child and his parents inherit from him, then for his mother is one-third' (4:11). And when there are not two of the brothers and sisters, as we will now explain. Completion: brothers, whether they are full, consanguine, or uterine, or mixed males and females, or more from one side, not their children, i.e., not the children of brothers and sisters. One-sixth: meaning for the mother with one of these mentioned is one-sixth, due to what we recited from His saying the Exalted: 'And for the parents, for each one of them is one-sixth of what he left if he has a child' (4:11) and His saying: 'But if he has brothers, then for his mother is one-sixth' (4:11). The plural term applies to two, so the mother is blocked from one-third to one-sixth by them, whether they are from one side or two sides, because the term 'brothers' applies to all. This is the saying of the majority of Companions, and it is narrated from Ibn Abbas that the mother is not blocked from one-third to one-sixth except by three, acting on the apparent meaning of the verse (Ramz al-Haqaiq 2/513). And with the father etc.: meaning for the mother with the father and one of the spouses is one-third of the remainder after extracting the share of one of the spouses. For example, if the deceased leaves a father, a husband, and a mother, then the husband has half, the mother has one-third of the remaining half, which is one-sixth of the whole, and the father takes what remains. If he leaves a father, a wife, and a mother, then the wife has one-quarter, the mother has one-third of the remainder, which is one-quarter of the whole, and the father takes what remains. The summary is that the mother has three states: one-third of the whole when there is no child or child's son and no number of brothers and sisters; one-third of the remainder when with the father and one of the spouses; and one-sixth when with a child or child's son or a number of brothers and sisters. So memorize this.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage explains the mother's fixed share. She receives one-third of the estate when there is no child (or child's son) and no group of brothers/sisters (two or more). She receives one-sixth when there is a child (or child's son) or two or more siblings. The Hanafi position, based on the majority of Companions, is that 'brothers' in the Quran means two or more, blocking the mother from one-third to one-sixth. A narration from Ibn Abbas holds that three siblings are required. The mother also receives one-third of the remainder when inheriting together with the father and one spouse: e.g., with husband and father, the husband takes half, mother takes one-third of the remaining half (one-sixth of total), father takes remainder. With wife, wife takes quarter, mother takes one-third of remaining three-quarters (one-quarter of total), father takes remainder. The commentator summarizes the three states for easy memorization.

Key Terms
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate; the mother's share when no child or siblings exist.
الإخوة (al-ikhwah): Brothers and sisters; the plural term includes two or more and blocks the mother from one-third to one-sixth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does the mother receive one-sixth of the estate?
A) When there is no child and no siblings
B) When there is a child or two or more siblings
C) When with father and spouse
D) When there are exactly two brothers

Key Takeaway
The mother's share is one-third of the whole, one-sixth, or one-third of the remainder, determined by the absence or presence of children, siblings, and the father.

Grandmothers' Inheritance and the Dispute on Dual Relations
Defines valid grandmothers, their fixed sixth, and a dispute on dual relations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify valid grandmothers, apply the condition of equal degree, and state the two positions in the intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing the one-sixth among grandmothers with dual relations.

Core Idea
Only valid grandmothers equal in degree share the one-sixth; Abu Yusuf splits by heads, Muhammad by number of relations.

Inheritance of grandmothers is a nuanced area of Hanafi faraid. Not every grandmother inherits: only those with no false grandfather in their lineage are valid. Even among the valid, if there are multiple, they must be equal in generational distance (mutahadhiyat) to share the fixed one-sixth. The passage then presents an internal Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on how to divide the sixth when one grandmother is related through two different lines (dhat jihhatayn). This lesson unpacks these rules and the practical difference in distribution.

Guided Path
1
1. Distinguish valid from invalid grandmothers
Identify whether a grandmother's lineage to the deceased includes a false grandfather (jad fasid). If yes, she is invalid and does not inherit.
A false grandfather is any male ancestor who is not a true grandfather, e.g., maternal grandfather.
2
2. Classify valid grandmothers into three types
Valid grandmothers are related through purely females, purely males, or a mix of females then males. This classification helps determine generational distance.
The type does not affect the share but affects whether they are equal in degree.
3
3. Check if multiple grandmothers are equal in degree (mutahadhiyat)
Count the number of generations separating each grandmother from the deceased. If all are at the same generational level, they are equal in degree; otherwise, the farther is blocked by the nearer.
Example: mother of mother of mother of mother and mother of mother of father of father are both at the fourth generation, so equal.
4
4. Apply the basic rule
If only one valid grandmother, she gets one-sixth. If multiple valid grandmothers equal in degree, they share one-sixth equally by heads. If not equal, only the nearest inherits.
This is the established rule in the Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
5. Analyze the dispute on dual relations
When a grandmother is related through two lines (e.g., both maternal and paternal), Abu Yusuf says the one-sixth is divided equally by persons. Muhammad (likely) says she receives more, proportional to the number of relations.
The text cuts off but the thamarah al-khilaf is real: different distributions result.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللجدات الخ: اعلم أن الجدة على قسمين: صحيحة ،وفاسدة، فالصحيحة من ليس في نسبتها إلى الميت جد فاسد، والفاسدة من في نسبتها إلى الميت جد فاسد كأم أب الأم، فإن أب الأم جد فاسد، ومن ينتسب إلى الميت بالجد الفاسد يكون فاسدا سواء كان ذكرا أو أنثى، والصحيحة على ثلاثة أقسام: قسم منها من ينتسب إلى الميت بمحض الإناث كأم أم الأم، أو كأم أم أم الأم إلى غير ذلك من الدرجات، وقسم منها من تنتسب بمحض الذكور كأم أب الأب، أو كأم أب أب الأب إلى غير ذلك، وقسم تنتسب بمحض الإناث إلى محض الذكور كأم أم الأب أو كأم أم أب الأب، وإذا علمت هذا فاعلم أن الجدة الصحيحة ترث دون الفاسدة كما بينه المصنف بقوله: "إن لم يتخلل جد فاسد". ثم ا الجدة الصحيحة إن كانت واحدة فلها السدس بلا شرط آخر، وإن كن أكثر من واحدة، فلهن السدس أيضا، لكن بشرط أن يكن متحاذيات متساويات في الدرجة، وهذا الشرط بينه المصنف بقوله: الآتي: "والبعدى تحجب بالقربى" فإذا وجدت أربع جدات وإحداهن أم أم أم الأم والثانية أم أم أم الأب والثالثة أم أم أب الأب، والرابعة: أم أب أب الأب، فهن متحاذيات في الدرجة ، ولهن السدس الواحد، وإن لم يكن كذلك فلسن متحاذيات فتحجب البعدى بالقربى، وطريق معرفة عدد المتحاذيات مذكور في "العيني" وغيره فليرجع إليه. (حبيب الرحمن) وذات جهتين إلخ : أي إذا كانت جدة ذات قرابة واحدة كأم أم الأب والأخرى ذات قرابتين كأم أم الأم، وهي أيضا أم أب الأب يقسم السدس بينهما أنصافا باعتبار الأبدان وهذا عند أبي يوسف، وعند محمد: =
And for grandmothers etc.: Know that the grandmother is of two types: valid and invalid. The valid is one in whose lineage to the deceased there is no false grandfather. The invalid is one in whose lineage to the deceased there is a false grandfather, like the mother of the father of the mother, for the father of the mother is a false grandfather. Whoever is related to the deceased through a false grandfather is invalid, whether male or female. The valid grandmother is of three types: one who is related to the deceased through purely females, like the mother of the mother of the mother, or the mother of the mother of the mother's mother, etc.; one who is related through purely males, like the mother of the father of the father, or the mother of the father of the father's father, etc.; and one who is related through females to males, like the mother of the mother of the father or the mother of the mother of the father's father. When you know this, know that the valid grandmother inherits, not the invalid, as the author explained by his saying: 'if no false grandfather intervenes'. Then, if the valid grandmother is one, she has one-sixth without any other condition. If there are more than one, they also have one-sixth, but on the condition that they are equal in degree (mutahadhiyat). This condition the author explained by his saying: 'And the farther is blocked by the nearer.' So if there are four grandmothers: one is the mother of the mother of the mother of the mother, the second is the mother of the mother of the mother of the father, the third is the mother of the mother of the father of the father, and the fourth is the mother of the father of the father of the father, they are equal in degree and they have the single one-sixth. If they are not like that, they are not equal, so the farther is blocked by the nearer. The method of knowing the number of those equal in degree is mentioned in al-'Ayni and others, so refer to it. (Habib al-Rahman) 'And a woman of two relations etc.': i.e., if there is a grandmother with one relation like the mother of the mother of the father, and another with two relations like the mother of the mother of the mother, who is also the mother of the father of the father, then the one-sixth is divided between them in halves by considering the persons. This is according to Abu Yusuf. And according to Muhammad: =
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage explains the inheritance of grandmothers. Grandmothers are either 'valid' (true) or 'invalid' (false). A valid grandmother has no false grandfather in her lineage; an invalid grandmother does (e.g., mother of the father of the mother). Valid grandmothers are of three types based on lineage: purely female, purely male, or mixed. Only valid grandmothers inherit. If there is only one, she gets one-sixth. If multiple, they share one-sixth, provided they are equal in degree (i.e., same generational distance from the deceased). If not equal, the farther is blocked by the nearer. The passage then mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a grandmother with dual relations (e.g., she is related through two lines). According to Abu Yusuf, the one-sixth is divided between the grandmothers equally by number of persons (heads). According to Muhammad (whose position is cut off), presumably each receives according to the number of relations, but the text is incomplete.

Key Terms
الجدة الصحيحة (al-jaddah al-sahihah): A valid grandmother with no false grandfather in her lineage to the deceased.
متحديات (mutahadhiyat): Grandmothers equal in degree of relationship to the deceased (same generational distance).
ذات جهتين (dhat jihhatayn): A grandmother who is related to the deceased through two different lines (e.g., both paternal and maternal).
جد فاسد (jad fasid): A false grandfather: any male ancestor who is not a true paternal grandfather (e.g., maternal grandfather).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition must multiple grandmothers meet to share the one-sixth?
A) They must be valid grandmothers
B) They must be equal in degree (متحاذيات)
C) They must be from the maternal side
D) They must be from the paternal side

Key Takeaway
Only valid grandmothers equal in degree inherit the fixed one-sixth, and the division among them is subject to an intra-Hanafi dispute when one has dual relations.

The Mother's Three Inheritance Shares
Explanation of mother's three share scenarios with Quranic proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for the mother's share in Hanafi inheritance and apply the correct share to a given set of heirs.

Core Idea
The mother's share varies between 1/3, 1/3 of remainder, and 1/6 depending on children, siblings, or father with spouse.

In this passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, the author explains the three distinct shares a mother can receive in inheritance. These are derived from Quranic verses and the principle of hijab (reduction). Understanding these scenarios is essential for correctly distributing estates in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three cases
The mother can receive 1/3 of the whole, 1/3 of the remainder, or 1/6. List these as the three possible shares.
2
Link each case to its condition
Determine which heirs are present: no children/grandchildren and no siblings → 1/3 of whole; father and one spouse present → 1/3 of remainder; child/grandchild or siblings present → 1/6 of whole.
Siblings must be two or more; a single sibling does not reduce the share.
3
Understand the Quranic proofs
The sixth is established by two verses: one for a child and one for siblings. The plural form 'ikhwa' in Hanafi usul includes two, so two siblings suffice to veil the mother from 1/3 to 1/6.
Dalala is zanni due to linguistic interpretation.
4
Account for the role of siblings
The passage mentions that the majority of Companions held that two siblings veil the mother, contrary to Ibn Abbas's initial view requiring three. The Hanafi school follows the majority.
This is a hijab nuqsan (reduction of share), not total exclusion.
5
Work through the numerical examples
Practice with the examples given: (a) father, husband, mother: husband gets 1/2, mother gets 1/3 of remainder = 1/6 of total, father gets the rest. (b) father, wife, mother: wife gets 1/4, mother gets 1/3 of remainder = 1/4 of total, father gets the rest.
The remainder is after the spouse's share is taken.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السدس: يعني للأم مع واحد من هؤلاء المذكورين السدس؛ لما تلونا من قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِأَبَوَيْهِ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ مِمَّا تَرَكَ إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ وَلَدٌ﴾ ولقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ﴾ (النساء:١١)، ولفظ الجمع يطلق على الاثنين، فتحجب الأم بهما من الثلث إلى السدس من أي جهة كانا أو من جهتين؛ لأن لفظ الإخوة يطلق على الكل، وهذا قول جمهور الصحابة، وروي عن ابن عباس هما أنه لم تحجب الأم من الثلث إلى السدس إلا بثلاثة عملا بظاهر الآية رمز الحقائق: ٥١٣/٢] ومع الأب إلخ: يعني للأم مع الأب وأحد الزوجين ثلث الباقي بعد أن يخرج نصيب أحد الزوجين مثلا إذا ترك الميت أبا وزوجا وأما يكون للزوج النصف، وللأم ثلث النصف الباقي، وهو سدس الكل، وللأب ما بقي، وإذا ترك أبا وزوجة وأما يكون للزوجة الربع، وللأم ثلث الباقي، وهو ربع الكل، وللأب ما بقي. والحاصل أن للأم ثلاثة أحوال ثلث الكل، وذلك عند عدم الولد أو ولد الابن والعدد من الإخوة والأخوات، وثلث الباقي، وذلك مع الأب وأحد الزوجين، والسدس، وذلك مع الولد أو ولد الابن أو العدد من الإخوة والأخوات فاحفظه.
The sixth: meaning for the mother with one of those mentioned [above] is the sixth; because of what we recited from His statement: 'And for his parents, to each one of them is a sixth of what he left if he has a child' and His statement: 'If he has brothers, then for his mother is a sixth' (4:11). And the plural form is applied to two, so the mother is veiled with them from the third to the sixth regardless of whether they are from one side or two sides; because the word 'ikhwa' applies to all. And this is the saying of the majority of the Companions, and it is narrated from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) that he did not veil the mother from the third to the sixth except with three, acting upon the apparent meaning of the verse. [Rami al-Haqa'iq: 513/2] And 'with the father etc.': meaning for the mother with the father and one of the spouses is a third of the remainder after extracting the share of one of the spouses. For example, if the deceased leaves a father, a husband, and a mother, the husband gets half, the mother gets a third of the remaining half, which is a sixth of the whole, and the father gets what remains. And if he leaves a father, a wife, and a mother, the wife gets a quarter, the mother gets a third of the remainder, which is a quarter of the whole, and the father gets what remains. The conclusion is that the mother has three states: a third of the whole, which is when there is no child or child of a son and no number of brothers and sisters; a third of the remainder, which is with the father and one of the spouses; and a sixth, which is with a child or child of a son or a number of brothers and sisters. So memorize it.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage explains the three possible shares of the mother in Hanafi inheritance law, based on Quranic evidence. The author begins by noting that the matn mentions 'السدس' (the sixth) in the context of the mother's share when certain heirs exist. He clarifies that the sixth applies when the deceased leaves a child or siblings (two or more). The Quranic proof is from Surah an-Nisa, verses 11 and 11, which specify the mother's sixth in the presence of a child or siblings. The author then addresses the linguistic point that the plural 'إخوة' can refer to two, so even two siblings veil the mother from the third to the sixth. He mentions that this is the view of the majority of Companions, while Ibn Abbas initially held that three siblings are required but later retracted. Next, the author explains the clause 'مع الأب وأحد الزوجين' (with the father and one of the spouses): when the father is present along with either the husband or wife, the mother gets a third of the remainder after the spouse's share is taken. He illustrates with two numerical examples. Finally, he summarizes the three cases: (1) mother gets 1/3 of the whole when there is no child/grandchild and no siblings; (2) mother gets 1/3 of the remainder when father and one spouse are present; (3) mother gets 1/6 when there is a child/grandchild or siblings. He emphasizes that this is a key principle to memorize.

Key Terms
الحجب (al-hajb): The prevention of an heir from receiving a larger share due to the presence of another heir (here, siblings reduce mother's share from 1/3 to 1/6).
السدس (al-suds): The fixed share of one-sixth given to certain heirs, including the mother under specified conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A deceased woman leaves behind a husband, a father, and a mother. What is the mother's share?
A) 1/3 of the whole
B) 1/6 of the whole
C) 1/3 of the remainder after the husband's share
D) Nothing because she is excluded by the husband

Key Takeaway
Memorize the three cases: mother gets 1/3 (no children/siblings), 1/3 of remainder (father + spouse), or 1/6 (children/siblings).

Share of Grandmothers and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Division
Explanation of grandmother types, share, exclusion rules, and an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify valid and invalid grandmothers in Hanafi inheritance law, state the fard share of grandmothers, and explain the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding division when grandmothers have different lineage connections.

Core Idea
Grandmothers inherit one-sixth, but the division among multiple grandmothers depends on their degree, with an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the number of lineage connections matters.

In Hanafi inheritance law, grandmothers are not all treated equally. The text from Kanz al-Daqaiq distinguishes between valid and invalid grandmothers and then delves into a dispute among the two leading disciples of Abu Hanifa—Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani—on how to divide the fixed share when there are multiple grandmothers with different connections. This lesson unpacks these rules and the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of grandmothers
First, distinguish between a valid grandmother (al-jaddatu al-sahihah) and an invalid one (al-jaddatu al-fasidah). A valid grandmother has no false grandfather in her lineage to the deceased. Only valid grandmothers inherit.
The three subcategories of valid grandmothers (pure female line, pure male line, mixed) are not essential for the dispute but help in identifying equal degree.
2
State the fard share for grandmothers
One valid grandmother receives 1/6 of the estate. If there are multiple valid grandmothers of the same degree (mutahadhiyat), they share that 1/6 equally. If they are not of the same degree, the nearer excludes the farther.
The criterion of equal degree is crucial for determining whether all share or some are excluded.
3
Examine the disputed scenario
Consider two grandmothers: one related through a single line (e.g., mother's mother's father) and another related through two lines (e.g., both mother's mother and father's father). How should the 1/6 be divided?
This is the exact case addressed by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
4
Compare the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Abu Yusuf holds that the division is by heads (by bodies) — each grandmother receives an equal share regardless of the number of lines. Muhammad considers the grandmothers as if they were from one line, meaning they share equally but without any distinction for multiple connections.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) has subtle effects when there are more than two grandmothers or when degrees differ.
5
Note the tarjih and consensus on exclusions
Later Hanafi works typically follow Abu Yusuf's view. Additionally, there is consensus that the mother excludes all grandmothers, and the father excludes paternal grandmothers. The nearer grandmother always excludes the farther, regardless of side.
These exclusion rules are independent of the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللجدات الخ: اعلم أن الجدة على قسمين: صحيحة ،وفاسدة، فالصحيحة من ليس في نسبتها إلى الميت جد فاسد، والفاسدة من في نسبتها إلى الميت جد فاسد كأم أب الأم، فإن أب الأم جد فاسد، ومن ينتسب إلى الميت بالجد الفاسد يكون فاسدا سواء كان ذكرا أو أنثى، والصحيحة على ثلاثة أقسام: قسم منها من ينتسب إلى الميت بمحض الإناث كأم أم الأم، أو كأم أم أم الأم إلى غير ذلك من الدرجات، وقسم منها من تنتسب بمحض الذكور كأم أب الأب، أو كأم أب أب الأب إلى غير ذلك، وقسم تنتسب بمحض الإناث إلى محض الذكور كأم أم الأب أو كأم أم أب الأب، وإذا علمت هذا فاعلم أن الجدة الصحيحة ترث دون الفاسدة كما بينه المصنف بقوله: 'إن لم يتخلل جد فاسد'. ثم ا الجدة الصحيحة إن كانت واحدة فلها السدس بلا شرط آخر، وإن كن أكثر من واحدة، فلهن السدس أيضا، لكن بشرط أن يكن متحاذيات متساويات في الدرجة، وهذا الشرط بينه المصنف بقوله: الآتي: 'والبعدى تحجب بالقربى' فإذا وجدت أربع جدات وإحداهن أم أم أم الأم والثانية أم أم أم الأب والثالثة أم أم أب الأب، والرابعة: أم أب أب الأب، فهن متحاذيات في الدرجة ، ولهن السدس الواحد، وإن لم يكن كذلك فلسن متحاذيات فتحجب البعدى بالقربى، وطريق معرفة عدد المتحاذيات مذكور في 'العيني' وغيره فليرجع إليه. (حبيب الرحمن) وذات جهتين إلخ : أي إذا كانت جدة ذات قرابة واحدة كأم أم الأب والأخرى ذات قرابتين كأم أم الأم، وهي أيضا أم أب الأب يقسم السدس بينهما أنصافا باعتبار الأبدان وهذا عند أبي يوسف، وعند محمد: = كذات جهة، والبعدى تحجب بالقربى، والكل بالأم، وللزوج النصف، ومع الولد أو ولد الابن وإن سفل الربع وللزوجة الربع، ومع الولد أو ولد الابن وإن سفل الثمن، وللبنت النصف، وللأكثر الثلثان . الصلبية الواحدة من البنات أي للزوجة مع الولد أثلاثا باعتبار الجهات مثاله امرأة زوجت بنت بنتها من ابن ابنها، فولد منها ولد، فهذه المزوجة أم أم أم أيضا أم أب أب الولد والجدة الأخرى أم أم أب الولد، فإن تزوج هذا الولد سبطا لها آخر فولد وهي بينهما ولد صارت هذه المرأة جدة لهذا الولد الآخر من ثلاثة أوجه. (ملا مسكين) الولد، جعلوا لها السدس مع الأب، عن جمهور العلماء، والبعدى تحجب إلخ أي البعدى من الجدات تحجب بالقربى منهن مطلقا سواء كانت القربى أو البعدى من جهة الأم أو الأب، وسواء كانت القربى وارثة كأم الأب مع أم أم الأم : عند عدم الأب، أو محجوبة بالأب عند وجوده، وفي رواية عن ابن مسعود مه لا تحجب الجدات إلا الأم، وفي رواية عنه وعن زيد بن ثابت : أن القربي إذا كانت من جهة الأب لا تحجب البعدى من جهة الأم، وبالعكس تحجب. (رد المحتار، عيني) والكل بالأم: أي كل الجدات يحجب بالأم إذا كانت وارثة وعليه الإجماع، وكذا الأبويات منهن يحجبن ذلك بالأب إذا كان وارثا، روي أخذ عثمان وعلى والزبير وسعد وزيد بن ثابت، وبه وروي عن عمر وابن مسعود وعمران ابن الحصين وأبي موسى الأشعري وأبي الطفيل عامر بن واثلة له أنهم وبه أخذ طائفة من أهل العلم من التابعين وغيرهم. [رمز الحقائق: ٥١٥/٢]
And regarding grandmothers: Know that a grandmother is of two types: correct (sahiha) and defective (fasida). The correct one is the one in whose lineage to the deceased there is no defective grandfather. The defective one is the one in whose lineage to the deceased there is a defective grandfather, like the mother of the father's mother, for the father's mother's father is a defective grandfather. And whoever is related to the deceased through a defective grandfather is defective, whether male or female. The correct grandmother is of three types: one who is related through pure females, like the mother of the mother's mother, or the mother of the mother's mother's mother, and so on; one who is related through pure males, like the mother of the father's father, or the mother of the father's father's father, and so on; and one who is related through females to males, like the mother of the mother's father, or the mother of the mother of the father's father. When you know this, know that the correct grandmother inherits, not the defective one, as the author clarifies by his saying: 'if no defective grandfather intervenes'. Then, if there is one correct grandmother, she gets one-sixth without any other condition. If there are more than one, they also get one-sixth, but on condition that they are equal in degree. The author clarifies this condition by his later saying: 'and the farther one is veiled by the nearer one'. So if there are four grandmothers, one of them is the mother of the mother's mother's mother, the second is the mother of the mother's mother's father, the third is the mother of the mother's father's father, and the fourth is the mother of the father's father's father, they are equal in degree, and they share one-sixth. If not, they are not equal, so the farther is veiled by the nearer. The method of knowing the number of those equal in degree is mentioned in al-Ayni and others, so refer to it. (Habib al-Rahman) And 'having two lines' etc.: that is, if one grandmother is related through one line, like the mother of the mother's father, and the other is related through two lines, like the mother of the mother's mother, who is also the mother of the father's father, the one-sixth is divided between them in halves by consideration of bodies (heads) according to Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, it is like one line. And the farther is veiled by the nearer, and all are veiled by the mother. And for the husband is half, and with a child or a child of a son however low, a quarter. And for the wife is a quarter, and with a child or a child of a son however low, an eighth. And for the daughter is half, and for two or more, two-thirds. The one pure daughter of the daughters, i.e., for the wife with a child, thirds in consideration of lines. Example: A woman married her daughter's daughter to her son's son, and a child was born. This woman becomes the mother of the mother's mother and also the mother of the father's father of the child, and the other grandmother is the mother of the mother's father. Then if this child marries another grandchild of hers and a child is born, she becomes a grandmother of this other child from three lines. (Mulla Miskin) The child, they gave her one-sixth with the father, according to the majority of scholars. And 'the farther is veiled by the nearer': meaning the farther of the grandmothers is veiled by the nearer among them absolutely, whether the nearer or farther is from the mother's side or father's side, and whether the nearer is an heir, like the mother's father with the mother's mother's mother, in the absence of the father, or is veiled by the father when he is present. There is a narration from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that only the mother veils grandmothers. And a narration from him and Zaid ibn Thabit that if the nearer is from the father's side, it does not veil the farther from the mother's side, but the reverse does. (Radd al-Muhtar, Ayni) And 'all are veiled by the mother': meaning all grandmothers are veiled by the mother if she is an heir, and upon this is consensus. Likewise, the paternal ones are veiled by the father if he is an heir. It is reported that Uthman, Ali, al-Zubair, Sa'd, and Zaid ibn Thabit took this, and it is also reported from Umar, Ibn Mas'ud, Imran ibn al-Husain, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Abu al-Tufail Amir ibn Wathila (may Allah be pleased with them) that they took this, and a group of scholars from the Tabi'un and others took it. [Rami al-Haqa'iq: 515/2]
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed explanation of the inheritance of grandmothers. The author first defines two categories: valid (sahiha) and invalid (fasida) grandmothers based on the presence of a false grandfather. Only valid grandmothers inherit. Valid grandmothers are further divided into three types based on how they are related to the deceased. The share for one valid grandmother is one-sixth, and if there are multiple valid grandmothers of the same degree, they divide that one-sixth equally. The condition of equal degree is highlighted: if some are closer, the farther ones are excluded. The author then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: when a grandmother is related through one line and another through two lines, Abu Yusuf divides the sixth by heads (equally), while Muhammad treats them as if they were from one line (the same degree). The text then clarifies that the nearer grandmother excludes the farther, regardless of side, and that the mother excludes all grandmothers. Similarly, the father excludes paternal grandmothers. The passage concludes with a reference to consensus and reports from several Companions supporting these rules.

Key Terms
الجدة الصحيحة (al-jaddatu al-sahihah): A grandmother whose lineage to the deceased does not include a false grandfather (e.g., not through the father's mother's father).
متحاذيات (mutahadhiyat): Grandmothers who are of the same degree (equal in closeness) in the family tree.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later relied-upon Hanafi view, how is the 1/6 share divided when there are two valid grandmothers of equal degree, one with a single lineage and one with a double lineage?
A) The grandmother with double lineage gets 2/3 of the 1/6 (1/9), the other gets 1/3 of the 1/6 (1/18).
B) They each get 1/12 of the estate (equal division by heads).
C) Only the grandmother with double lineage inherits; the other is excluded.
D) The 1/6 is given to the closest grandmother based on the number of lines.

Key Takeaway
Valid grandmothers inherit one-sixth, shared equally if of equal degree, but when one grandmother has multiple lineage connections, Abu Yusuf divides by heads while Muhammad treats all as equal, with later practice following Abu Yusuf.

Share of the Husband in Inheritance
Ruling with Quranic proof for husband's share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the husband's share in inheritance based on the presence or absence of a child or grandchild, and apply the rule that the term 'child' includes descendants through sons.

Core Idea
Husband inherits half if no child/grandchild, quarter if any child or grandchild exists.

In Hanafi inheritance law, the husband's share is a fixed Quranic portion. The verse 4:12 explicitly sets his share based on whether the deceased wife left any child. But what counts as a 'child'? This passage clarifies that grandchildren through sons are included, and that the child need not be from the husband himself. We will explore the two scenarios and the Quranic proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible shares
State the husband's share: half when no child or child of a son (however low), and quarter when any such child exists.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof
Read the verse (4:12) and note the conditional structure: 'if they have no child, half; if they have a child, quarter.' Recognize that the term 'walad' in the verse includes grandchildren through sons, by text or consensus.
The word 'walad' is general and includes descendants through sons.
3
Apply to the multiple husbands scenario
If two or more men each prove marriage to the deceased (without cohabitation or consummation), they collectively receive the share of one husband and divide it equally.
This is based on lack of precedence among claimants.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللزوج النصف : أي للزوج حالتان النصف إذا لم يكن معه الولد أو ولد الابن وإن سفل، والربع إذا كان معه أحدهما؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَكُمْ نِصْفُ مَا تَرَكَ أَزْوَاجُكُمْ إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُنَّ وَلَدٌ فَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُنَّ وَلَدٌ فَلَكُمُ الرُّبُعُ مِمَّا تَرَكْنَ﴾ (النساء:۱۲) فيستحق كل زوج إما النصف وإما الربع، ولفظ الولد يتناول ولد الابن، فيكون مثله بالنص، أو بالإجماع على بينا من قبل، والولد أعم من أن يكون من الزوج الوارث أو من غيره، أو لا يعرف له أب كولد اللعان وغيره والزوج الواحد والجماعة في استحقاق سهم الأزواج سواء حتى لو ادعى رجلان فأكثر نكاح ميتة وبرهنا ولم تكن في بيت واحد منهما، ولا دخل بها، فإنهم يقسمون ميراث زوج واحد؛ لعدم الأولوية، هذا حاصل ما في 'العيني' و'التكملة' و'رد المحتار'.
And for the husband is half: meaning the husband has two states: half when there is no child or child of a son, however low, and a quarter when one of them is present. Because of His statement: 'And for you is half of what your wives leave if they have no child. But if they have a child, then for you is a quarter of what they leave' (4:12). So every husband is entitled to either half or a quarter. And the word 'child' includes the child of a son, so it is like it by text or by consensus as we have explained before. And 'child' is general, whether from the inheriting husband or from another, or whose father is unknown, like the child of li'an, etc. The one husband and a group [of husbands] are equal in entitlement to the share of husbands. So much so that if two or more men claim marriage to a deceased woman and provide proof, and she was not in the same house with either of them, and there was no consummation, they divide the inheritance of one husband; because there is no precedence. This is the gist of what is in al-Ayni, al-Takmila, and Radd al-Muhtar.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage explains the husband's inheritance. The husband is entitled to either half or a quarter of his wife's estate depending on whether she had any child or grandchild. The primary proof is the Quranic verse 4:12. The author clarifies that the term 'child' includes grandchildren through sons (even if low), and that the child need not be from the husband himself. He also discusses the scenario where multiple men claim to be the husband: they are treated as one husband and divide the husband's share equally among themselves, as none has precedence.

Key Terms
ولد الابن (waladu al-ibn): Child of a son, i.e., grandson or granddaughter, who counts as a child for veiling purposes.
ولد اللعان (waladu al-li'an): Child born from li'an (imprecation), whose paternity is disowned; such a child is still considered a child of the mother for inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman dies leaving her husband and a grandson (son's son). What is the husband's share?
A) 1/2
B) 1/4
C) 1/8
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The husband inherits half if the wife has no child or grandchild, and a quarter if any descendant through sons exists, with the child defined broadly.

Share of Daughters in Inheritance
Determination of the share of daughters based on number

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic share of one daughter and of two or more daughters, and explain the consensus among Companions on the two-thirds share.

Core Idea
One daughter inherits half; two or more inherit two-thirds — a fixed Quranic ruling.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the fundamental rule for daughters' inheritance. The Quran explicitly gives half to an only daughter, and the unanimous understanding of the Companions establishes two-thirds for multiple daughters. We also examine an early difference from Ibn Abbas and his subsequent retraction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two cases: a single daughter and two or more daughters. Note the share for each: half for one, two-thirds for multiple.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Find the verse (4:11) cited in the text. The explicit phrase 'and if there is one, for her is half' directly proves the share for one daughter.
The verse also implies two-thirds for multiple daughters, as understood by the Companions.
3
Understand the derivation for two or more
The two-thirds share is derived from the context of the verse and the consensus (ijma) of the Companions. The text notes that Ibn Abbas initially disagreed but later retracted, confirming the consensus.
The Hanafi school relies on the consensus after the retraction.
4
Examine the difference and resolution
Ibn Abbas held that two daughters get half based on a literal reading. The text states that he later agreed with the majority, establishing the two-thirds share.
This shows that early differences were resolved through scholarly discussion.
5
Apply the rule
When faced with an inheritance case involving only daughters, identify the number and apply the corresponding share: half if one, two-thirds if two or more, divided equally among them.
This rule applies when there are no sons; with sons, the distribution changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللبنت النصف أي للبنت الواحدة النصف؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ كَانَتْ وَاحِدَةً فَلَهَا النِّصْفُ﴾ (النساء: ۱۱) قوله: 'وللأكثر الثلثان' أي للأكثر من البنات الثلثان، وهو قول عامة الصحابة، وبه أخذ علماء الأمصار ، وروي عن ابن عباس هما أنه جعل حكم الثنتين منهن حكم الواحدة فجعل لهما النصف بظاهر النص، وقد صح رجوع ابن عباس الله لهما إلى موافقة الصحابة. (تكملة، عيني، فتح)
And for the daughter is half: meaning for one daughter is half; because of His statement: 'And if there is one, then for her is half' (4:11). His saying: 'and for two or more, two-thirds': meaning for more than one daughter, two-thirds. This is the saying of the generality of the Companions, and scholars of the cities took it. It is narrated from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) that he made the ruling of two daughters like the ruling of one, making half for them by the apparent text, but it is established that Ibn Abbas returned to the agreement of the Companions. (Takmila, Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage explains the share of daughters. A single daughter receives half of the estate. If there are two or more daughters, they collectively receive two-thirds, which they divide equally. The proof is from Surah an-Nisa 4:11. The author notes that Ibn Abbas initially thought two daughters should get half (like one), but he later retracted and agreed with the majority of Companions that two or more get two-thirds.

Key Terms
الأكثر من البنات (al-akthar min al-banat): Two or more daughters; the text uses 'two or more' as the threshold for the two-thirds share.

Key Takeaway

Blocking of Grandmothers: Near Over Remote and Mother Over All
Explanation of grandmother inheritance blocking rules with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and ijma proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for blocking grandmothers in inheritance, apply it to determine which grandmothers inherit given the presence of the mother or nearer grandmothers, and explain the evidence of ijma supporting the rule.

Core Idea
A nearer grandmother always blocks a more remote one, and the mother blocks all grandmothers.

Inheritance among female ancestors can be complex, especially with multiple grandmothers from paternal and maternal lines. The Hanafi school provides clear rules: the nearer grandmother in lineage excludes the more remote, and the mother excludes all grandmothers if she is an heir. This lesson unpacks these rules, the intra-Hanafi differences, and the consensus (ijma) that supports the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of grandmothers
Recognize that grandmothers come from two directions: paternal (e.g., father's mother) and maternal (e.g., mother's mother). The passage refers to them as 'ذات جهة' (possessing direction).
2
Apply the near-blocks-remote rule
Determine which grandmother is nearer in lineage to the deceased; the nearer grandmother excludes the more remote one, regardless of which side (paternal or maternal) they come from.
This absolute blocking is the Hanafi view; other schools may differentiate.
3
Apply the mother-blocks-all rule
If the mother is alive and entitled to inherit (i.e., not blocked by the father in some cases), she excludes ALL grandmothers, both paternal and maternal.
The phrase 'والكل بالأم' encapsulates this.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note the differing narrations: Ibn Mas'ud held that only the mother blocks grandmothers; another narration from him and Zayd ibn Thabit distinguishes between paternal and maternal lines. Understand why the majority view (absolute blocking) is preferred.
The majority of Companions and later Hanafi authorities adopt the absolute view.
5
Understand the evidence of ijma
The commentator states there is consensus (ijma) on the mother blocking all grandmothers. Recognize how this ijma strengthens the ruling, even though the specific details of near/remote blocking are from practice of Companions.
Ijma is a primary source of law; here it is used to confirm the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كذات جهة، والبعدى تحجب بالقربى، والكل بالأم. والبعدى تحجب إلخ أي البعدى من الجدات تحجب بالقربى منهن مطلقا سواء كانت القربى أو البعدى من جهة الأم أو الأب، وسواء كانت القربى وارثة كأم الأب مع أم أم الأم : عند عدم الأب، أو محجوبة بالأب عند وجوده، وفي رواية عن ابن مسعود مه لا تحجب الجدات إلا الأم، وفي رواية عنه وعن زيد بن ثابت : أن القربي إذا كانت من جهة الأب لا تحجب البعدى من جهة الأم، وبالعكس تحجب. (رد المحتار، عيني) والكل بالأم: أي كل الجدات يحجب بالأم إذا كانت وارثة وعليه الإجماع، وكذا الأبويات منهن يحجبن ذلك بالأب إذا كان وارثا، روي أخذ عثمان وعلى والزبير وسعد وزيد بن ثابت ، وبه وروي عن عمر وابن مسعود وعمران ابن الحصين وأبي موسى الأشعري وأبي الطفيل عامر بن واثلة له أنهم وبه أخذ طائفة من أهل العلم من التابعين وغيرهم. [رمز الحقائق: ٥١٥/٢]
Like multiple directions, and the remote is blocked by the near, and all by the mother. The remote is blocked: meaning the remote grandmothers are blocked by the near absolutely, whether the near or remote are on the mother's side or father's side, and whether the near is an heir like mother's mother with father's mother when father is absent, or blocked by the father when he exists. In a narration from Ibn Mas'ud, grandmothers are not blocked except by the mother. In another narration from him and Zayd ibn Thabit, if the near is on the father's side, it does not block the remote on the mother's side, and vice versa it blocks. (Radd al-Muhtar, 'Ayni) And all by the mother: meaning all grandmothers are blocked by the mother if she is an heir, and there is consensus on this. Likewise, those from the father's side are blocked by the father if he is an heir. It is narrated that Uthman, Ali, al-Zubayr, Sa'd, and Zayd ibn Thabit took this, and it was also taken by a group of the people of knowledge among the Tabi'un and others.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about grandmothers in inheritance. The matn states that grandmothers are considered by their direction (maternal or paternal), and the more remote grandmother is blocked by the nearer grandmother, and all grandmothers are blocked by the mother. The commentator clarifies that this blocking is absolute: a nearer grandmother, whether from mother's side or father's side, blocks the more remote, regardless of whether the nearer is actually inheriting or is herself blocked by the father. There is an ikhtilaf: Ibn Mas'ud reported that only the mother blocks grandmothers, while another report from him and Zayd ibn Thabit says that a near grandmother from the father's side does not block a remote from the mother's side, but the opposite does block. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the first one: all grandmothers are blocked by the mother if she is an heir, and those from the father's side are also blocked by the father if he is an heir. This is supported by consensus and practice of the Companions.

Key Terms
البعدى تحجب بالقربى (al-bu'da tuhjabu bi al-qurba): The more remote female ancestor (grandmother) is excluded from inheritance by the nearer one.
الكل بالأم (al-kullu bi al-umm): All grandmothers are blocked (excluded) by the mother if she is alive and entitled to inherit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, who blocks all grandmothers?
A) The father
B) The mother
C) The grandfather
D) The son

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi inheritance, a nearer grandmother blocks a more remote one absolutely, and the mother blocks all grandmothers, a ruling supported by ijma and the practice of the Companions.

Husband's Share in Inheritance
States the husband's share and clarifies the definition of 'walad'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the husband's two fixed shares (half and quarter) in inheritance and apply the rule to scenarios involving children, grandchildren, and multiple husbands.

Core Idea
A husband inherits either half or quarter of his wife's estate, depending on whether she has a child.

The husband's share in inheritance is straightforward: half if the wife has no child, and quarter if she does. But what counts as a child? The Hanafi school includes grandchildren and even children from previous marriages. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its Quranic proof, and a surprising scenario where multiple husbands share one share.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two states of the husband's share
The matn states half and quarter. The key condition is the presence or absence of a child (including grandchildren).
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Surah al-Nisa 4:12 explicitly divides the husband's share into half and quarter based on whether the wife has a child. The proof is qat'i in both transmission and meaning.
3
Understand the inclusive definition of 'walad'
The commentator explains that 'walad' includes grandchildren (children of the son) and children from any father, even illegitimate children like those from li'an. This is based on consensus.
4
Apply to multiple husbands scenario
If multiple men prove marriage to the same woman with no priority, they divide the single husband's share equally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللزوج النصف : أي للزوج حالتان النصف إذا لم يكن معه الولد أو ولد الابن وإن سفل، والربع إذا كان معه أحدهما؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَكُمْ نِصْفُ مَا تَرَكَ أَزْوَاجُكُمْ إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُنَّ وَلَدٌ فَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُنَّ وَلَدٌ فَلَكُمُ الرُّبُعُ مِمَّا تَرَكْنَ (النساء:۱۲) فيستحق كل زوج إما النصف وإما الربع، ولفظ الولد يتناول ولد الابن، فيكون مثله بالنص، أو بالإجماع على بينا من قبل، والولد أعم من أن يكون من الزوج الوارث أو من غيره، أو لا يعرف له أب كولد اللعان وغيره والزوج الواحد والجماعة في استحقاق سهم الأزواج سواء حتى لو ادعى رجلان فأكثر نكاح ميتة وبرهنا ولم تكن في بيت واحد منهما، ولا دخل بها، فإنهم يقسمون ميراث زوج واحد؛ لعدم الأولوية، هذا حاصل ما في "العيني" و"التكملة" و"رد المحتار".
And for the husband is half: meaning the husband has two states: half if there is no child or child of the son even if descending, and quarter if there is one of them; due to His statement: 'And for you is half of what your wives leave if they have no child. But if they have a child, then for you is a quarter of what they leave.' (4:12). So each husband deserves either half or quarter. The word 'walad' includes the child of the son, so it is like him by text or by consensus as previously clarified. 'Walad' is general, whether from the inheriting husband or from someone else, or has no known father like the child of li'an or others. The single husband and multiple husbands are equal in entitlement to the share of husbands, so if two or more men claim marriage to a deceased woman and prove it, and she was not in one house with any of them, nor had intercourse, then they divide the inheritance of one husband due to lack of priority. This is the summary of what is in al-'Ayni, al-Takmila, and Radd al-Muhtar.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the husband's share. The matn states: 'And for the husband is half, and with a child or son's child (even if descending) a quarter.' The commentator explains that the husband has only two possible shares: half when there is no child (including grandchildren) and quarter when there is a child. The proof is from Quran 4:12, which explicitly mentions these two scenarios. The term 'walad' (child) includes grandchildren (children of the son) by consensus, even if they are lower in lineage. The ruling applies whether the child is from the husband himself or from another man, and even if the child is illegitimate (like from li'an). Furthermore, if multiple men all prove they were married to the deceased, and none had priority (e.g., no exclusive residence or consummation), they share the share of one husband equally. This is the Hanafi position based on the text and the commentaries of al-'Ayni, al-Takmila, and Radd al-Muhtar.

Key Terms
ولد الابن وإن سفل (walad al-ibn wa in safala): Child of the son, even if descending to lower generations (i.e., grandson, great-grandson, etc.)
ولد اللعان (walad al-li'an): A child born from a marriage that was dissolved by li'an (mutual imprecation), who inherits from the mother but not from the father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman dies leaving a husband and a son from a previous marriage, what is the husband's share?
A) Half
B) Quarter
C) Eighth
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The husband's share in inheritance is fixed by Quran: half if no child, quarter if any child exists, including grandchildren and children from any father.

The Wife's Share in Inheritance: Quarter or Eighth
States the wife's share with proof from Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wife's share in Hanafi inheritance law and apply the rule to scenarios with and without children.

Core Idea
The wife's share is halved when children are present — from a quarter to an eighth.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational faraid ruling: the share of the wife (or wives) in the husband's estate. The matn and commentary from Al-Hidayah clarify the two possible fractions: a quarter when there is no child, and an eighth when there is a child (including a son's descendant). The ruling is directly from the Quran, so it is wajib and undisputed within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the distribution of the wife's share from the husband's estate. The ruling states two possible fractions: a quarter or an eighth, depending on the presence of children.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 4:12, which explicitly mentions the quarter and eighth for wives.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut (certain transmission) and qat'i al-dalalah (clear meaning).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse directly states: 'And for them is a quarter... if you have no child... if you have a child, then for them is an eighth.' The condition is clearly the presence or absence of a child.
The child includes both sons and daughters, and their descendants (e.g., grandchildren through a son).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no ikhtilaf among the Hanafi school or with other major schools on this ruling; it is muttafaq alayh.
However, there is a nuance regarding the definition of 'child' for the purpose of reducing the share.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario, determine which fraction applies based on the presence of any child (including a son's son).
Multiple wives share the designated fraction equally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللزوجة الربع: أي للزوجة مطلقا، سواء كانت واحدة أو أكثر حالتان الربع إذا لم يكن معها الولد أو ولد الابن وإن سفل، والثمن إن كان معها أحدهما؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَهُنَّ الرُّبُعُ مِمَّا تَرَكْتُمْ إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَكُمْ وَلَدٌ فَإِنْ كَانَ لَكُمْ وَلَدٌ فَلَهُنَّ الثُّمُنُ مِمَّا تَرَكْتُمْ (النساء:۱۲) (ملا مسكين تكملة
And for the wife is a quarter: meaning for the wife in absolute terms, whether one or more, two states: a quarter if there is no child or child of the son even if descending, and an eighth if there is one of them; due to His statement: 'And for them (women) is a quarter of what you leave if you have no child. But if you have a child, then for them is an eighth of what you leave.' (4:12) (Mulla Miskin, Takmilah)
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the wife's share. The matn says: 'And for the wife is a quarter, and with a child or son's child, an eighth.' The commentator explains that the wife (or wives) has two possible shares: a quarter when there is no child (including grandchildren) and an eighth when there is a child. The proof is from the Quranic verse (4:12), which explicitly states these fractions. The ruling is the same whether there is one wife or multiple wives; they share the allotted fraction equally among themselves. This is the standard Hanafi position, directly from the text.

Key Terms
الزوجة (al-zawjah): Wife; the text specifies that the share applies to all wives collectively, not per wife.

Daughter's Share: One Gets Half, More Get Two-Thirds
States the shares of daughters: half for one, two-thirds for two or more

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the share of daughters in Hanafi inheritance law and cite the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
A single daughter inherits half; two or more share two-thirds — a Quranic fixed share.

In this lesson, we examine the shares of daughters in inheritance as established by the Quran and consensus. The Hanafi school, following the majority of Companions, rules that one daughter receives half the estate, while two or more daughters collectively receive two-thirds, divided equally among them. We will explore the textual evidence and note the historical agreement on this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their shares
State the ruling for a single daughter (half) and for two or more daughters (two-thirds collectively).
The term 'al-akthar' means two or more.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the Quranic verse (4:11) that explicitly gives half to a single daughter.
The verse is cited in the matn.
3
Understand the derivation for two-thirds
Recognize that the two-thirds for multiple daughters is not explicitly in the verse but is derived from the same verse and supported by consensus of the Companions.
The commentator mentions ijma as the basis.
4
Note the historical objection
Acknowledge that Ibn Abbas initially gave half to two daughters as well, but he later retracted and agreed with the majority.
This shows the strength of the consensus.
5
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school follows the majority view that two or more daughters share two-thirds. This is the mufta bihi.
There is no intra-Hanafi dispute.
