6 min
Inheritance of Children of the Son (Grandchildren) in Hanafi Faraid
Faraid: inheritance rules for grandchildren through son

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the shares of grandchildren when the son is absent, applying the Hanafi rules of blocking and the completion of two-thirds.

Core Idea
Grandchildren step into the shoes of children when the son is absent, but are blocked by a living son or two daughters.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq expands on the inheritance rights of grandchildren through a son. The matn provides concise rules: the son blocks his own children, and granddaughters receive one-sixth only when a single full daughter exists. The commentator clarifies the conditions under which granddaughters are blocked or become 'asaba with a grandson. Understanding these rules is essential for accurate faraid calculations involving multiple generations of descendants.

Guided Path
1
Identify the presence of a son or daughters
First, check if a son is alive: the son blocks his own children entirely. Next, check the number of full daughters: two full daughters block granddaughters unless a grandson exists.
The blocking rule for granddaughters by two daughters is specific to the Hanafi school.
2
Determine the share of granddaughters when one daughter exists
If there is one full daughter and no grandson, granddaughters receive one-sixth to complete the two-thirds share. The one-sixth is takmilatan li al-thuluthayn.
If there is no full daughter, granddaughters take the place of daughters, receiving half for one, two-thirds for two or more.
3
Apply the 'asabah rule with a grandson
If a grandson of the same or lower level is present, granddaughters become 'asaba with him and lose the fixed one-sixth share. They inherit via 'asabah, with the male taking double the female.
The presence of a grandson changes the category from fixed-share to residuary.
4
Apply the principle of descending levels among granddaughters
When there are granddaughters from multiple sons at different levels, the closest in lineage takes the place of a full daughter, the next takes the place of a granddaughter, and so on.
This ensures that inheritance follows the nearer block of descendants.
5
Apply blocking by two full daughters
Two full daughters complete the two-thirds share, so granddaughters are blocked entirely unless a grandson is present to make them 'asaba. If a grandson exists, they inherit through him.
If there is only one full daughter, granddaughters are not blocked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعصبها الابن وله مثل حظهما، وولد الابن كولده عند عدمه ويحجب بالابن، ومع البنت لأقرب الذكور الباقي، وللإناث السدس تكملة للثلثين، وحجبن ببنتين الصلبية إلا أن يكون معهن أو أسفل منهن ذكر. ولا يرثون معه أي ولا يرث بنات الابن مع ابن الابن إذا كان في درجته أو أسفل، بل يعصبهن. وأما إذا كان معهن ابن ابن في درجته يكن عصبة معه فلا يرثن السدس، وإنما كان لهن السدس عند انفرادهن. (فتح، تكملة) وحجبن ببنتين: أي يحجب بنات الابن ببنتين صلبيتين؛ لأن إرثهن كان تكملة للثلثين، وقد كمل ببنتين فسقط؛ إذ لا سبيل لتوريثهن فرضا وتعصيبا تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٤٦/٩] إلا أن يكون إلخ: أي تحجب بنات الابن ببنتين صلبيتين إلا إذا كان معهن في درجتهن أو أسفل منهن ذكر، سواء كان أخا لهن أو لم يكن، فحينئذ كانت فوقه ممن لم يكن ذات سهم، ويسقط أي الذكر الإناث، ومن من يعصب ذلك الذكر من كانت بحذائه من دونه، ثم الأصل في بنات الابن عند عدم بنات الصلب أن أقربهن إلى الميت ينزل منزلة البنت الصلبية، والتي تليها في القرب منزلة بنات الابن وهكذا وإن سفلن مثاله لو ترك ثلاث بنات الابن بعضهن أسفل من بعض، وثلاث بنات ابن ابن آخر بعضهن أسفل من بعض، وثلاث بنات ابن ابن ابن آخر بعضهن أسفل من بعض، -
And the son makes them ('asabah) and he has a portion like that of two females. And the son's child is like his child in his absence, and he is blocked by the son. And with a (full) daughter, the remainder goes to the nearest male descendant. And for the females (granddaughters) is one-sixth as completion of the two-thirds. And they are blocked by two full daughters unless there is with them or below them a male. And they (granddaughters) do not inherit with him (i.e., with a grandson) [commentary: they are made 'asabah by him]. When the grandson is of the same level or below, he makes them 'asabah and they do not inherit the sixth; the sixth is only when they are alone. And they are blocked by two full daughters because their inheritance was a completion of two-thirds, and it has been completed by two daughters, so it falls. Unless there is with them a male of the same level or below, whether her brother or not, then the male drops the females. Then the principle for granddaughters in the absence of full daughters is that the nearest to the deceased takes the place of a full daughter, and the next in closeness takes the place of granddaughters, and so on even if lower. Example: If one leaves three granddaughters some lower than others, and three daughters of another son's son some lower than others, and three daughters of another son's son's son some lower than others.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings about the inheritance of children of the son (grandchildren). The matn states: 'The son makes them 'asabah and he has double the share. The child of the son is like the child in his absence and is blocked by the son. With a sole daughter, the remainder goes to the nearest male. For the females (granddaughters) is one-sixth as completion of two-thirds. They are blocked by two full daughters unless with them is a male.' The commentator elaborates: When a son is present, the son's children are blocked entirely. When the son is absent, the son's sons take the role of sons (as 'asaba), and the son's daughters take the role of daughters (as fixed-share heirs). A single granddaughter gets half, two or more get two-thirds. However, if there is a full daughter, the granddaughters may get one-sixth to complete two-thirds for the daughters (full daughter gets half, granddaughters get one-sixth to reach two-thirds total). This is provided there is no grandson with them; if there is a grandson of the same level or below, they become 'asaba with him, dropping the sixth. The granddaughters are blocked by two full daughters because the two-thirds is complete without them, unless there is a grandson to make them 'asaba. The commentator gives an example involving multiple classes of granddaughters to illustrate the application of these rules.

Key Terms
ولد الابن (walad al-ibn): Children of the son (both male and female), i.e., grandchildren
عصبها الابن (asabaha al-ibn): The son makes them (the daughters) 'asaba, meaning the daughters are turned into residuary heirs through the son, so the son takes double.
تكملة للثلثين (takmilatan li al-thuluthayn): The one-sixth given to granddaughters is to complete the two-thirds share (that daughters are entitled to as a group).
حجبن ببنتين (hujibna bi-bintayn): Granddaughters are blocked (prevented from inheriting) by two full daughters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man dies leaving one full daughter and two granddaughters (son's daughters), what do the granddaughters inherit?
A) Half
B) One-sixth
C) Nothing
D) Two-thirds

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, granddaughters inherit one-sixth to complete two-thirds when one full daughter exists, but are blocked by two daughters unless a grandson of the same or lower level is present to make them 'asaba.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
12 min
Inheritance Rules for Grandchildren (Awlad al-Ibn)
Commentary on faraid rules for grandchildren

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for inheritance of grandchildren and apply them to determine the shares of granddaughters in various scenarios.

Core Idea
Grandchildren inherit like children in the absence of the son, but granddaughters are blocked by two daughters unless a male grandchild makes them agnates.

This lesson explains the Hanafi faraid rules for grandchildren (awlād al-ibn), based on a detailed commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. You will learn how granddaughters receive fixed shares similar to daughters, how they are affected by the presence of a son or daughters of the deceased, and how a male grandchild can convert their inheritance from fixed shares to agnatic residue (ta'sib). These rules are grounded in consensus and analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Recall the basic rule for grandchildren
Understand that the children of a son (grandchildren) are treated like the children of the deceased when the deceased has no living son. This includes both sons and daughters of the son.
This is a well-established Hanafi principle, supported by consensus.
2
Identify the fixed shares for granddaughters
For granddaughters alone (no son or daughter of the deceased): one granddaughter gets 1/2; two or more get 2/3. This mirrors the shares of daughters.
In Hanafi faraid, granddaughters take the same prescribed shares as daughters when there are no direct children.
3
Apply the rule with a single daughter
When the deceased has one daughter (bint ṣulbiyya) and one or more granddaughters, the daughter takes 1/2, and the granddaughters take 1/6 to complete the 2/3. This is based on the principle of 'completion of the two-thirds'.
The reason is that the Qur'anic term 'children' includes grandchildren by metaphorical extension or consensus.
4
Recognize blocking by two daughters
Two or more daughters of the deceased exhaust the 2/3 share, so granddaughters are completely blocked (hajb hirmān) and inherit nothing, unless a male grandchild (e.g., a son's son) is present.
If a male grandchild is present in the same or lower degree, the granddaughters become 'asaba (agnatic) through him and inherit by residue, not by fixed share.
5
Analyze multiple levels of granddaughters
When granddaughters are at different degrees (e.g., daughter of a son, daughter of a son's son), the closest takes the place of a daughter, the next takes the place of a granddaughter, and so on. The residual agnatic inheritance goes to the nearest male.
A detailed example in the text illustrates this with three groups.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعصبها الابن وله مثل حظهما ،وولد الابن كولده عند عدمه ويحجب بالابن، ومع أي البنت أي للابن أي عدم الابن أي ولد الابن البنت لأقرب الذكور الباقي، وللإناث السدس تكملة للثلثين، وحجبن ببنتين الصلبية من نصيب البنت إلا أن يكون معهن أو أسفل منهن ذكر أي مع بنات الابن بنات الابن وعصبها الابن إلخ معناه إذا اختلط البنون والبنات عصب البنون البنات فيكون للابن مثل، حظهما فصار للبنات ثلاثة أحوال النصف للواحدة والثلثان للاثنين فصاعدا، والتعصيب عند الاختلاط بالذكور. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٤٥/٩] وولد الابن إلخ : أي ولد الابن يكون كولده عند عدم الابن، حتى يكون بنو الابن عصبة كالبنين وبنات الابن كالبنات حتى يكون للواحدة ،النصف وللثنتين فصاعدا الثلثان، فيعصبهن الذكور عند اختلاطهن بالذكور، فيكون للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين. (فتح) ويحجب بالابن: أي ولد الابن يحجب بالابن ذكورهم وإناثهم فيه سواء؛ لأن الابن أقرب وهم عصبة، بالعصوبة، وكذا بالفرض؛ لأن بنات الابن يدلين به فلا يرثن مع الابن وإن كن لا يدلين به، فإن كان عمهن فهو مساو لأصلهن، فيحجبهن كما يحجب أولاده؛ لأن ما ثبت لأحد المثلين ثبت لمساويه ضرورة. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٤٥/٩] لأقرب الذكور الباقي: أي إذا كان مع بنت الميت الصلبية أولاد الابن أو أولاد ابن الابن وإن سفل أو المجموع كان الباقي بعد فرض البنت الصلبية لأقرب الذكور منهم؛ لأنه عصبة فيحجب الأبعد، وأطلق في الذكور، والمراد أولاد الابن وهذا المجموع إنما يستقيم إذا لم تكن في درجته بنت ابن، وأما إذا كانت في فلا يرثون معه درجته بنت ابن، فلا يكون الباقي من فرض البنت له وحده بل تشاركه فيه تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٤٥/٩] وللإناث إلخ: أي لبنات الابن مع البنت الواحدة الصلبية السدس تكملة للثلثين، فقوله: "تكملة للثلثين" دليل على دخولهن في لفظ الأولاد بعموم المجاز أو بالإجماع، فأخذت الصلبية النصف لقربها، وبقي السدس، فيعطى لهن، وهذا أي كون السدس لبنات الابن إذا لم يكن في درجتهن ابن ابن، وأما إذا كان معهن ابن ابن يكن عصبة معه فلا يرثن السدس، وإنما كان لهن السدس عند انفرادهن. (فتح، تكملة) وحجبن ببنتين: أي يحجب بنات الابن ببنتين صلبيتين؛ لأن إرثهن كان تكملة للثلثين، وقد كمل ببنتين فسقط؛ إذ لا سبيل لتوريثهن فرضا وتعصيبا تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٤٦/٩] إلا أن يكون إلخ: أي تحجب بنات الابن ببنتين صلبيتين إلا إذا كان معهن في درجتهن أو أسفل منهن ذكر، سواء كان أخا لهن أو لم يكن، فحينئذ كانت فوقه ممن لم يكن ذات سهم، ويسقط أي الذكر الإناث، ومن من يعصب ذلك الذكر من كانت بحذائه من دونه، ثم الأصل في بنات الابن عند عدم بنات الصلب أن أقربهن إلى الميت ينزل منزلة البنت الصلبية، والتي تليها في القرب منزلة بنات الابن وهكذا وإن سفلن مثاله لو ترك ثلاث بنات الابن بعضهن أسفل من بعض، وثلاث بنات ابن ابن آخر بعضهن أسفل من بعض، وثلاث بنات ابن ابن ابن آخر بعضهن أسفل من بعض، فيعصب من الذكر كانت بحذائه من الإناث من بنات الابن صورته هكذا: الفريق الاول زید الفريق الثاني أي عدم بنات الصلب الفريق الثالث الذكر ابن (عمرو) ابن (بكر) ابن (خالد) ابن ابن العليا من الفريق الأول وهي بنت الابن ابن ابن العليا من الفريق الثاني بنت ابن الوسطى من الفريق الأول وهي بنت ابن الابن بنت السفلى من الفريق الأول وهي بنت ابن ابن الابن وهي بنت ابن الابن بنت ابن ابن الوسطى من الفريق الثاني وهي بنت ابن ابن الابن ابن بنت السفلى من الفريق الثاني وهي بنت ابن ابن ابن الابن العليا من الفريق الثالث وهي بنت ابن ابن الابن بنت الوسطى من الفريق الثالث وهي بنت ابن ابن ابن الابن السفلى من الفريق الثالث وهي بنت ابن ابن ابن ابن الابن فالعليا من الفريق الأول لا يوازيها أحد، فيكون لها النصف والوسطى من الأول يوازيها العليا من الثاني، فلهما السدس تكملة للثلثين، ولا شيء للسفليات إلا أن يكون مع واحدة منهن غلام فيعصبها، ومن بحذائها ومن فوقها ممن لم يكن صاحبة فرض حتى لو كان الغلام مع السفلى في الفريق الأول عصبها وعصب الوسطى من الفريق الثاني والعليا من الفريق الثالث وسقطت السفليات [رمز الحقائق: ٥١٧/٢]
And her agnate is the son, and he gets the share of two females. And the son's son is like his son in his absence, and is blocked by the son. And with any daughter, the (residue) goes to the nearest male (agnate). And for the females (granddaughters) is one-sixth as a completion of the two-thirds. And they are blocked by two daughters (of the deceased) unless there is with them or below them a male. The meaning of 'And her agnate is the son etc.' is that when sons and daughters mix, the sons make the daughters agnates, so the male gets twice the share of the female. So for girls (daughters) there are three cases: half for one, two-thirds for two or more, and agnatic inheritance when mixed with males. (Complement from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) 'And the son's son etc.' means the son's son is like his son in the absence of the son, such that sons of the son are agnates like sons, and daughters of the son like daughters, so for one (granddaughter) half, for two or more two-thirds. The males make them agnates when they mix with males, so the male gets twice the share of the female. (Fath) 'And is blocked by the son' means the son's son is blocked by the son, both males and females equally, because the son is closer and they are agnates by agnation, and also by (fixed) share because daughters of the son descend through him so they do not inherit with the son even if they do not descend through him. If their paternal uncle (the son's brother) is equal to their origin (the deceased), he blocks them as he blocks his own children, because what is established for one of the two equals is established for his equal by necessity. (Complement) 'For the nearest male the residue' means if with the deceased's daughter there are children of a son or children of a son's son even if lower, or a combination, the residue after the fixed share of the daughter goes to the nearest male among them, because he is an agnate and blocks the more distant. He generalized in mentioning males, but the intention is children of the son. This combination is valid only if there is not a daughter of a son in his degree. If there is a daughter of a son in his degree, then the residue from the daughter's share is not for him alone but she shares it with him. (Complement) 'And for the females etc.' means for the daughters of a son with one daughter (of the deceased) is one-sixth to complete the two-thirds. His saying 'completion of the two-thirds' is evidence that they are included in the word 'children' by metaphorical generality or by consensus. So the (deceased's) daughter takes half due to her closeness, and one-sixth remains, so it is given to them. This (i.e., the one-sixth being for granddaughters) is when there is not a son's son in their degree, but if there is a son's son with them, they become agnates with him and do not take the one-sixth. They only take the one-sixth when alone. (Fath, Takmila) 'And they are blocked by two daughters' means that granddaughters are blocked by two daughters (of the deceased), because their inheritance was a completion of the two-thirds, and it is completed by two daughters, so it falls, as there is no way to give them a fixed share or agnatic inheritance. (Complement) 'Unless there is etc.' means granddaughters are blocked by two daughters unless there is with them in their degree or lower a male, whether he is their brother or not. In that case, those above him who are not entitled to a fixed share fall, and the male makes (the females) agnates. Then the principle for granddaughters when there are no daughters is that the closest to the deceased takes the place of a daughter (of the deceased), and the next in closeness takes the place of granddaughters, and so on even if lower. Example: Suppose someone leaves three granddaughters (daughters of a son) some lower than others, and three daughters of a son's son some lower than others, and three daughters of a son's son's son some lower than others. Then the male (among them) makes agnate those females who are opposite him. The picture of the granddaughters is as follows: Group 1: Zaid. Group 2: meaning no daughters. Group 3: the male. (Then a diagram with names and relations). So the topmost of Group 1 (bint al-ibn) has no one equal to her, so she takes half. The middle of Group 1 is matched by the top of Group 2, so both get one-sixth to complete two-thirds. And the lowest ones get nothing unless there is a boy (ghulam) with one of them, in which case he makes her agnate, and also those opposite her and above her who are not entitled to a fixed share. So if the boy is with the lowest in Group 1, he makes her agnate and also makes agnate the middle of Group 2 and the top of Group 3, and the lowest ones fall. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq)
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the inheritance rules for grandchildren (awlād al-ibn), particularly granddaughters (banāt al-ibn). The author begins by stating the general rule: a son's son (ibn al-ibn) is like a son in being an agnatic heir ('asaba) and takes the residue, with each male getting twice the share of a female when mixed with females. A granddaughter (bint al-ibn) is like a daughter in having a prescribed share: half for one, two-thirds for two or more. However, when grandchildren are mixed with males, the males make the females 'asaba bi-ghayrihim (agnates through others), giving each male twice the share of a female.

The text then explains that grandsons are blocked (mahjūb) by a son (al-ibn), because the son is closer. Similarly, granddaughters are blocked by a son, even though they do not descend through him directly. If there is a daughter (bint ṣulbiyya) with grandchildren, the residue after her fixed share goes to the nearest male agnate among the grandchildren.

The commentary then addresses a common scenario: one daughter with one or more granddaughters. The granddaughters receive one-sixth to complete the two-thirds (since the daughter takes half, leaving one-sixth). This is based on the principle that the term 'awlād' in the Qur'an includes grandchildren by metaphorical extension (majāz) or by consensus (ijmā').

Granddaughters are blocked (ḥujibna) by two daughters, because the two-thirds is already fulfilled, leaving no room for them. An exception is made: if there is a male (e.g., a son's son) in the same degree or lower with the granddaughters, the male makes them 'asaba (agnatic), and they no longer take a fixed share but instead inherit by ta'sīb (residue).

The rule for ordering granddaughters when there are no daughters is that the closest in degree takes the place of a daughter, the next takes the place of a granddaughter, and so on. A detailed example is given with three groups of granddaughters at different levels (e.g., daughters of a son, daughters of a son's son, etc.). The text explains which ones inherit and which are excluded based on proximity and the presence of a male (ghulām). For instance, the topmost granddaughter (the closest) takes half; the middle one of the first group and the top of the second group share one-sixth each to complete two-thirds; and the lower ones get nothing unless accompanied by a male who makes them 'asaba.

The passage relies on reasoning and consensus, with references to earlier Hanafi works like al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Fath, and Ramz al-Haqa'iq. It reflects the established Hanafi position on grandchild inheritance, which is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
بنات الابن (banāt al-ibn): Granddaughters from a son (i.e., daughters of the deceased's son).
ولد الابن (walad al-ibn): Children of a son, including both sons and daughters of the son.
تعصيب (ta'sīb): Making a female heir an agnatic heir ('asaba) through the presence of a male agnate, so she inherits by residue rather than fixed share.
حجب (ḥajb): Blocking or excluding an heir from inheritance due to the presence of a closer heir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the share of granddaughters when the deceased has two daughters?
A) 1/6 each
B) 1/3 total
C) 1/4 each
D) Nothing (blocked)

Key Takeaway
Granddaughters inherit like daughters in the absence of direct daughters, but two daughters block them unless a male grandchild provides agnatic inheritance.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate

Full Sisters: Shares and Ta'sib with Brothers
Rule establishing full sisters as substitutes for daughters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the shares of full sisters (half for one, two-thirds for two or more) and calculate distribution when full brothers are present (2:1 male-to-female ratio).

Core Idea
Full sisters inherit half (one) or two-thirds (two or more) like daughters, and become residuaries with brothers at a 2:1 ratio.

The Hanafi madhhab treats full sisters as substitutes for daughters and granddaughters when these are absent. This rule, grounded in the Quranic kalala verse, prescribes fixed shares for sisters and transforms them into residuaries (asaba) when brothers are present. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs
Determine whether the deceased has full sisters (al-ukhawāt li-ab wa-umm) and full brothers. Note the absence of daughters and granddaughters (the primary condition for the rule).
Sisters are 'full' only if they share both parents with the deceased.
2
Apply the fixed shares
If no brother exists, one sister receives 1/2; two or more sisters share 2/3 equally. If brothers exist, sisters become residuaries (asaba) and the male-to-female ratio is 2:1.
The fixed shares apply only when there are no daughters or granddaughters.
3
Calculate with brothers present
When brothers are present, siblings share the residue after any other fixed heirs. Divide the residue by treating each brother as two sisters, then allocate accordingly.
Example: one brother and one sister share residue 2:1, so brother gets 2/3, sister 1/3.
4
Consider daughters or granddaughters
If daughters or granddaughters exist, full sisters do not receive fixed shares; instead they inherit as asaba, taking the residue after the daughters’ shares.
This distinguishes full sisters from daughters: daughters block sisters from fixed shares but not from residue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأخوات لأب وأم كبنات الصلب عند عدمهن، أي الأخوات لأب وأم كبنات الصلب عند عدم بنات الصلب وبنات الابن حتى يكون للواحدة النصف، وللثنتين الثلثان، ومع الإخوة لأب وأم للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ الْكَلالَةِ إِنِ امْرُؤٌ هَلَكَ لَيْسَ لَهُ وَلَدٌ وَلَهُ أُخْتٌ فَلَهَا نِصْفُ مَا تَرَكَ وَهُوَ يَرثُهَا إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهَا وَلَدٌ فَإِنْ كَانَتَا اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُمَا الثُّلُثَانِ مِمَّا تَرَكَ وَإِنْ كَانُوا إِخْوَةً رِجَالًا وَنِسَاءً فَلِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ ﴾ (النساء:١٧٦) ولهن الباقي مع البنات أو بنات الابن. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٤٨/٩]
And full sisters are like daughters in their absence. That is, full sisters are like daughters in the absence of daughters and granddaughters, such that for one (sister) is half, for two is two-thirds, and with full brothers the male gets twice the share of the female; due to His saying the Exalted: 'Say, Allah gives you a ruling concerning al-kalala: if a man dies having no child and he has a sister, then for her is half of what he left, and he will inherit from her if she has no child; and if there are two, then for them is two-thirds of what he left; and if there are brothers and sisters, then for the male is the share of two females.' (Al-Nisa' 4:176) And for them (the sisters) is the residue with daughters or granddaughters. (Complement of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq)
Source pages p. 536

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the inheritance of full siblings (ikhwa li-ab wa-umm). The matn states that full sisters are like daughters in their absence. The commentary clarifies that full sisters take the place of daughters (banāt ṣulbiyya) and also of granddaughters (banāt al-ibn) when none exist. Thus, one sister gets half, two or more get two-thirds. When mixed with full brothers, the brothers make them 'asaba (agnatic), so each male gets twice the share of a female, as per the principle of ta'sīb.

The proof is the Qur'anic verse from Sūrat al-Nisā' (4:176), which specifically addresses inheritance in the case of kalāla (a person who dies with no ascendant or descendant). The verse prescribes the shares for siblings: half for one sister, two-thirds for two sisters, and for brothers and sisters together, each male gets twice the share of a female.

The text also notes that full siblings take the residue (al-bāqī) when there are daughters or granddaughters. This means that if there is a daughter or granddaughter, the full siblings inherit as 'asaba after the fixed shares of the daughters/granddaughters are given. This is a key Hanafi ruling: full siblings are not blocked by daughters but rather inherit alongside them as residuaries.

Key Terms
الأخوات لأب وأم (al-ukhawāt li-ab wa-umm): Full sisters (sisters sharing both father and mother with the deceased).
كلالة (kalāla): A person who dies leaving no ascendant (father) nor descendant (child). This is the context of the Qur'anic verse for sibling inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what share does one full sister receive if the deceased has no children, no grandchildren, and no brothers?
A) One-fourth
B) One-half
C) Two-thirds
D) The entire estate

Key Takeaway
Full sisters inherit like daughters when no daughters exist, with shares half (one) or two-thirds (two or more), and become residuaries with brothers at a 2:1 ratio.

The Quranic Proof: Kalala Verse (Al-Nisa' 4:176)
Quranic proof for sibling inheritance shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Surah Al-Nisa' 4:176 provides the proof for the inheritance shares of full siblings and identify the condition of kalala.

Core Idea
The Quranic kalala verse directly establishes the half, two-thirds, and 2:1 male-female ratio for full siblings.

The commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq cites the famous kalala verse from Surah Al-Nisa' as the primary evidence for the ruling on full siblings. This lesson examines the verse's structure, its legal implications, and how the Hanafi school applies it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verse and its context
The passage quotes Quran 4:176, which addresses inheritance in the case of kalala (a person with no ascendant or descendant). Recognize that this verse is the foundational text for sibling inheritance.
Kalala is defined in Hanafi law as someone who leaves neither parent nor child.
2
Extract the three rulings
The verse gives three scenarios: (1) one sister gets half, (2) two sisters get two-thirds, (3) brothers and sisters together: male gets twice female. These correspond to the fixed shares and ta'sib.
The third scenario implies that brothers make sisters 'asaba.
3
Analyze the thubut and dalala
The verse is mutawatir (qat'i al-thubut) as part of the Quran. Its meaning is zanni (open to interpretation) regarding the absence of children; the Hanafi school interprets 'walad' to include child or grandchild, but the verse explicitly mentions 'no child'.
The text's clarity on the shares is strong, but details like the presence of daughters are derived through qiyas.
4
Connect to the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi school extends the verse's ruling to cases where there are no daughters or granddaughters, and also applies the ta'sib rule when brothers are present. The passage also notes that sisters take residue with daughters via qiyas.
This expansion is based on the principle that the absence of a child triggers sibling shares, and qiyas on the verse's logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Shares of Half-Sisters and Uterine Siblings in Hanafi Faraid
Explains shares of half-sisters and uterine siblings with hajb rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares of consanguine half-sisters and uterine siblings and apply the rules of exclusion (hajb) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Half-sisters get half or two-thirds; uterine siblings get one-sixth or one-third; all siblings excluded by son, father, and grandfather.

This lesson unpacks the fixed shares of siblings who do not share both parents: consanguine half-sisters (same father) and uterine siblings (same mother). Understanding their shares and when they are excluded is essential for accurate estate division. The passage also clarifies the concept of 'asabah and the controversial exclusion by the grandfather.

Guided Path
1
Identify sibling categories
Distinguish between full siblings (banu al-'ayan), consanguine half-siblings (banu al-'ila), and uterine siblings (banu al-akhyaf). Their shares depend on their category.
Full siblings inherit as 'asabah after fixed shares; half-siblings have prescribed fixed shares unless 'asabah applies.
2
Apply fixed shares for half-sisters
One consanguine half-sister gets 1/2; two or more get 2/3 equally. If a consanguine brother exists, they become 'asabah: son gets double daughter.
This mirrors the rule for daughters of a son below a daughter.
3
Apply fixed shares for uterine siblings
One uterine sibling (male or female) gets 1/6; two or more share 1/3 equally between males and females.
Based on Quran 4:12, interpreted by Hanafis to refer to uterine siblings only.
4
Determine 'asabah relations
Half-sisters become 'asabah with their consanguine brothers, the grandfather (if no brother), or with a daughter/son's daughter (but the daughter does not make them 'asabah; they become 'asabah with her).
The daughter herself is not an 'asabah; sisters become 'asabah with her due to hadith.
5
Apply exclusion (hajb) rules
All siblings (full, half, uterine) are excluded by the son, grandson, father, and grandfather (per Abu Hanifa). The grandfather's exclusion is disputed by Malik and Shafi'i.
The condition for sibling inheritance is kalalah (no parent or child).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الفرائض
بيان ذوي الفروض
ولأب كبنات الابن مع الصلبيات، وعصبهن اخوتهن والبنت وبنت الابن، وللواحد من ولد الأم السدس، وللأكثر الثلث ذكرهم كأنثاهم، وحجبن بالابن وابنه وإن سفل، وبالأب والجد والبنت تحجب .
في القسمة والاستحقاق
ولأب إلخ: أي الأخوات لأب مع الأخوات لأب وأم كبنات الابن مع البنات الصلبيات حتى يكون للواحدة من الأخوات لأب النصف، وللثنتين فصاعدا الثلثان، ومع الإخوة لأب للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين، ومع الأخت الواحدة لأب وأم السدس تكملة للثلثين، ويسقطن بالأختين لأم وأب إلا أن يكون معهن أخ لأب فيعصبهن. رمز الحقائق: ۵۱۷/۲] وعصبهن إخوتهن : يعني يعصب الأخوات لأب وأم أو لأب إخوتهن يعني الموازي لهن، و"الإخوة" ليس بقيد، وكذا يعصبهن الجد عند عدم الأخ الموازي لهن، فيقاسمها الجد، وفي "كشف الغوامض": ولا يعصب الشقيقة الأخ لأب إجماعا؛ لأنها أقوى منه في النسب، بل تأخذ فرضها، ولا يعصب الأخت لأب أخ شقيق، بل يحجبها؛ لأنه أقوى منها إجماعا تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٤٩/٩] والبنت: أي يعصبهن أيضا البنت وبنت الابن؛ لقوله عليه: "اجعلوا الأخوات مع البنات عصبة"، وجعل الشيخ يطلبه البنت ممن تعصب الأخوات، وهو مجاز، وفي الحقيقة لا ،تعصبهن، وإنما يصرن عصبة معها؛ لأن البنت ليست بعصبة في هذه الحالة فكيف تعصب غيرها، بخلاف الإخوة على ما يجيء عن قريب إن شاء الله تعالى، وهذا قول الصحابة ، وروي عن ابن عباس هما: أنه أسقط الأخوات بالبنت [ رمز الحقائق: ٥١٨/٢] وللواحد إلخ يعني للواحد من ولد الأم السدس وللأكثر من الواحد الثلث ذكورهم كإناثهم؛ لقوله تعالى: وَإِنْ كَانَ رَجُلٌ يُورَثُ كَلالَةٌ أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ وَلَهُ أَخٌ أَوْ أُخْتٌ فَلِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ فَإِنْ كَانُوا أَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ فَهُمْ شُرَكَاءُ القلب (النساء: ۱۲) والمراد به أولاد الأم؛ لأن أولاد الأم والأب مذكورون في آية النصف على ما ذكرنا من قبل، ولهذا قرأها بعضهم ولأخ أو أخت لأم" ، وإطلاق الشركة يقتضي المساواة كما إذا قال: شريكي فلان في هذا المال، أو قال له شركة؛ لأن الله تعالى سوى بينهما حالة الانفراد، فدل ذلك على استوائهما حالة الاجتماع تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٥٠/٩]
جمهور
و حجبن بالابن إلخ [ أي جميع الإخوة والأخوات من أي جهة كانوا (طائي)] أي الأخوات كلهن يحجبن بهؤلاء المذكورين وهم الابن وابن الابن وإن سفل، والأب والجد وإن علا، وكذا الإخوة يحجبون؛ لأن ميراثهم مشروط بالكلالة واختلفوا في الكلالة هل هي صفة للميت، أو للورثة أو للتركة، وقرئ "يورث" بكسر الراء وفتحها، وأياما كان يشترط لتسميته به عدم الوالد والولد للميت فيسقطون بهم تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٥٠/٩] والجد: أي عند أبي حنيفة، وقال مالك والشافعي: لا يحجبن بالجد، ويسقط أولاد الأب بهؤلاء، وبالأخ لأب وأم كذا في "ملا مسكين"، قال في "الفتح": وعلى قول أبي حنيفة الفتوى كما في "شرح السراجية"، والخلاف في الإخوة والأخوات الأشقاء، أو لأب، أما الإخوة والأخوات لأم فلا خلاف في سقوطهم بالجد.

ثم ذكر في التكملة والفتح: وللأخوات لأب سبع هذه الخمس، والسدس مع شقيقة واحدة والسقوط مع شقيقتين إلا إذا عصبهن أخوهن، واعلم أن أولاد الأب والأم يسمون "بني الأعيان"، والإخوة والأخوات لأب "بني العلاة"، والإخوة والأخوات لأم "بني الأخياف".
Book of Inheritance. Explanation of fixed shares. And for father's side sisters, like daughters of son with daughters, and their 'asabah are their brothers, and the daughter and son's daughter. And for the single among uterine siblings, one-sixth, and for multiple, one-third, males like females. And they are excluded by the son and his son however low, and by the father and grandfather, and by the daughter. In division and entitlement. 'And for father's side' etc.: meaning sisters from father's side with sisters from both parents are like daughters of son with daughters, so that for one sister from father's side half, for two or more two-thirds, and with brothers from father's side the male is like the share of two females, and with one sister from both parents one-sixth completing the two-thirds, and they are dropped by two sisters from mother and father unless there is a brother from father's side who makes them 'asabah. Their 'asabah are their brothers: meaning brothers from father's side and both parents make them 'asabah, i.e., those equivalent to them, and 'brothers' is not a restriction, likewise the grandfather makes them 'asabah when the equivalent brother is absent, so the grandfather divides with her. And in Kashf al-Ghawamid: The full sister is not made 'asabah by the consanguine brother by consensus because she is stronger in lineage, rather she takes her fixed share, and the consanguine sister is not made 'asabah by the full brother, rather he excludes her because he is stronger than her by consensus. And the daughter: meaning also the daughter and son's daughter make them 'asabah due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Make sisters with daughters 'asabah.' The Sheikh sought the daughter from among those who make sisters 'asabah, but it is metaphorical; in reality, they do not make them 'asabah, rather they become 'asabah with her, because the daughter is not an 'asabah in this case, so how can she make others 'asabah? Unlike brothers as will come shortly. This is the saying of the Companions, and it is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas that he dropped sisters by the daughter. And 'for a single etc.' means for the single among uterine siblings one-sixth, and for more than one one-third, males like females due to His statement: 'And if a man is inherited kalalah or a woman, and he has a brother or a sister, then for each of them one-sixth, and if they are more than that, then they are partners in the third' (4:12). And what is meant by it is uterine siblings, because the full siblings are mentioned in the verse of half as we mentioned before. Hence some recited 'or a brother or a sister from the mother'. And the expression of partnership implies equality, as if one says: my partner so-and-so in this wealth, or he says to him partnership; because Allah made them equal in the case of singularity, so that indicates their equality in the case of plurality. 'And they are excluded by the son etc.' i.e., all siblings from whatever side are excluded by these mentioned: the son, the son's son however low, the father, the grandfather however high, and likewise the brothers are excluded because their inheritance is conditional upon kalalah, and they differed concerning kalalah: whether it is a description of the deceased, the heirs, or the estate, and it was recited 'yurathu' with kasra and fatha of the ra', and in any case, it requires the absence of parent and child for the deceased, so they fall by them. And the grandfather: according to Abu Hanifa; Malik and al-Shafi'i said: they are not excluded by the grandfather. And the children of the father are dropped by these, and by the full brother, as in Mulla Miskin. Al-Fath said: and the fatwa is on the saying of Abu Hanifa as in Sharh al-Sirajiyyah, and the dispute is concerning full and consanguine siblings; as for uterine siblings, there is no dispute about their exclusion by the grandfather. Then in al-Takmila and al-Fath: And for sisters from father's side seven cases: these five, and one-sixth with one full sister, and being dropped by two full sisters unless they have a brother who makes them 'asabah. And know that the children of father and mother are called 'banu al-'ayan', the siblings from father only 'banu al-'ila', and the uterine siblings 'banu al-akhyaf'.
Source pages p. 537

Commentary
This passage is a ruling commentary that explains the inheritance shares of half-sisters (from father's side) and uterine siblings (from mother's side), along with rules of exclusion (hajb). The author, commenting on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, clarifies that sisters from father's side are analogous to daughters of son with daughters: one sister gets half, two or more get two-thirds, and brothers make them 'asabah (residuaries). The text also discusses the concept of 'asabah: brothers, grandfather, daughter, and son's daughter can make sisters into 'asabah, but there is a subtlety: the daughter herself is not an 'asabah but sisters become 'asabah with her. For uterine siblings, the share is one-sixth for one, one-third for two or more, divided equally among males and females, based on the Quranic verse (4:12) interpreted to refer to uterine siblings. The exclusion rules state that all siblings are excluded by the son, grandson, father, and grandfather. However, there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the grandfather excludes siblings, while Malik and al-Shafi'i disagree. The fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view. The passage concludes with a summary of the seven states for consanguine sisters and the terminology for different types of siblings: full siblings (banu al-'ayan), consanguine (banu al-'ila), and uterine (banu al-akhyaf).

Key Terms
العصبة (al-'asabah): Residuary heirs who take the remainder of the estate after fixed shares are distributed, or the entire estate if no fixed shares.
الكلالة (al-kalalah): A person who dies without leaving a parent or child.
بني الأعيان (banu al-'ayan): Full siblings (same father and mother).
بني العلاة (banu al-'ila): Consanguine siblings (same father, different mother).
بني الأخياف (banu al-akhyaf): Uterine siblings (same mother, different father).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following heirs excludes all siblings (full, half, and uterine)?
A) Grandfather
B) Grandson
C) Full brother
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
Half-sisters and uterine siblings have fixed shares; their inheritance is conditional on the absence of descendants and ascendants, and the grandfather excludes them in the Hanafi view.

Definition and Classification of 'Asabah
Defines 'asabah and classifies its types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'asabah, distinguish between lineage-based and cause-based 'asabah, and identify the three subcategories of lineage-based 'asabah with examples.

Core Idea
An 'asabah inherits all alone or the remainder after fixed shares; it is either by lineage or by cause.

The passage opens the second category of heirs after fixed-share holders. It defines 'asabah and then classifies 'asabah into two major types: nasabi (by lineage) and sababi (by cause). Within nasabi, there are three divisions: 'asabah bi-nafsihi (by self), bi-ghayrihi (by others), and ma'a ghayrihi (with others). Understanding this taxonomy is essential for determining who inherits the residue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Locate the definition of 'asabah: 'one who takes the entire estate when alone, and the remainder with a fixed share holder.' Note that this definition has two parts.
The definition immediately follows 'Wa 'asabah'.
2
Distinguish the two main types
The text states that 'asabah is of two types: nasabi (lineage-based) and sababi (cause-based). List the subcategories under each.
Nasabi has three; sababi has two.
3
Analyze 'asabah bi-nafsihi
Understand the condition: every male whose lineage path to the deceased does not include a female. Give examples: son, father, brother, paternal uncle.
This is the default 'asabah.
4
Analyze 'asabah bi-ghayrihi
These are females whose fixed share is half or two-thirds (e.g., sisters, daughters) who become 'asabah through a male co-heir (brother). Note the condition: they must have a brother alongside them.
The male elevates them from fixed-share to 'asabah.
5
Analyze 'asabah ma'a ghayrihi
These are females who become 'asabah in conjunction with another female (e.g., daughters with sisters). The sister takes the remainder after the daughter's fixed share.
No male is present; two females combine.

بيان العصبات
وعصبة أي من أخذ الكل إذا انفرد، والباقي مع ذي سهم، والأحق عطف على قوله: ذو فرض الابن ثم ابنه وإن سفل أي كل المال أي أخذ الباقي مقدر من العصبات
ثم تفسير: ولد الأم فقط: يعني البنت تحجب الإخوة والأخوات من الأم، ولا تحجب الإخوة والأخوات من الأبوين، أو من الأب؛ لأن شرط إرث ولد الأم الكلالة، ولا كلالة مع الولد والبنت ولد فتحجبهم، وكذا بنت البنت؛ لأن بنت الابن يقوم مقامه، فإن قيل: وجب أن لا ترث الإخوة والأخوات لأب وأم، أو لأب فقط البنت مع وبنت الابن؛ لأن شرط إرثهم الكلالة قلنا : الكلالة شرطت في حقهم لإرث النصف أو الثلثين، ولإرث الكل بالعصوبة فإذا انتفت الكلالة انتفى هذا الإرث المشروط بها لا مطلق الإرث، فيستحقون الإرث بالعصوبة مع البنت بنص آخر، بخلاف إرث أولاد الأم؛ فإن جميع إرثهم مشروط بالكلالة، فينتفي بعدمها، فصار للأخوات لأب وأم خمس أحوال للواحدة ،النصف والثلثان للأكثر ، والتعصيب بأخيهن، وكذا مع البنات أو بنات الابن والسقوط مع الابن. وللأخوات لأب سبع هذه الخمس، والسدس مع شقيقة واحدة والسقوط مع شقيقتين إلا إذا عصبهن أخوهن، واعلم أن أولاد الأب والأم يسمون "بني الأعيان، والإخوة والأخوات لأب "بني العلاة"، والإخوة والأخوات لأم "بني الأخياف". (تكملة، فتح) وعصبة: لما فرغ من الصنف الأول من الورثة شرع في الثاني، فقال: "وعصبة وهو بالرفع عطف على قوله: "ذو "فرض" في أول الكتاب تقديره والورثة ذو فرض وعصبة ، ثم فسر العصبة بقوله: أي من أخذ الكل إذا انفرد. رمز الحقائق ٥١٨/٢] (ملا مسكين) أي من أخذ الكل يعني العصبة أخذ كل المال إذا كان من وحده، وأخذ الباقي الذي يبقيه صاحب الفرض إذا كان مع ذي سهم ،مقدر واعلم أن العصبة نوعان: نسبية، وسببية، والأولى ثلاثة أقسام عصبة بنفسه، وهو كل ذكر لا يدخل في نسبته إلى الميت أنثى، وهو الذي عرفه المصنف. وعصبة بغيره، وهي كل أنثى فرضها النصف أو الثلثان يصرن عصبة بإخوتهن كما تقدم. وعصبة مع غيره، وهي كل أنثى تصير عصبة مع أنثى أخرى كالبنات مع الأخوات والسببية نوعان: مولى العتاقة، ومولى الموالاة، وسيأتي بيانه. (تكملة وغيره)
أخذ الكل إلخ المراد به من أخذ الكل بجهة واحدة لئلا يرد البنت ونحوها؛ فإنها وإن أخذت الكل عند الانفراد لكن لا بجهة واحدة بل بجهتين هما الفرض والرد ولا حاجة إلى هذا القيد؛ لخروجها بقوله: "وأخذ الباقي مع ذي سهم" فتحصل أن العصبة. له الأمران لكن يرد مولى الموالاة وذوو الأرحام؛ فإنهما يأخذان ما أبقاه الزوجان، والكل عند الانفراد، وأجيب بأن السهم مطلق يشمل النسبي والسببي وهما لا يأخذان مع ذي سهم نسبي، (فتح) والأحق الابن: أي أحق العصبات وأولاهم بالعصوبة جزء الميت، وهو ابنه وإن سفل، وغيرهم محجوبون بهم؛ لقوله تعالى: يُوصِيكُمُ اللهُ فِي أَوْلادِكُمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ (النساء: ۱۱) إلى أن قال سبحانه وتعالى: ﴿وَلِأَبَوَيْهِ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ مِمَّا تَرَكَ إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ وَلَدٌ﴾ (النساء:۱۱) فجعل الأب صاحب فرض مع الولد، ولم يجعل =
Explanation of 'asabah. And an 'asabah is one who takes the entire estate when alone, and the remainder with a fixed share holder. And the foremost is attached to his statement: 'fixed share holder' - the son, then his son however low. i.e., all the wealth, i.e., takes the remainder, determined from the 'asabah. Then explanation: 'Only children of the mother' means: the daughter excludes siblings from the mother, and does not exclude siblings from both parents or from the father, because the condition for inheritance of uterine siblings is kalalah, and there is no kalalah with a child, and the daughter is a child, so she excludes them. Likewise the daughter of the son, because the daughter of the son takes his place. If it is said: It should be that siblings from both parents or from father only should not inherit with the daughter or son's daughter, because their inheritance condition is kalalah. We say: Kalalah is conditioned for them regarding inheritance of half or two-thirds, and for inheritance of all by 'asabah. So if kalalah is absent, this inheritance conditioned by it is absent, not inheritance absolutely; so they deserve inheritance by 'asabah with the daughter by another text, unlike the inheritance of uterine siblings; for all their inheritance is conditioned by kalalah, so it is negated by its absence. So for sisters from both parents there are five states: half for one, two-thirds for more, and being made 'asabah by their brothers, and likewise with daughters or son's daughters, and being dropped by the son. And for sisters from father's side seven states: these five, and one-sixth with one full sister, and being dropped by two full sisters unless their brother makes them 'asabah. And know that children of father and mother are called 'banu al-'ayan', siblings from father only 'banu al-'ila', and uterine siblings 'banu al-akhyaf'. (al-Takmila, al-Fath) And 'asabah: When he finished from the first category of heirs, he started on the second, so he said: 'And an 'asabah' with nominative case as an conjunct to his statement: 'a fixed share holder' at the beginning of the book, its estimation: 'and the heirs are fixed share holder and 'asabah'. Then he interpreted 'asabah by his statement: 'i.e., one who takes the entire estate when alone.' And know that 'asabah are of two types: by lineage and by cause. The first is three divisions: 'asabah by self, which is every male whose relation to the deceased does not include a female, and this is what the author defined. 'Asabah by others, which is every female whose fixed share is half or two-thirds, they become 'asabah by their brothers as previously. 'Asabah with others, which is every female who becomes 'asabah with another female, like daughters with sisters. And the cause-related 'asabah are of two types: the freed slave and the client of allegiance, and their explanation will come. (al-Takmila and others) 'Takes the entire etc.' The intended meaning is one who takes the entire estate by a single means, so as to exclude the daughter and the like, for although she takes the entire estate when alone, it is not by a single means but by two means: the fixed share and return (radd). But there is no need for this restriction due to his statement: 'and takes the remainder with a fixed share holder.' So it is established that the 'asabah has both attributes, but the client of allegiance and distant kindred (dhawu al-arham) are excluded because they take what the spouses leave behind, and the entirety when alone. And it is answered: the share absolutely includes lineage and cause, and they do not take with a fixed share holder of lineage. (al-Fath) And the foremost is the son: i.e., the most deserving of 'asabah and the first in 'asabah is the part of the deceased, which is his son however low, and others are blocked by them due to His statement: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male is like the share of two females' (4:11) until He said: 'And for his parents, for each of them one-sixth of what he left, if he has a child' (4:11), so He made the father a fixed share holder with a child, and did not make =
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage defines 'asabah (residuary heirs) and explains their categories. The matn states that an 'asabah is one who takes the entire estate alone, or the remainder after fixed shares. The commentator clarifies that the son is the foremost 'asabah, then his son, etc. He then addresses a nuance: the daughter excludes uterine siblings (because her presence negates kalalah) but does not exclude full or consanguine siblings; they instead become 'asabah with her. The passage then enumerates the five states for full sisters and seven for consanguine sisters. It introduces terminology for sibling types: full (banu al-'ayan), consanguine (banu al-'ila), and uterine (banu al-akhyaf). The 'asabah section then divides 'asabah into two types: nasabi (by lineage) and sababi (by cause). Nasabi is further divided into three: 'asabah bi-nafsihi (by self: any male without a female in lineage, e.g., son, father), 'asabah bi-ghayrihi (by others: females like sisters who become 'asabah through their brothers), and 'asabah ma'a ghayrihi (with others: females like daughters who become 'asabah with another female, e.g., daughters with sisters). Sababi 'asabah are two: the freed slave (mu'taq) and the client of allegiance (mawla al-muwalah). The passage also discusses the condition of taking the entire estate by one means, explaining that a daughter takes by both fixed share and return, so she is not an 'asabah in the strict sense. The son is the foremost 'asabah, proven by Quranic verses that give the son a fixed priority and reduce the father to a fixed share when there is a child.

Key Terms
العصبة بنفسه (al-'asabah bi-nafsihi): A male whose lineage to the deceased does not pass through a female, e.g., son, father, brother.
العصبة بغيره (al-'asabah bi-ghayrihi): A female whose fixed share is half or two-thirds who becomes an 'asabah through a male relative, e.g., sisters with brothers.
العصبة مع غيره (al-'asabah ma'a ghayrihi): A female who becomes an 'asabah in conjunction with another female, e.g., daughters with sisters.
مولى العتاقة (mawla al-'itaqa): The former master who freed a slave; inherits from the freed slave as an 'asabah by cause.
مولى الموالاة (mawla al-muwalah): A freed slave's client who has a contract of allegiance; inherits if no other heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many types of lineage-based 'asabah (nasabi) are there?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
An 'asabah inherits the entire estate alone or the remainder after fixed shares, and is classified as either lineage-based (nasabi) with three subcategories, or cause-based (sababi) with two types.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
10 min
Priority and Detailed Rules of 'Asabah: Son, Sister States
Explains priority of son and details inheritance states of sisters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the priority order among 'asabah (son foremost), and apply the five states of full sisters and seven states of consanguine sisters in inheritance calculations.

Core Idea
The son is the foremost 'asabah; full sisters and consanguine sisters have distinct inheritance states depending on presence of other heirs.

After defining 'asabah, the passage establishes the priority among 'asabah: the son (and his descendants) are the most deserving, blocking all others. It then addresses a common point of confusion: the daughter does not block full or consanguine siblings; instead, those siblings become 'asabah with her. The text then enumerates the five inheritance states for a full sister and seven for a consanguine sister, providing the foundational rules for their entitlement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foremost 'asabah
The passage states: 'al-aḥaqq al-ibn' – the son is the most deserving. Explain that 'son' includes his male descendants (son's son, etc.), and they block other 'asabah.
Proof from Quran 4:11.
2
Understand the daughter's effect on siblings
The passage discusses how a daughter (or son's daughter) does NOT exclude full or consanguine siblings; instead, those siblings become 'asabah with her. Uterine siblings are excluded because their inheritance requires kalalah.
This is a key distinction between uterine and other siblings.
3
List the five states of a full sister
From the text: a full sister inherits in five ways: (1) half when alone, (2) two-thirds when more than one, (3) 'asabah with a full brother, (4) 'asabah with a daughter or son's daughter, (5) dropped by a son.
She never gets a fixed share with a brother; she becomes 'asabah.
4
List the seven states of a consanguine sister
She has all the above five, plus: (6) one-sixth with one full sister, (7) dropped by two full sisters unless she has a consanguine brother to make her 'asabah.
The one-sixth is a fixed share when with one full sister.
5
Distinguish sibling terminology
The passage introduces names: banu al-'ayan (full siblings), banu al-'ila (consanguine), banu al-akhyaf (uterine). Know these terms.
Useful for text recognition.

Key Terms
بني الأعيان (banu al-'ayan): Full siblings sharing both father and mother.
بني العلاة (banu al-'ila): Consanguine siblings sharing only the father.
بني الأخياف (banu al-akhyaf): Uterine siblings sharing only the mother.
الكلالة (al-kalalah): The state of a deceased who has no ascendant or descendant; a condition for uterine siblings to inherit.

Checkpoint
How many states does a consanguine sister have?
A) Five
B) Six
C) Seven
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
The son is the foremost 'asabah; full sisters have five states, consanguine sisters seven, and the daughter does not block full/consanguine siblings but makes them 'asabah.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Types of 'Asaba (Residuary Heirs)
Definition and classification of 'asabat in Hanafi faraid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'asaba according to the Hanafi school and classify its types into lineage (nasabiyyah) and causal (sababiyyah), listing the three subtypes of lineage 'asaba.

Core Idea
The 'asaba takes all when sole, and the remainder after fixed-share heirs; it is of two main types: by lineage and by cause.

In this lesson, we begin the second category of heirs: the 'asabat. The author defines what makes an heir an 'asaba and then breaks down the types. Understanding this classification is fundamental to determining inheritance when there is no fixed-share heir, or when fixed-share heirs leave a residue.

Guided Path
1
Define 'Asaba
State the definition: one who takes the whole estate when alone, and the remainder after fixed-share heirs when present. Note the nuance that the daughter is excluded because she takes by both fard and radd, not solely by 'usubah.
The definition has two parts: taking the whole when alone and taking the remainder with a fixed-share heir.
2
Distinguish Types by Cause
Identify the two main categories: lineage ('asaba nasabiyyah) and causal ('asaba sababiyyah). The causal type arises from emancipation (mu'tiq) or alliance (mawla al-muwalah).
Causal 'asaba are discussed later.
3
Classify Lineage 'Asaba Subtypes
Split lineage 'asaba into three: bi-nafsihi (every male whose relation to deceased does not pass through a female, e.g., son, father), bi-ghayrihi (females with prescribed share half or two-thirds who become 'asaba with their brothers, e.g., full sister with full brother), and ma'a ghayrihi (females who become 'asaba with another female, e.g., daughters with sisters).
Memorize examples for each subtype.
4
Understand the Effect of Daughters on Siblings
The text explains that a daughter blocks uterine siblings (bani al-akhyaf) but does not block agnatic siblings (bani al-a'yan and bani al-'alat). This is because the condition of kalalah applies fully to uterine siblings, but only to the fixed-share portion of agnatic siblings; they can become 'asaba with the daughter.
This explains why full and consanguine sisters can inherit with daughters.

ولد الأم فقط. وعصبة أي من أخذ الكل إذا انفرد، والباقي مع ذي سهم، والأحق عطف على قوله: ذو فرض الابن ثم ابنه وإن سفل أي كل المال أي أخذ الباقي مقدر من العصبات ولد الأم فقط: يعني البنت تحجب الإخوة والأخوات من الأم، ولا تحجب الإخوة والأخوات من الأبوين، أو من الأب؛ لأن شرط إرث ولد الأم الكلالة، ولا كلالة مع الولد والبنت ولد فتحجبهم، وكذا بنت البنت؛ لأن بنت الابن يقوم مقامه، فإن قيل: وجب أن لا ترث الإخوة والأخوات لأب وأم، أو لأب فقط البنت مع وبنت الابن؛ لأن شرط إرثهم الكلالة قلنا : الكلالة شرطت في حقهم لإرث النصف أو الثلثين، ولإرث الكل بالعصوبة فإذا انتفت الكلالة انتفى هذا الإرث المشروط بها لا مطلق الإرث، فيستحقون الإرث بالعصوبة مع البنت بنص آخر، بخلاف إرث أولاد الأم؛ فإن جميع إرثهم مشروط بالكلالة، فينتفي بعدمها، فصار للأخوات لأب وأم خمس أحوال للواحدة ،النصف والثلثان للأكثر ، والتعصيب بأخيهن، وكذا مع البنات أو بنات الابن والسقوط مع الابن. وللأخوات لأب سبع هذه الخمس، والسدس مع شقيقة واحدة والسقوط مع شقيقتين إلا إذا عصبهن أخوهن، واعلم أن أولاد الأب والأم يسمون "بني الأعيان، والإخوة والأخوات لأب "بني العلاة"، والإخوة والأخوات لأم "بني الأخياف". (تكملة، فتح) وعصبة: لما فرغ من الصنف الأول من الورثة شرع في الثاني، فقال: "وعصبة وهو بالرفع عطف على قوله: "ذو "فرض" في أول الكتاب تقديره والورثة ذو فرض وعصبة ، ثم فسر العصبة بقوله: أي من أخذ الكل إذا انفرد. رمز الحقائق ٥١٨/٢] (ملا مسكين) أي من أخذ الكل يعني العصبة أخذ كل المال إذا كان من وحده، وأخذ الباقي الذي يبقيه صاحب الفرض إذا كان مع ذي سهم ،مقدر واعلم أن العصبة نوعان: نسبية، وسببية، والأولى ثلاثة أقسام عصبة بنفسه، وهو كل ذكر لا يدخل في نسبته إلى الميت أنثى، وهو الذي عرفه المصنف. وعصبة بغيره، وهي كل أنثى فرضها النصف أو الثلثان يصرن عصبة بإخوتهن كما تقدم. وعصبة مع غيره، وهي كل أنثى تصير عصبة مع أنثى أخرى كالبنات مع الأخوات والسببية نوعان: مولى العتاقة، ومولى الموالاة، وسيأتي بيانه. بيان العصبات
ثم الأب، ثم أب الأب وإن علا، ثم الأخ لأب وأم، ثم الأخ لأب، ثم ابن الأخ لأب وأم ثم ابن الأخ لأب، ثم الأعمام، ثم أعمام الأب، ثم أعمام الجد على أي ثم الأحق بالعصوبة الترتيب، ثم المعتق، ثم عصبته على الترتيب، أي مولى العتاقة أي المعتق المذكور للولد الذكر سهما ،مقررا، فتعين الباقي له فدل أن الولد الذكر مقدم عليه بالعصوبة، وابن الابن وإن سفل كالابن على ما بيناه؛ لأنه يقوم مقامه فيقدم عليه أيضا تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٥٣/٩] ثم الأب: أي ثم أولاهم بالعصوبة أصول الميت وإن علوا، وأولاهم به الأب؛ لأن الله تعالى شرط الإرث للإخوة بالكلالة وهو الذي لا ولد له ولا والد على ما بينا، فعلم بذلك أنهم لا يرثون مع الأب ضرورة، وعليه إجماع الأمة، فإذا كان ذلك مع الإخوة وهم أقرب الناس إليه بعد فروعه وأصوله فما ظنك بمن هو أبعد منه كأعمامه وأعمام أبيه والجدات. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٥٣/٩] ثم الأخ لأب إلخ حاصله: أنه يقدم ذو القرابتين على ذي قرابة واحدة كالأخ لأب وأم يقدم على الأخ لأب، وكالأخت لأب وأم إذا صارت عصبة مع البنت أولى من الأخ لأب، هذا عند الاستواء في الدرجة، وعند التفاوت يقدم الأعلى، وإذا لم تكن عصبة بل كانت ذات فرض فلها فرضها والباقي للأخ لأب، وإنما قدموا على الأعمام؛ لأن الله تعالى جعل الإرث في الكلالة للإخوة عند عدم الولد والوالد، فعلم بذلك أنهم يقدمون على الأعمام؛ لأنهم جزء الجد. (فتح، تكملة) ثم الأعمام: أي أولاهم بالميراث بعد الإخوة أعمام الميت؛ لأنهم بعد ذلك جزء الجد فكانوا أقرب، وقد قال : ألحقوا الفرائض بأهلها فما أبقت فلأولى .رجل. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٥٤/٩] ويعتبر بين هؤلاء الأصناف الأعمام قرب الدرجة أولا وقوة القرابة ثانيا، فعم الميت يقدم على عم أبيه المقدم على عم جده، وذلك لقرب الدرجة، وفي كل واحد من هذه الأصناف يقدم ذو القرابتين على ذي قرابة واحدة مع التساوي في الدرجة، فعم الميت لأب وأم أولى من عمه ،لأب، وكذا الحال في عم وعم جده، وهكذا الحكم في فروع هذه الأصناف فيعتبر أولا قرب الدرجة وثانيا قوة القرابة، فابن عم ا الميت يقدم على ابن ابن عمه، وابن عم الميت لأب وأم مقدم على ابن عمه لأب. (تكملة، فتح ثم المعتق: بكسر التاء أي ثم الأحق بالميراث بعد هؤلاء المعتق أي الذي أعتق؛ لقوله عليه: "الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب"، وهو آخر العصبات؛ لقوله علي : لمن أعتق عبدا: "إن مات ولم يدع وارثا كنت عصبة له". (عيني، تكملة)

من
ثم عصبته: أي عصبة المولى ومعناه: إذا لم يكن للمعتق عصبة من النسب على الترتيب الذي ذكرناه فعصبته مولاه الذي أعتقه، فإن لم يكن مولاه فعصبته عصبة المعتق وهو المولى على الترتيب الذي ذكرناه بأن يكون جزء المولى أولى، وإن سفل، ثم أصوله، ثم جزء أبيه، ثم جزء جده يقدم لقوة القرابة عند الاستواء، وبعلو الدرجة عند التفاوت، ولا يرث عصبة عصبة المعتق مثلا إذا أعتقت امرأة عبدا وماتت وتركت ابنا وزوجا، ثم مات المعتق -
Book of Inheritances: Explanation of the 'Asabat (residuary heirs). Only the child of the mother [i.e., the daughter?] blocks [the siblings from the mother]. And 'asaba is one who takes the whole when alone, and the remainder with a fixed-share heir. And the most entitled [heir] is a conjunctive phrase upon his saying: 'fixed-share' [i.e., the previous category]. The son, then his son even if lower. [Explanation]: 'the whole wealth' means taking the remainder. [The rest are from the 'asabat?] Only the child of the mother: meaning the daughter blocks the brothers and sisters from the mother, and does not block the brothers and sisters from both parents or from the father; because the condition for the inheritance of the child of the mother is kalalah (no ascending or descending heir), and there is no kalalah with the child, and the daughter is a child so she blocks them, and likewise the daughter of the son; because the son's daughter takes his place. If it is said: then the brothers and sisters from both parents or from the father only should not inherit with the daughter and the son's daughter because the condition for their inheritance is kalalah. We say: kalalah is stipulated for them regarding inheritance of half or two-thirds, and for inheritance of the whole by 'asabah; so if kalalah is absent, this inheritance that is conditioned by it is absent, not absolute inheritance; so they deserve inheritance by 'asabah with the daughter by another text, unlike the inheritance of children of the mother; for all their inheritance is conditioned by kalalah, so it is negated by its absence. So for the sisters from father and mother there are five states: for one, half; for more, two-thirds; and 'asabah with their brothers; likewise with daughters or daughters of sons; and fall with a son. For sisters from father only there are seven: these five, and a sixth with one full sister; and fall with two full sisters unless their brother makes them 'asabah. And know that children of father and mother are called 'bani al-a'yan', brothers and sisters from father only 'bani al-'alat', and brothers and sisters from mother only 'bani al-akhyaf'. (Tatmimah, Fath). And 'asaba: When he finished with the first category of heirs, he started on the second, so he said: 'And 'asaba' – which is in the nominative, conjunctive upon his saying 'fixed-share' at the beginning of the book; its estimation: 'the heirs are fixed-share and 'asaba'. Then he explained 'asaba by his saying: 'i.e., one who takes the whole when alone'. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/518) (Mulla Miskin) 'i.e., one who takes the whole': meaning the 'asaba takes the whole wealth if he is alone, and takes the remainder left by the fixed-share owner if he is with a fixed-share heir. And know that 'asaba is of two types: relative and causal. The first is of three divisions: 'asaba bi-nafsihi – which is every male with no female in his relation to the deceased, and this is what the author defined. 'Asaba bi-ghayrihi – which is every female whose prescribed share is half or two-thirds who become 'asaba with their brothers as mentioned. And 'asaba ma'a ghayrihi – which is every female who becomes 'asaba with another female, like daughters with sisters. And the causal type is of two: the freeer (mawla al-'itaqah) and the client of alliance (mawla al-muwalah), and its explanation will come. (Tatmimah wa ghayruh). 'Takes the whole etc.': the intended meaning is one who takes the whole by one avenue, to exclude the daughter and the like; for they, even though they take the whole when alone, but not by one avenue but by two avenues: the prescribed share and the return. And there is no need for this condition because of its exclusion by his saying 'and takes the remainder with a fixed-share heir'. So it is established that the 'asaba has both matters [taking whole and remainder]. But it would include the client of alliance and distant relatives (dhawi al-arham), for they take what the spouses leave, and the whole when alone. And it is answered that the share [mentioned] is absolute and includes the relative and causal, and they do not take with a relative fixed-share heir. (Fath). 'And the most entitled is the son': i.e., the most entitled of the 'asabat and the foremost of them in 'usubah is the part [offspring] of the deceased, which is his son even if lower, and others are excluded by them; because of the Almighty's saying: 'Allah enjoins you concerning your children: for the male is the like of the share of two females' (4:11) up to His saying: 'And for his parents, for each of them a sixth of what he leaves if he has a child' (4:11). So He made the father a fixed-share heir with the child, and did not make [the father an 'asaba?]. So the remainder is determined for the male child, indicating that the male child takes precedence over him in 'usubah. And the son's son even if lower is like the son as we explained; because he takes his place, so he takes precedence over him too. (Tatmimah al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9/453). Then the father: i.e., then the foremost of them in 'usubah are the ascendants of the deceased even if higher, and the foremost of them is the father; because Allah conditioned inheritance for the brothers on kalalah, which is that there is no child nor father as we explained, so it is known that they do not inherit with the father necessarily, and upon this is the consensus of the ummah. So if this is the case with the brothers, and they are the closest people to him after his branches and roots, what do you think of those who are farther than him like his paternal uncles and his father's paternal uncles and grandmothers? (Tatmimah al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9/453). Then the brother from father etc. In summary: the one with two ties [full brother] takes precedence over the one with one tie [consanguine brother], like the full brother takes precedence over the consanguine brother; and similarly the full sister when she becomes 'asaba with the daughter takes precedence over the consanguine brother. This is when there is equality in degree; when there is difference, the higher degree takes precedence. And if she is not an 'asaba but rather a fixed-share holder, then she gets her fixed share and the remainder goes to the consanguine brother. And they are given precedence over the paternal uncles because Allah made the inheritance in kalalah for brothers when there is no child or parent, so it is known that they take precedence over paternal uncles because they are part of the grandfather. (Fath, Tatmimah). Then the paternal uncles: i.e., the foremost in inheritance after the brothers are the paternal uncles of the deceased; because they are after that part of the grandfather, so they are closer. And it is reported: 'Give the fixed shares to their owners, and whatever is left goes to the nearest male person.' (Tatmimah al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9/454). And among these categories of paternal uncles, consideration is given first to closeness of degree and second to strength of kinship. So the deceased's paternal uncle takes precedence over his father's paternal uncle, and the father's paternal uncle takes precedence over his grandfather's paternal uncle, due to closeness of degree. And within each of these categories, the one with two ties takes precedence over the one with one tie when equal in degree. So the deceased's full paternal uncle is more entitled than his consanguine paternal uncle. Similarly in the case of father's paternal uncle and grandfather's paternal uncle. And likewise the ruling in the branches of these categories: closeness of degree is considered first, then strength of kinship. So the deceased's cousin (son of paternal uncle) takes precedence over the son of his cousin, and the deceased's full cousin takes precedence over his consanguine cousin. (Tatmimah, Fath). Then the freeer (mu'tiq): i.e., then the most entitled in inheritance after these is the freeer, i.e., the one who emancipated; because of his saying: 'Wal is a relationship like the relationship of lineage.' And he is the last of the 'asabat; because of his saying to the one who emancipated a slave: 'If he dies leaving no heir, you are his 'asaba.' (Ayni, Tatmimah). Then his 'asaba: i.e., the 'asaba of the patron (mawla); its meaning: if the freeer does not have a relative 'asaba in the order we mentioned, then his 'asaba is the patron he emancipated. If he does not have a patron, then his 'asaba is the 'asaba of the patron, i.e., the patron's 'asaba according to the order we mentioned, such that the patron's offspring takes precedence even if lower, then his ascendants, then his father's offspring, then his grandfather's offspring, with priority given to strength of kinship when equal in degree, and to higher degree when different. And the 'asaba of the 'asaba of the patron do not inherit. For example, if a woman emancipated a slave, and she dies leaving a son and a husband, then the freed slave (mu'taq) dies...
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq dealing with the second category of heirs: the 'asabat (residuary heirs). The author begins by defining 'asaba as one who takes the whole estate when alone, and the remainder when with a fixed-share heir. The commentary then clarifies that this definition does not apply to the daughter who takes the whole by both fard and radd; she is excluded because she does not take by a single avenue. The 'asaba are of two types: nasabiyyah (by lineage) and sababiyyah (by cause). The lineage type has three subdivisions: (1) 'asaba bi-nafsihi – every male whose relation to the deceased does not pass through a female (e.g., son, father, brother); (2) 'asaba bi-ghayrihi – females whose prescribed share is half or two-thirds who become 'asaba with their brothers (e.g., full sister with her full brother); (3) 'asaba ma'a ghayrihi – females who become 'asaba with another female (e.g., daughters with full sisters). The causal type includes the slave's emancipator (mu'tiq) and the client of alliance (mawla al-muwalah).

Next, the commentary explains the order of priority among the 'asabat. The most entitled is the son, then his son (descending), based on the Quranic verses (4:11) which give the son a determined share of the estate when there are other heirs, implying his precedence over others. After the son's line, the father takes precedence, then grandfather (ascending). Then come brothers: full brother precedes consanguine brother; then their sons, then paternal uncles (full then consanguine), then their sons, then the emancipator, then the emancipator's 'asaba in the same order. The rule is: among those of equal degree, the one with a stronger blood tie (both parents) takes precedence over one with only paternal tie. When degrees differ, the closer degree takes precedence.

The passage also explains the distinction between children of the mother (bani al-akhyaf) who are excluded by the presence of a child, and children of the father and mother (bani al-a'yan) and of the father only (bani al-'alat) who are not excluded by a daughter; rather, they become 'asaba with her. This is because the condition of kalalah applies to the uterine siblings' entire inheritance, but only to the fixed-share portion of the agnatic siblings.

The commentary ends with a discussion of the 'asaba of the patron (mu'tiq) and clarifies that the 'asaba of the 'asaba of the patron do not inherit.

Key Terms
عصبة ('asaba): A residuary heir who takes the whole estate when alone, and the remainder after fixed-share heirs when present.
كلالة (kalalah): The state of having no descendant or ascendant heir (no child or father).
بني الأعيان (bani al-a'yan): Siblings from the same parents (full siblings).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the three subtypes of lineage 'asaba in the Hanafi school?
A) 'Asaba bi-nafsihi, 'asaba bi-ghayrihi, 'asaba ma'a ghayrihi
B) 'Asaba qarib, 'asaba ba'id, 'asaba dhawi al-arham
C) 'Asaba nasabiyyah, 'asaba sababiyyah, 'asaba haqiqiyyah
D) 'Asaba fard, 'asaba radd, 'asaba ta'sib

Key Takeaway
The 'asaba is the residuary heir: one who takes the whole when alone and the remainder after fixed shares; the Hanafi school classifies 'asaba into three lineage subtypes and two causal types.

Faraid — Inheritance

Hierarchy of 'Asabat and Quranic Proof
Hierarchical order of 'asabat and its Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of 'asabat from the most entitled to the least, explain the Quranic proof for the son's precedence, and apply the rules of degree and kinship strength to determine priority.

Core Idea
The son (and his male line) is the most entitled 'asaba, followed by the father, then brothers, then uncles, then the emancipator and his 'asaba – based on closeness to the deceased.

Having defined and classified the 'asaba, the commentator now establishes the order of priority among them. The hierarchy is derived from the Quran and the principle that closer relatives take precedence. This lesson provides the complete list and the evidence for the son's top position.

Guided Path
1
Learn the Hierarchical Order
Memorize the order: son → son's son (descending) → father → grandfather (ascending) → full brother → consanguine brother → son of full brother → son of consanguine brother → full paternal uncle → consanguine paternal uncle → their sons → the emancipator (mu'tiq) → his 'asaba.
The order is from the closest in degree to the farthest, and within the same degree, the stronger blood tie (both parents) precedes the weaker (one parent).
2
Understand the Rule of Degree and Kinship Strength
When two 'asaba are of the same degree (e.g., full brother and consanguine brother), the one with two ties (full) takes precedence. When degrees differ (e.g., son vs. father), the closer degree (son) takes precedence regardless of kinship strength.
This rule applies throughout the hierarchy: first degree, then strength.
3
Analyze the Quranic Proof for the Son's Precedence
The text quotes Surah al-Nisa 4:11, which gives the son a determined share (male double the female) and assigns a fixed share to the father only when a child exists. This implies that the son is more entitled to the residue than the father, establishing the son as the foremost 'asaba.
The verse is a divine text (qati' al-thubut) but its interpretation of the son's precedence is zanni al-dalala, subject to scholarly understanding.
4
Note the Position of the Emancipator (Mu'tiq)
After all blood 'asaba, the emancipator (mu'tiq) becomes the 'asaba if no relative 'asaba exists. His 'asaba (his own heirs) inherit if he is deceased, following the same order of degree and strength.
This is based on the hadith: 'al-wala' luhmah ka-luhmat al-nasab' and the instruction to the one who frees a slave.

ثم الأب، ثم أب الأب وإن علا، ثم الأخ لأب وأم، ثم الأخ لأب، ثم ابن الأخ لأب وأم ثم ابن الأخ لأب، ثم الأعمام، ثم أعمام الأب، ثم أعمام الجد على أي ثم الأحق بالعصوبة الترتيب، ثم المعتق، ثم عصبته على الترتيب، أي مولى العتاقة أي المعتق المذكور للولد الذكر سهما ،مقررا، فتعين الباقي له فدل أن الولد الذكر مقدم عليه بالعصوبة، وابن الابن وإن سفل كالابن على ما بيناه؛ لأنه يقوم مقامه فيقدم عليه أيضا تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٥٣/٩] ثم الأب: أي ثم أولاهم بالعصوبة أصول الميت وإن علوا، وأولاهم به الأب؛ لأن الله تعالى شرط الإرث للإخوة بالكلالة وهو الذي لا ولد له ولا والد على ما بينا، فعلم بذلك أنهم لا يرثون مع الأب ضرورة، وعليه إجماع الأمة، فإذا كان ذلك مع الإخوة وهم أقرب الناس إليه بعد فروعه وأصوله فما ظنك بمن هو أبعد منه كأعمامه وأعمام أبيه والجدات. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٥٣/٩] ثم الأخ لأب إلخ حاصله: أنه يقدم ذو القرابتين على ذي قرابة واحدة كالأخ لأب وأم يقدم على الأخ لأب، وكالأخت لأب وأم إذا صارت عصبة مع البنت أولى من الأخ لأب، هذا عند الاستواء في الدرجة، وعند التفاوت يقدم الأعلى، وإذا لم تكن عصبة بل كانت ذات فرض فلها فرضها والباقي للأخ لأب، وإنما قدموا على الأعمام؛ لأن الله تعالى جعل الإرث في الكلالة للإخوة عند عدم الولد والوالد، فعلم بذلك أنهم يقدمون على الأعمام؛ لأنهم جزء الجد. (فتح، تكملة) ثم الأعمام: أي أولاهم بالميراث بعد الإخوة أعمام الميت؛ لأنهم بعد ذلك جزء الجد فكانوا أقرب، وقد قال : ألحقوا الفرائض بأهلها فما أبقت فلأولى .رجل. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٥٤/٩] ويعتبر بين هؤلاء الأصناف الأعمام قرب الدرجة أولا وقوة القرابة ثانيا، فعم الميت يقدم على عم أبيه المقدم على عم جده، وذلك لقرب الدرجة، وفي كل واحد من هذه الأصناف يقدم ذو القرابتين على ذي قرابة واحدة مع التساوي في الدرجة، فعم الميت لأب وأم أولى من عمه ،لأب، وكذا الحال في عم وعم جده، وهكذا الحكم في فروع هذه الأصناف فيعتبر أولا قرب الدرجة وثانيا قوة القرابة، فابن عم ا الميت يقدم على ابن ابن عمه، وابن عم الميت لأب وأم مقدم على ابن عمه لأب. (تكملة، فتح ثم المعتق: بكسر التاء أي ثم الأحق بالميراث بعد هؤلاء المعتق أي الذي أعتق؛ لقوله عليه: "الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب"، وهو آخر العصبات؛ لقوله علي : لمن أعتق عبدا: "إن مات ولم يدع وارثا كنت عصبة له". (عيني، تكملة)
